The State of the Deceased During Grave Questioning
The author describes the return of faculties and the varying conditions of the questioned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of what happens to the deceased during the grave questioning, including the restoration of faculties and the varying conditions described in Islamic scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
The grave questioning varies in form and duration based on the person's state.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid discusses the events after burial. It explains how the deceased is restored to a state of awareness for the questioning and how the experience differs for different individuals. The author draws on hadith and scholarly reports to describe these variations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it, then read the full translation. Let the author's description of the grave questioning come through clearly.
2
Identify the restored faculties
Notice that the author says the senses, intellect, and knowledge are restored to the extent necessary for understanding and responding. This is the baseline condition for the questioning.
This restoration is like a partial waking from sleep.
3
Note the variations in questioning
The text mentions variations: some are questioned by both angels (severity), some by one (leniency). There is also a marginal note about the angels' positions. Then different reports on duration are given: once, three times, seven days for the believer, forty mornings for the disbeliever.
These variations show divine wisdom and justice.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: why might questioning vary? The author indicates severity or leniency. This teaches that Allah treats people according to their state and deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتوسط النوم بينهما، ويُرَدُّ إليه من الحواس والعقل والعلم ما يتوقف عليه فهم الخطاب، ويتأتى معه رد الجواب حتى يُسأل وأحوال المسؤولين مختلفة، فمنهم من يسأله الملكان جميعاً تشديداً عليه، ومنهم من يسأله أحدهما تخفيفاً عليه، ووجد بطرة (1) المؤلف : أن أحدهما يكون تحت رجليه والآخر عند رأسه، ويُسأل مرة واحدة، وفي حديث أسماء أنه يُسأل ثلاثاً، وعن الجلال أن المؤمن يُسأل سبعة أيام، والكافر أربعين صباحاً
Like the state of sleep between them, and there is restored to him from the senses, intellect, and knowledge that which is necessary for understanding the address and being able to respond until he is questioned. And the conditions of those questioned vary: some are questioned by both angels together as a severity upon him, and some are questioned by one of them as a leniency upon him. And it was found in the margin of the author: that one of them is under his feet and the other at his head. And he is questioned once, and in the hadith of Asma' that he is questioned three times, and from al-Jalal that the believer is questioned for seven days and the disbeliever for forty mornings.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage describes the state of the deceased during the grave questioning. It begins by comparing the state to sleep, with the return of faculties necessary for comprehension and response. The author then explains variations: some are questioned by both angels as a severity, some by one as a leniency. A marginal note adds the positions of the angels. Finally, different reports about the frequency and duration of questioning are mentioned: once, three times (hadith of Asma'), and for believers seven days, disbelievers forty mornings.

Key Terms
الحواس
العقل
العلم
الملكين
السؤال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the questioning happens only once for everyone.
Correction: The text shows variation in frequency and duration based on the person's state and reports, so it is not uniform.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is restored to the deceased for the questioning?
A) Only the soul
B) Senses, intellect, and knowledge
C) Only the body
D) Memory alone

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is a real event that involves restored faculties and varies in its particulars based on divine wisdom and the person's state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to be questioned in the grave tonight, would the faculties restored to you be enough to give a correct answer? What are you doing now to ensure that?
?
The passage notes that some are questioned by both angels as severity. Do you think you deserve severity or leniency based on your current deeds? What change can you make today?
?
The believer is questioned for seven days, the disbeliever for forty mornings. Which category do you belong to, and what does that reveal about your preparation for the grave?

The Language of the Grave Questioning is Arabic
The author affirms that the questioning is in Arabic, refuting the view that it is in Syriac.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct doctrine that the grave questioning occurs in each person's language, and the evidence refuting the claim that it is in Syriac.

Core Idea
Each person is questioned in their own tongue, not a single foreign language.

This brief passage settles a debate about the language of the grave questioning. Some held that the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) question the deceased in Syriac, but the correct view, which the author presents, is that the questioning is in the language of the person being questioned. The author reinforces this with a poetic anecdote that expresses surprise at the Syriac claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation once to get the overall meaning. Pay attention to the phrase 'كل أحدٍ بلسانه' (everyone in his tongue).
The poetry lines have some OCR uncertainties, but the main idea is clear.
2
Identify the correct and refuted views
The passage states the correct view ('على الصحيح') and then mentions the opposing view ('خلافاً لمن قال بالسرياني'). Note how the author dismisses the Syriac claim.
3
Understand the evidence from poetry
The two lines of rajaz poetry express amazement at the Syriac claim. The poet says he only heard this from one teacher and never from anyone else, implying its weakness.
The word 'القَيْر' is likely 'القبر' (the grave). 'أنتى' might be 'أتى' (came).
4
Reflect on the wisdom behind diversity of languages
Consider why it makes sense that Allah would question each person in their own language: it is a form of justice and clarity, ensuring no one is at a disadvantage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسألان كل أحدٍ بلسانه على الصحيح، خلافاً لمن قال بالسرياني . ولذلك قال بعضهم : [من الرجز] ومِنْ عَجِيبِ ما تَرَى العَينانِ أَنَّ سُؤالَ القَيْر بِالسُّرْيانِي أنتى بِهَذا شَيْخُنا اليُلْقِيني ولَمْ أَرَهُ لِغَيْرِهِ بِعَيْنِي
And they both question everyone in his tongue according to the correct view, contrary to those who said in Syriac. And therefore some said: [in rajaz]: Among the wondrous things that the two eyes see is that the questioning of the grave is in Syriac. Our teacher brought this to me who met me, and I have not seen it for anyone else with my own eyes.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the grave questioning is conducted in Syriac. The author states the correct view that each person is questioned in his own language. He then quotes two lines of rajaz poetry that express amazement at the Syriac claim, noting that the poet only heard it from one teacher and never from anyone else.

Key Terms
اللسان
السرياني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The grave questioning is conducted in Syriac for all people.
Correction: The correct belief is that each person is questioned in their own language.

Checkpoint

A) Arabic only
B) Syriac
C) In the language of the deceased
D) Hebrew

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is conducted in the language of the deceased, not in Syriac or any single language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The poet found the Syriac view 'wondrous' because it came from only one teacher. Are there beliefs about the afterlife that you hold solely because you heard them from a single source without verifying against the Quran and Sunnah? What will you do today to ensure your understanding of the unseen is built on solid evidence?
?
You will be questioned in your own tongue—the language of your heart and deeds, not just your speech. What does your life's 'language' currently say about your faith? If your actions were translated into words right now, would they confess belief or denial? What one change can you make today so that your deeds speak clearly of Iman?

The Deceased is Questioned Even if the Body is Destroyed
The author argues that the questioning applies even if the body is dismembered or eaten by beasts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the grave questioning applies even if the body is completely destroyed, because Allah's power is sufficient to restore life to scattered remains.

Core Idea
Divine omnipotence makes the grave questioning inevitable, regardless of the body's condition.

A common objection to the doctrine of grave questioning is that the body may be completely destroyed, making it impossible. The author addresses this by grounding the possibility in Allah's absolute power. This passage clarifies that no physical destruction can prevent the spiritual realities of the barzakh.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then its literal translation. Notice the author's concise phrasing and logical connectors like 'إذ لا يبعد' and 'لأن'.
The Arabic uses a conditional tone: 'even if' (ولو).
2
Identify the key argument
Find the author's central claim and the evidence supporting it. The claim is that questioning occurs despite bodily destruction; the evidence is Allah's power to restore life.
Look for the phrase 'قدرة الله صالحة لذلك'.
3
Reflect on divine omnipotence
Consider how this passage highlights Allah's unlimited power. Even scattered limbs can be reconstituted. This reinforces the Islamic principle that nothing is beyond Allah's ability.
This ties into broader discussions of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُسأل الميتُ ولو مزقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السباع في أجوافها، إذ لا يبعد أن الله يعيد له الروح في أعضائه، ولو كانت متفرقةٌ ؛ لأن قدرة الله صالحة لذلك؛ ويحتمل أن يعيده كما كان،
And the deceased is questioned even if his limbs are torn apart or beasts have eaten him in their bellies, for it is not remote that Allah restores the soul to his limbs, even if they were scattered; because Allah's power is sufficient for that; and it is possible that He restores him as he was.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a theological proof that the grave questioning is not hindered by the destruction of the body. The author argues that since Allah is all-powerful, He can reconstitute the body and restore life to it, no matter how scattered or consumed. The phrase 'لا يبعد' (it is not remote) and 'قدرة الله صالحة' (Allah's power is sufficient) emphasize the ease of this for divine omnipotence. The author also suggests the possibility of restoration to the original state.

Key Terms
القدرة
إعادة الروح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Bodily destruction prevents the grave questioning.
Correction: Allah's power can restore life to scattered limbs, so questioning can occur.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the author's argument that the questioning occurs even if the body is destroyed?
A) The soul is independent of the body
B) Allah's power can restore life to scattered limbs
C) The questioning is only of the soul
D) The body is never completely destroyed

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is not hindered by physical destruction because Allah's power can restore life to any state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every single cell of your body will be reassembled and you will be asked about your deeds, how would that change the way you live tomorrow?
?
Is there an area of your life where you act as if your actions will not be questioned—perhaps because you think 'it won't matter' or 'no one will know'? What does this lesson reveal about that assumption?
?
The ease with which Allah can restore life from beasts' bellies—does that make you more aware of His constant presence, or more afraid of the accountability that follows? What will you do with that awareness today?

Simultaneous Questioning and the Multiplication of Angels
Three scholarly opinions on simultaneous questioning of the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars explain the possibility of simultaneous questioning of deceased people in different places through magnification or multiplication of angels.

Core Idea
Angels can be multiplied or magnified to question all the deceased.

When many people die at the same time in different places, how can the two angels Munkar and Nakir question them all? Scholars offer three reasonable explanations grounded in Allah's power. This passage presents the opinions of al-Qurtubi, al-Suyuti, and al-Halimi, each offering a different perspective on how the questioning occurs simultaneously.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation to understand the core discussion about simultaneous questioning.
2
Identify the three scholarly opinions
The passage presents three opinions: al-Qurtubi's magnification view, al-Suyuti's multiplication suggestion, and al-Halimi's preference for a large group of angels. Notice how each scholar addresses the challenge.
Pay attention to the names and their proposals.
3
Compare the opinions
Compare al-Qurtubi's idea of magnification with al-Suyuti and al-Halimi's idea of multiplication. Ask yourself which explanation seems more plausible and why.
All are valid because Allah is all-powerful.
4
Note the author's conclusion
The author ends with 'والله أعلم' (Allah knows best), acknowledging that the ultimate knowledge belongs to Allah. This teaches humility in theological discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا مات جماعةٌ في وقتٍ واحدٍ بأقاليم مختلفة . . قال القرطبي : جاز أن تعظم جثتهما، ويخاطبان الخلق الكثير مُخاطبةٌ واحدةٌ . وقال الحافظ السيوطي: ويحتمل تعدّد الملائكة المعدة لذلك؛ ثم رأيت الحليمي ذهب إليه فقال في «منهاجه»: والذي يشبه أن يكون ملائكة السؤال جماعة كثيرة، ويُسمَّى بعضهم منكراً، وبعضهم نكيراً، فيبعث إلى كل ميت اثنان منهم، والله أعلم
And if a group dies at one time in different regions... al-Qurtubi said: It is permissible that their two bodies are magnified and they address the many creation with a single address. And al-Hafiz al-Suyuti said: It is possible that the angels prepared for that are multiplied; then I saw al-Halimi inclined to that and said in his 'Minhaj': The closest is that the angels of questioning are a large group, some of them are called Munkar and some Nakir, and two of them are sent to every deceased person, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection of how simultaneous deaths in different places are handled. Three scholarly opinions are presented: 1) Al-Qurtubi says the two angels' bodies are magnified so they can speak to all at once. 2) Al-Suyuti suggests the angels are multiplied. 3) Al-Halimi prefers the view of a large group of angels, with two (Munkar and Nakir) sent to each deceased. The author ends with 'والله أعلم', acknowledging that the ultimate knowledge belongs to Allah.

Key Terms
ملائكة السؤال
منكر
نكير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the same two angels (Munkar and Nakir) question everyone simultaneously, which seems impossible for different locations.
Correction: Scholars explain that either the angels are magnified to speak to all at once, or there are multiple angels (or many pairs) sent to each deceased, showing Allah's power to enable questioning.

Checkpoint
According to al-Halimi, how many angels are sent to each deceased?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Allah's power enables either the magnification of the two angels or the multiplication of angels to question all deceased simultaneously.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die today, do you know with certainty what your answer would be when Munkar and Nakir ask you about your Lord, your Prophet, and your religion? What are you doing right now to ensure that answer is correct?
?
The angels are already prepared to question you. Is your life a preparation for that moment, or are you ignoring it? What one concrete change will you make today to live with the grave in mind?
?
You have read that Allah can magnify or multiply angels at will. How does this reminder of His absolute power change the way you view the difficulties and limitations in your own life? Will you trust Him more starting today?

Variations in the Grave Questioning According to Hadiths
The author reports different narrations about the content of the grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different hadith narrations about what is asked in the grave questioning and the wisdom behind the angels' manner of questioning.

Core Idea
The grave questioning tests sincerity, and its content varies by hadith.

The author, citing al-Qurtubi, explains that the hadiths differ on what exactly is asked in the grave. Some mention a few questions, others many. This shows that the questioning is tailored, but its purpose remains the same: to distinguish true believers from doubters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the different opinions and the explanation for the angels' manner.
Pay attention to the names: Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah.
2
Identify the different opinions cited
List the two opinions mentioned: one from Ibn Abbas (shahadatayn) and one from Ikrimah (faith in Muhammad and tawhid). Also note the common wording 'What do you say about this man?'
3
Reflect on the wisdom mentioned
Consider why the angels ask without glorification. The passage says it is to distinguish the truthful from the doubter. How does this test sincerity?
Think about the outcome for the truthful (answer correctly) and the doubter (says 'I do not know' and suffers).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفت الأحاديث كما قاله القرطبي في كيفية السؤال والجواب : فمنهم من يسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته . ومنهم من يُسأل عن كلّها، قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : (يسألون عن الشهادتين)، وقال عكرمة : (يسألون عن الإيمان بمحمد ، وأمر التوحيد). وقد ورد أنهما يقولان : ما تقول في هذا الرجل؟ وإنما يقولان ذلك من غير تعظيم وتفخيم ليتميّز الصادق في الإيمان من المرتاب، فيجيب الأول، ويقول الثاني : لا أدري فيشقى شقاء الأبد.
And the hadiths differed, as al-Qurtubi said, concerning the manner of the question and answer. Among them are those who are asked about some of their beliefs, and among them are those who are asked about all of them. Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: 'They are asked about the two testimonies.' And Ikrimah said: 'They are asked about faith in Muhammad and the matter of tawhid.' And it has been reported that they say: 'What do you say about this man?' And they only say that without glorification and exaltation to distinguish the truthful in faith from the doubter. So the first answers, and the second says, 'I do not know,' and thus he is miserable with eternal misery.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage discusses the variations in the content of the grave questioning. The author notes that hadiths differ: some mention selective queries, some comprehensive. He cites Ibn Abbas saying they are asked about the two testimonies, and Ikrimah saying about faith in Muhammad and tawhid. Then he mentions the common wording 'What do you say about this man?' and explains the wisdom behind the lack of awe in the angels' manner: to test sincerity. The result is clear: the believer answers correctly, the doubter fails and suffers eternal misery.

Key Terms

الإيمان بمحمد
التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the questioning is exactly the same for everyone.
Correction: The hadiths show variation in scope: some are asked about a few beliefs, others about all.

Checkpoint

A) To frighten the deceased
B) To distinguish the truthful from the doubter
C) Because they are not real angels
D) To speed up the questioning

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning varies in scope according to different hadiths, but its purpose is always to distinguish the truthful believer from the doubter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The doubter says 'I do not know' and suffers eternal misery. Is there any area of your faith where you are still a 'doubter'—not because you lack knowledge, but because you have not truly committed? What will you do today to turn that doubt into certainty?
?
The angels ask without glorification to distinguish the truthful from the doubter. If you were in the grave right now, what would your answer be based on your current state of faith? Are you living in a way that you would answer with confidence?
?
The questioning varies in scope, but the core is the shahada and tawhid. Is your daily life a reflection of sincere shahada, or have you allowed other loyalties to compete with your devotion to Allah? What is one concrete change you can make tonight to strengthen your tawhid?

The Dead Are Questioned Even If Body Destroyed
Discusses the possibility of questioning in the grave despite bodily destruction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic scholars argue that the grave questioning is possible even if the body is completely destroyed, based on Allah's unlimited power.

Core Idea
Divine power makes the grave questioning possible regardless of the body's state.

This passage addresses a common doubt: how can the dead be questioned in the grave if their body has perished? The author presents the argument that Allah's power is sufficient to restore the soul to scattered limbs. He also cites scholars like Qurtubi, Suyuti, and Halimi who offer additional explanations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the poetic opening and the scholarly names.
The poetry may be unclear due to OCR.
2
Identify the main argument
Find the sentence that states the dead are questioned even if their body is destroyed, and the reason given (divine power).
3
Examine the scholarly opinions
List what Qurtubi, Suyuti, and Halimi each added to the argument.
Notice how each scholar addresses a different aspect (simultaneous deaths, number of angels).
4
Reflect on the misconception
Think about the doubt that the questioning is impossible if the body perishes. How does this passage answer that?
The core is Allah's power; the opinions provide additional support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولذلك قال بعضهم : [من الرجز] ومِنْ عَجِيبِ ما تَرَى العَينانِ أَنَّ سُؤالَ القَيْر بِالسُّرْيانِي أنتى بِهَذا شَيْخُنا اليُلْقِيني ولَمْ أَرَهُ لِغَيْرِهِ بِعَيْنِي ويُسأل الميتُ ولو مزقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السباع في أجوافها، إذ لا يبعد أن الله يعيد له الروح في أعضائه، ولو كانت متفرقةٌ ؛ لأن قدرة الله صالحة لذلك؛ ويحتمل أن يعيده كما كان، وإذا مات جماعةٌ في وقتٍ واحدٍ بأقاليم مختلفة . . قال القرطبي : جاز أن تعظم جثتهما، ويخاطبان الخلق الكثير مُخاطبةٌ واحدةٌ . وقال الحافظ السيوطي: ويحتمل تعدّد الملائكة المعدة لذلك؛ ثم رأيت الحليمي ذهب إليه فقال في «منهاجه»: والذي يشبه أن يكون ملائكة السؤال جماعة كثيرة، ويُسمَّى بعضهم منكراً، وبعضهم نكيراً، فيبعث إلى كل ميت اثنان منهم، والله أعلم
And therefore some of them said: [in rajaz meter] 'From the wondrous things that the two eyes see is that the question of the grave [is] in Syriac...' [rest of line unclear] 'You came with this, our shaykh, al-Yulqini, and I have not seen it for anyone else with my eye.' And the dead person is questioned even if his limbs are torn apart or beasts eat him in their stomachs, for it is not unlikely that Allah returns the soul to his limbs, even if they are scattered, because the power of Allah is sufficient for that; and it is possible that He returns him as he was. And if a group dies at one time in different regions... al-Qurtubi said: It is permissible that their two bodies are magnified and they address the many people with a single address. And al-Hafiz al-Suyuti said: And it is possible that the angels prepared for that are numerous; then I saw al-Halimi tending to that, and he said in his 'Minhaj': The likeliest is that the angels of questioning are a large group, some are called Munkar and some Nakir, and two of them are sent to every deceased person. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage argues for the possibility of the grave questioning (sual al-qabr) even when the body is completely destroyed. The author begins by citing a poetic testimony: 'From the wondrous things that the two eyes see is that the question of the grave...' (the lines are somewhat obscure in the OCR). The core argument follows: the deceased is questioned even if his body is torn apart or eaten by beasts, because Allah can restore the soul to the scattered limbs. Divine power (qudra) suffices for this. al-Qurtubi is then quoted to support the idea that if many people die at once in different regions, their bodies could be magnified (ta'zim) and they could address many people simultaneously. al-Suyuti suggests the number of angels is multiplied for this purpose. al-Halimi explicitly states that the angels of questioning are many, with some called Munkar and some Nakir, and two are sent to each deceased. The passage concludes with 'Allah knows best', indicating this is a matter of interpretation within the bounds of divine power.

Key Terms
سؤال القبر
قدرة الله
منكر ونكير
القرطبي
السيوطي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe questioning in the grave is impossible if the body is completely destroyed or scattered.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah's absolute power makes it possible; He can restore the soul to the limbs and bring the dead back to a state capable of being questioned.

Checkpoint

B) Because Allah can restore the soul to the scattered limbs
C) Because the angels collect all body parts
D) Because the questioning is only spiritual

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is possible regardless of bodily destruction because Allah's power is unlimited and can restore life to any state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
The power of Allah makes the grave questioning certain for every person. Does that certainty frighten you enough to repent from sins you keep hidden? What sin are you still holding onto that you need to abandon right now?

The Variety of Questions in the Grave
Differing hadiths on the questions in the grave and the wisdom behind the angels' approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differences in hadith reports about the questioning in the grave and the rationale behind the angels' unvenerating manner.

Core Idea
The angels test faith by asking without awe.

The hadiths vary in how they describe the questions posed to the deceased in the grave. Some mention only certain beliefs, others cover all. This passage, citing al-Qurtubi and two Companions, highlights that the angels ask in a plain manner to distinguish true believers from doubters. Understanding this variation helps us appreciate the wisdom in the prophetic teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the different opinions cited.
2
Identify the two views
Ibn 'Abbas says they are asked about the two testimonies; 'Ikrimah says about faith in Muhammad and tawhid. Compare these.
Both views are complementary, not contradictory.
3
Understand the angels' manner
The angels ask 'What do you say about this man?' without veneration. Understand why: to test sincerity.
4
Reflect on the outcome
The true believer answers correctly; the doubter says 'I do not know' and suffers eternal misery. See the gravity of the test.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفت الأحاديث كما قاله القرطبي في كيفية السؤال والجواب : فمنهم من يسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته . ومنهم من يُسأل عن كلّها، قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : (يسألون عن الشهادتين)، وقال عكرمة : (يسألون عن الإيمان بمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأمر التوحيد). وقد ورد أنهما يقولان : ما تقول في هذا الرجل؟ وإنما يقولان ذلك من غير تعظيم وتفخيم ليتميّز الصادق في الإيمان من المرتاب، فيجيب الأول، ويقول الثاني : لا أدري فيشقى شقاء الأبد.
And the hadiths differed, as al-Qurtubi said, concerning the manner of the questioning and the answer: some of them are asked about some of their beliefs, and some are asked about all of them. Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: 'They are asked about the two testimonies.' And 'Ikrimah said: 'They are asked about faith in Muhammad, peace be upon him, and the matter of monotheism.' And it has been reported that the two [angels] say: 'What do you say about this man?' And they only say that without veneration and magnification to distinguish the truthful in faith from the doubter. So the first answers, and the second says: 'I do not know,' and thus he becomes wretched with eternal wretchedness.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage addresses the variety of hadith reports regarding the specific questions posed in the grave. al-Qurtubi's observation is used: some reports indicate the deceased is asked about some of his beliefs, while others mention all of them. Two sahaba are cited: Ibn 'Abbas says they are asked about the two shahadas (testimonies of faith), and 'Ikrimah says they are asked about faith in Muhammad and the matter of tawhid (monotheism). The passage then clarifies a key point: the angels ask 'What do you say about this man?' (referring to the Prophet Muhammad) without veneration or magnification. This is intentional, so that the truly faithful person is distinguished from the doubter (murtab). The faithful one answers correctly, while the doubter says 'I do not know' and thus suffers everlasting misery (shaqa' al-abad). The passage thus highlights both the variety of hadith and the underlying wisdom of the questioning style.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that the angels ask without veneration or magnification to test sincerity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The hadiths show variation in questioning, but the test is the same: sincerity. In your daily life, are you trying to appear faithful or truly be faithful? How can you cultivate sincerity in your heart starting now?

The Questioning Is Specific to This Ummah and Its Exceptions
States that the grave questioning is particular to this ummah and lists those exempted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of the grave questioning, the different interpretations of its trial, and the specific categories of people exempted from it.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is not universal—prophets and certain righteous are exempt.

This lesson explores the nature of the grave questioning for the Muslim community. The passage defines the trial of the grave and lists those who are spared from it, including prophets, the truthful, martyrs, and those with consistent acts of worship. Understanding these exceptions gives comfort and insight into Allah's mercy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scope of questioning
The passage states that the questioning is specific to this ummah, with a minority view that it applies to all nations. Notice how the author begins with a general rule.
2
Define 'fitnat al-qabr'

3
Identify the exempted categories

The author emphasizes that the Prophet should not be a subject of disagreement.
4

This ties back to the core idea of the lesson.

وهذا السؤال خاص بهذه الأمَّة ، وقيل : كل نبي مع أمنه كذلك؛ وهذا السؤال هو عين فتنة القبر ، وقيل : هي التلجلج في الجواب وقيل : هي ما ورد من حضور إبليس في زاوية من زوايا القبر مُشيراً إلى نفسه بأن (أنا) ، عند قول الملك للميت: مَنْ ربُّك؟ مُستدعياً منه جوابه بهذا ربي)، ولم يثبت حضورُ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا رؤية الميت له عند السؤال . ويُستثنى من عموم قول الناظم: (سؤالنا) مَنْ وردَ الأثر بعدم سؤاله كالأنبياء، فالحقُ أنهم لا يسألون ، وقيل : يسألون عن جبريل والوحي الذي أُنزل عليهم، ولا ينبغي أن يكون سيدهم الأعظم محلَّ خلاف وكالصديقين والشهداء، والمرابطين والملازمين لقراءة تبارك (الملك) كل ليلة من حين بلوغ الخبر لهم، والمراد بالملازمة: الإتيان بها في غالب الأوقات، فلا يضرُّ الترك مرةً بعذر؛ سواء أقرأها عند النوم أو قبل ذلك، وهكذا سورة السجدة فيما ذكره بعضهم، وكذا من قرأ في مرض موته وقُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ [الإخلاص]، ومريض البطن، والميت بالطاعون أو
And this questioning is specific to this community, and it is said: every prophet with his community is likewise. And this questioning is the very trial of the grave, and it is said: it is the hesitation in the answer, and it is said: it is what has been reported about the presence of Iblis in a corner of the grave pointing to himself saying 'I am' at the time when the angel says to the deceased: 'Who is your Lord?' seeking from him the answer 'My Lord is this,' and the presence of the Prophet, peace be upon him, nor the deceased's seeing him at the time of questioning is not established. And from the generality of the statement of the author: 'our questioning' are excepted those for whom the tradition has come that they are not questioned, like the prophets, for the truth is that they are not questioned, and it is said: they are questioned about Jibril and the revelation sent down to them, and it is not fitting that their greatest master be a place of disagreement, and likewise the siddiqin (truthful ones) and the shuhada' (martyrs), and the murabitin (those guarding frontiers) and those who are constant in reciting Tabarak (Surah al-Mulk) every night from the time they receive the news (of its virtue). And the meaning of constancy is: performing it most of the time, so omitting it once due to an excuse does not harm, whether one recites it at bedtime or before that, and likewise Surah al-Sajdah as some have mentioned, and similarly the one who recites 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' [Surah al-Ikhlas] in the illness of his death, and the one with a stomach ailment, and the one who dies of plague or...
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage addresses the scope and exceptions of the grave questioning. It begins by stating that the questioning is specific to this ummah (the Muslim community), with some saying that each prophet with his community is also questioned. Then it defines 'fitnat al-qabr' (trial of the grave): some say it is the hesitation (taljulj) in answering, others say it is the presence of Iblis in the grave pointing to himself saying 'I am' when the angel asks 'Who is your Lord?', prompting the deceased to answer 'My Lord is this'. The author notes that neither the Prophet's presence nor the deceased's seeing him at the time of questioning is established. Next, exceptions are listed from the author's general statement 'our questioning': those for whom there is textual evidence that they are not questioned. These include: prophets (who, it is said, are not questioned; though some say they are questioned about Jibril and the revelation, but the author asserts it is not fitting for the Prophet to be subject to disagreement), the siddiqin (truthful ones), the shuhada' (martyrs), the murabitin (those guarding frontiers), and those who consistently recite Surah al-Mulk every night. The constancy (mulazama) is defined as performing it most of the time, so a single omission with an excuse is not harmful. Similarly, reciting Surah al-Sajdah, reciting Surah al-Ikhlas during the illness of death, those who die of stomach illness, and those who die of plague are also exempted. The passage ends abruptly mid-sentence, likely continuing with more exceptions.

The Questioning in the Grave: Definition and Specificity
Defines the questioning in the grave and explains its nature and specific scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the questioning in the grave (su'āl al-qabr) is, its specific nature for this ummah, and the interpretations of the trial of the grave.

Core Idea
The questioning itself is the trial of the grave.

The author begins by clarifying that the questioning in the grave is specifically for the ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and then equates this questioning with the trial of the grave. He presents differing interpretations of the trial and clarifies that the Prophet's presence during the questioning is not established from authentic sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the technical terms: سؤال القبر and فتنة القبر.
2
Identify the key claims
Look for: (1) the questioning is specific to this ummah, (2) it is the very trial, (3) two opinions on what the trial is, (4) negation of the Prophet's presence.
3
Understand the two interpretations
The trial is either hesitation in answering or the presence of Iblis pointing to himself. Reflect on how each interpretation fits the concept of a trial.
These are scholarly views; the author does not prefer one.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why it matters to know that the questioning is specific to this ummah and that the Prophet is not present. This shapes our understanding of the unseen events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا السؤال خاص بهذه الأمة (1) ، وقيل : كل نبي مع أمته كذلك؛ وهذا السؤال هو عين فتنة القبر ، وقيل : هي التلجلج في الجواب وقيل : هي ما ورد من حضور إبليس في زاوية من زوايا القبر مشيراً إلى نفسه بأن (أنا) ، عند قول الملك للميت: مَنْ ربُّك؟ مستدعياً منه جوابه بهذا ربي)، ولم يثبت حضورُ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا رؤية الميت له عند السؤال .
And this questioning is specific to this ummah (1), and it was said: every prophet with his ummah is like that; and this questioning is the very trial of the grave, and it was said: it is hesitation in answering, and it was said: it is what has been reported of the presence of Iblis in a corner of the corners of the grave, pointing to himself saying 'I' at the time when the angel says to the dead: 'Who is your Lord?' seeking from him the answer 'My Lord is this', and the presence of the Prophet ﷺ nor the dead person's seeing him at the questioning has not been established.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the questioning of the grave (su'āl al-qabr) and its nature. The author begins by stating that this questioning is specific to the ummah of Muhammad, though some say it applies to every prophet and his ummah. Then he equates the questioning itself with the trial of the grave (fitnat al-qabr) – it is that very trial. He gives two interpretations of the fitna: some say it is hesitation and confusion in answering the angels' questions; others say it is the appearance of Iblis (Satan) in the grave pointing to himself as if to say 'I am your lord,' prompting the dead to reject that and answer correctly. Finally, he clarifies that it is not established that the Prophet ﷺ is present or seen by the deceased during this questioning.

فتنة القبر
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: The author states that the questioning itself is the fitna, not a separate occurrence.

Key Takeaway
The questioning in the grave is the very trial, specific to this ummah, with interpretations involving hesitation or Iblis's presence, and the Prophet's presence is not established.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Iblis will be present in your grave, pointing to himself as if to say 'I am your lord.' How does the thought of encountering your sworn enemy in that moment make you feel about your current reliance on Allah? Identify one way you can strengthen your trust in Allah alone before that day.
?
The presence of the Prophet (saw) is not established at the questioning. This means no intercessor will be there to help you answer. Does this thought make you anxious or motivated? What will you do today to deepen your personal knowledge of Allah so that you can answer without needing anyone else?

Exceptions from Grave Questioning
Lists categories exempt from grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of people exempt from grave questioning according to authentic traditions.

Core Idea
Not everyone is questioned in the grave; many are exempt by divine mercy.

This passage discusses exceptions to the general rule that every deceased is questioned in the grave. The author lists several categories based on hadith evidence, showing Allah's mercy in sparing certain individuals from this trial.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule and exception
Recognize that the author is making exceptions from the general rule of grave questioning. The phrase 'ويستثنى من عموم' signals this.
2

3
Note the other categories and conditions
List the subsequent categories: siddiqin, shuhada', murabitin, those constant in reciting Surat al-Mulk, those reciting al-Ikhlas at death, those with stomach ailments, plague victims, and those dying on Friday. Note conditions like constancy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستثنى من عموم قول الناظم: (سؤالنا) مَنْ وردَ الأثر بعدم سؤاله كالأنبياء، فالحقُ أنهم لا يسألون ، وقيل : يسألون عن جبريل والوحي الذي أُنزل عليهم، ولا ينبغي أن يكون سيدهم الأعظم محلَّ خلاف وكالصديقين والشهداء، والمرابطين والملازمين لقراءة تبارك (الملك) (۲) كل ليلة من حين بلوغ الخبر لهم، والمراد بالملازمة: الإتيان بها في غالب الأوقات، فلا يضرُّ الترك مرةً بعذر؛ سواء أقرأها عند النوم أو قبل ذلك، وهكذا سورة السجدة فيما ذكره بعضهم، وكذا من قرأ في مرض موته ﴿قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ﴾ [الإخلاص: (٣) ، ومريض البطن (٤) ، والميت بالطاعون أو بغيره في زمنه صابراً محتسباً (۱) ، والميتُ ليلة الجمعة أو يومها (٢)، إلى غير ذلك

This passage enumerates exceptions from the general rule that the dead are questioned in the grave. Who Is Questioned in the Grave? Categories and Conditions
Enumerates who is questioned in the grave and the condition of accountability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of beings who are questioned in the grave according to the preponderant view, and the rationale behind the questioning.

Core Idea
Grave questioning applies to accountable beings, but not all equally.

This passage from the commentary clarifies which souls are subject to the questioning in the grave. It distinguishes between prophets, martyrs, children, angels, and jinn, showing that legal accountability is the key criterion. This lesson will help you map out these categories and grasp the wisdom behind this divine practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Notice how the author lists different groups and their rulings.
The passage ends mid-sentence; we have only the beginning of the wisdom.
2
Identify the four categories
Find and list the four groups mentioned: non-prophets and martyrs, children, angels, and jinn. Note what is said about each concerning grave questioning.
Non-prophets and martyrs are grouped together.
3
Understand the condition of accountability
Notice that children are excluded because they are not legally accountable (mukallaf). Jinn are included because they are accountable. This shows the principle: questioning is for the accountable.
Prophets and martyrs are also accountable but receive a lighter questioning.
4
Reflect on the wisdom
The passage begins to explain the wisdom: 'to manifest what...' Think about what might be manifested (e.g., faith, hypocrisy). The full wisdom is stated in later lessons.
The text cuts off, so we cannot know the complete wisdom here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والراجح أن غير الأنبياء وشهداء المعركة يُسألون سؤالاً خفيفاً، وبعضهم أخذ بظاهر ذلك، والظاهر كما جزم به الجلال السيوطي وغيره اختصاص السؤال بمن يكون مُكلَّفاً بخلاف الأطفال والظاهر أيضاً عدم سؤال الملائكة، وأما الجن فجزم الجلال بسؤالهم لتكليفهم، وعموم أدلة السؤال لهم) ، وحكمة السؤال : إظهار ما
And the preponderant view is that other than the prophets and martyrs of battle are questioned with a light questioning, and some have taken the apparent meaning of that, and the apparent view, as affirmed by al-Jalal al-Suyuti and others, is that the questioning is specific to one who is accountable (mukallaf), unlike children, and the apparent view is also that angels are not questioned. As for the jinn, al-Jalal affirmed their questioning due to their being accountable, and the generality of the evidences of questioning apply to them. And the wisdom of the questioning is to manifest what...
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage presents the preponderant ruling on who is questioned in the grave. It states that non-prophets and martyrs of battle are questioned, but lightly. Some scholars take this at face value. Then it reports the view of al-Jalal al-Suyuti that questioning is specific to those who are mukallaf (legally accountable), excluding children. Similarly, angels are not questioned. For jinn, al-Suyuti affirms they are questioned because they are accountable, and the general evidences of questioning include them. The passage ends by beginning to explain the wisdom behind the questioning: to manifest something (the text cuts off, but likely to manifest the believer's faith or the disbeliever's hypocrisy).

Key Terms
غير الأنبياء
شهداء المعركة
مكلف
أطفال
ملائكة
جن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All dead are questioned equally and severely.
Correction: The passage shows gradation: prophets and martyrs have a light questioning, children and angels are not questioned at all, and jinn are questioned like humans.

Checkpoint

A) They are not questioned
B) They are questioned like humans because they are accountable
C) Only Muslim jinn are questioned
D) They are questioned only lightly

Key Takeaway
Grave questioning is tied to accountability; only those who are mukallaf are questioned, with exceptions for prophets and martyrs who receive a light questioning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The prophets and martyrs receive only a light questioning. Does your longing for such a status drive you to actually live like them, or is it just a comfortable thought? What step will you take this week to embody their example?

Who Is Questioned in the Grave? The Ruling and Wisdom
The author states the dominant view on who is questioned and the wisdom behind it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the preponderant view on who is questioned in the grave and the wisdom behind the questioning.

Core Idea
Not everyone is questioned in the grave—prophets, martyrs, children, and angels are exempt.

This passage from the Tuhfat al-Murid clarifies the ruling on the questioning in the grave (sual al-qabr). It explains which categories of beings are questioned and which are exempt, along with the underlying wisdom. As you read, pay attention to the specific exemptions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic text and its literal English translation to get a sense of the content. Note the key terms like 'mukallaf' and 'jinn'.
2
Identify the exempted groups
The passage lists several groups that are not questioned or are questioned lightly. List them: prophets, martyrs of battle, children, and angels.
The 'light questioning' for non-prophets/non-martyrs is still a form of questioning.
3
Focus on the jinn
Notice that the jinn are specifically affirmed to be questioned because they are mukallaf (legally responsible). Reflect on why this is significant.
This shows that the questioning is tied to moral responsibility.
4
Understand the wisdom
The wisdom (hikma) is to manifest what was concealed in the world. Consider how this serves to honor believers and expose disbelievers.
The angels boast of believers and others are disgraced.
5
Apply to a misconception
The common misunderstanding is that everyone is questioned equally. From this passage, correct that by noting the exemptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والراجح أن غير الأنبياء وشهداء المعركة يُسألون سؤالاً خفيفاً، وبعضهم أخذ بظاهر ذلك، والظاهر كما جزم به الجلال السيوطي وغيره اختصاص السؤال بمن يكون مُكلَّفاً بخلاف الأطفال والظاهر أيضاً عدم سؤال الملائكة، وأما الجن فجزم الجلال بسؤالهم لتكليفهم، وعموم أدلة السؤال لهم، وحكمة السؤال: إظهار ما كتمه العباد في الدنيا من إيمان أو كفر أو طاعة أو عصيان؛ فالمؤمنون الطائعون يباهي بهم الملائكة، وغيرهم يفضحون عند الملائكة.
And the preponderant view is that other than the prophets and the martyrs of battle are questioned with a light questioning. And some took the apparent meaning of that, and the apparent view, as al-Jalal al-Suyuti and others affirmed, is the specification of the questioning to those who are obligated (mukallaf), unlike children. And the apparent view also is the absence of questioning for the angels. As for the jinn, al-Jalal affirmed their questioning due to their being obligated, and the generality of the evidences of questioning for them. And the wisdom of the questioning is the manifestation of what the servants concealed in the world of faith or disbelief or obedience or disobedience; so the believing obedient ones, the angels boast of them, and others are exposed before the angels.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage defines and expands upon the ruling on the questioning in the grave (sual al-qabr). The author first states the preponderant opinion: that non-prophets and non-martyrs are questioned lightly. Some scholars took the apparent meaning of hadiths that only prophets and martyrs are exempt. He then clarifies that according to al-Suyuti, questioning is specific to those who are mukallaf (legally responsible), excluding children. He also states that angels are not questioned. As for jinn, al-Suyuti affirmed they are questioned because they are also obligated. The wisdom of the questioning is to reveal what each person concealed in life—faith, disbelief, obedience, or disobedience—so that believers are honored and others disgraced.

مُكلَّف
الجن

Correction: The passage specifies that prophets, martyrs, children, and angels are not questioned (or questioned lightly). Thus, not everyone faces the same questioning.

The Universality and Reality of the Punishment of the Grave
Sanusi explains the universality and reality of the punishment of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave is obligatory for all whom God wills to punish, regardless of burial, and that both body and soul are punished together according to Ahl al-Haqq.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is real and universal, affecting both body and soul.

Sanusi clarifies a common misunderstanding about the punishment of the grave. Many think it only occurs if the body is buried intact. He explains that the punishment is not limited by burial status, and that both body and soul experience it. He also addresses a dissenting view and explains who receives the punishment and how it may be alleviated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's argument.
Pay attention to the examples given (crucified, drowned, etc.).
2
Identify the key claim
Notice that the punishment of the grave is not dependent on being buried; any dead person can be punished if God wills it.
The author refutes the idea that the state of the body prevents punishment.
3
Analyze the consensus and dissent
Identify the consensus (Ahl al-Haqq) that both body and soul are punished together, and the dissenting view of al-Tabari and Ibn Karram who hold only the body is punished.
Understand why the dissenting view is considered weak.
4
Understand the categories of people
List who receives punishment (disbelievers, hypocrites, sinful believers) and note the difference in duration: perpetual for the first two, may be lifted for some sinful believers.
Also note that those not questioned are not punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ثُمَّ عَذَابُ القَبْرِ) عطف على قوله: (سؤالنا)، لمشاركته له في حكمه الآتي وهو الوجوب، وإنما أضيف إلى القبر لأنه الغالب، وإلا فكل ميت أراد الله تعذيبه عُذْبَ، قبر أو لم يُقبر، ولو صلب أو غرق في بحر أو أكلته الدواب أو أحرق حتى صار رماداً وذُريَ في الريح، ولا يمنع من ذلك كون الميت تفرقت أجزاؤه، والمعذب البدن والروح جميعاً باتفاق أهل الحق، وخالف محمد بن جرير الطبري وعبد الله بن كرام، وطائفةٌ فقالوا: المعذب البدن فقط، ويخلق الله فيه إدراكاً بحيث يسمع ويعلم ويلتذ ويتألم. ويكون للكافر والمنافق وعصاة المؤمنين، ويدوم على الأولين، وينقطع عن بعض عصاة المؤمنين؛ وهو من خفت جرائمهم من العصاة فإنهم يعذبون بحسبها، وقد يُرفع عنهم بدعاء أو صدقةٍ أو غير ذلك، كما قاله ابن القيم وكل من كان لا يُسأل في قبره لا يُعذب فيه أيضاً.
His saying: 'Then the punishment of the grave' is coordinated with his saying: 'Our questioning', because of its participation with it in its upcoming ruling, which is obligation. And it was only attributed to the grave because it is the prevalent [case]; otherwise, every dead person whom God wills to punish is punished, whether buried or not buried, even if crucified or drowned in the sea or eaten by beasts or burned until he becomes ashes and scattered in the wind. And the fact that the dead person's parts have scattered does not prevent that. And the punished one is the body and the soul together, by agreement of the people of truth (ahl al-haqq). Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari, Abd Allah ibn Karram, and a group opposed and said: the punished one is only the body, and God creates in it perception such that it hears and knows and experiences pleasure and pain. And it is for the disbeliever, the hypocrite, and the disobedient believers. It continues for the first two, and ceases for some disobedient believers; and it is for those among the disobedient whose sins are light—they are punished according to them, and it may be lifted from them by supplication or charity or other than that, as Ibn al-Qayyim said. And everyone who is not questioned in his grave is not punished in it either.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage constitutes a definition and explanation of the punishment of the grave (adhab al-qabr). The author explains a line from the poem: 'Then the punishment of the grave' is syntactically coordinated with 'our questioning' because both share the ruling of obligation. The punishment is attributed to the grave only because that is the usual case; in reality, any dead person whom God wills to punish is punished regardless of burial—even if crucified, drowned, eaten, or cremated and scattered. This refutes the idea that the state of the body prevents punishment. The author then states the consensus of Ahl al-Haqq that both body and soul are punished together. He notes the dissenting view of al-Tabari and Ibn Karram, who held that only the body is punished with a specially created perception. The punishment applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and sinful believers. It is perpetual for the first two but may be lifted from the latter through supplication, charity, etc. Finally, he concludes that whoever is not questioned is also not punished.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
المعذب
البدن والروح
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The punishment of the grave only occurs if the body is buried intact.
Correction: The author explicitly states that punishment occurs regardless of burial, even if the body is scattered, cremated, or eaten.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consensus of Ahl al-Haqq regarding the punished entity in the grave?
A) Only the body is punished
B) Only the soul is punished
C) Both body and soul are punished together
D) Neither body nor soul is punished

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is a reality that applies to the body and soul together for those whom God wills, regardless of how the body is treated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight and God willed that you be punished, do you truly believe that not even the scattering of your ashes could prevent that punishment? How does that certainty affect the choices you make before you sleep?
?
The passage says that for sinful believers, punishment may be lifted through the supplication or charity of others. Name one deceased person you have not prayed for in the last month. Will you set a daily reminder to pray for them starting today?
?
You claim to believe in the punishment of the grave, yet do you live as if it is more real than your next meal? What concrete action will you take this week to reduce the sins that could make you among the 'disobedient believers' who suffer?

Examples of Punishment: Dragons and the Pressure of the Grave
The author cites a hadith about ninety-nine dragons and describes the pressure of the grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two specific examples of punishment of the grave from hadith and how they illustrate the reality of the grave's torment.

Core Idea
The grave's punishment includes tangible physical torment, except for prophets.

The previous lesson established the reality of the punishment of the grave. Now the author provides concrete examples that bring this doctrine to life. These examples, drawn from authentic hadith, show that the punishment is not abstract but involves physical sensations of biting, stinging, and crushing pressure.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith about dragons
Read the Arabic hadith carefully, noting the number (ninety-nine) and the description of the dragons. Notice the connection to the ninety-nine names of Allah.
The author explains the wisdom behind the number.
2
Understand the pressure of the grave
Read about the pressing (daghṭa) and its universality. Note the exception of prophets.
The exception is crucial for understanding divine justice.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why these specific examples are given and how they reinforce the seriousness of belief in the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عذاب القبر ما أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة وابن ماجه عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: يُسلّط الله على الكافر في قبره تسعةً وتسعين تنيناً، تنهشُهُ وتلدغُهُ حتى تقوم الساعة، ولو أن تنيناً منها نفخ على الأرض ما أنبتت خضراء، والتنين: بكسر المثناة الفوقية وتشديد النون؛ وهو أكبر الثعابين قيل: وحكمة هذا العدد أنه كفر بأسماء الله الحسنى، وهي تسعة وتسعون. ومن عذابه أيضاً ضغطته، وهي التقاء حافتيه، وورد أن الأرض تضمه حتى تختلف أضلاعُه، ولا ينجو منها أحد ولو صغيراً؛ سواء كان صالحاً أو طالحاً إلا الأنبياء.
And from the punishment of the grave is what Ibn Abi Shayba and Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may God be pleased with him, who said: I heard the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, say: 'God will set upon the disbeliever in his grave ninety-nine dragons, which bite and sting him until the Hour is established, and if a dragon of them were to blow on the earth, it would not grow anything green.' And al-tinnin (the dragon) is with a kasra of the second letter and a shadda on the nun; it is the largest of snakes. It is said: The wisdom of this number is that he disbelieved in the beautiful names of God, which are ninety-nine. And from his punishment also is its pressing (daghṭatuh), which is the meeting of its two sides, and it has been reported that the earth presses him until his ribs become different, and no one escapes it, even a small person, whether righteous or wicked, except the prophets.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage provides concrete examples of the punishment of the grave, forming an expansion on the earlier definition. The author first cites a hadith from Ibn Abi Shayba and Ibn Majah: God will send ninety-nine dragons upon the disbeliever in his grave, which will continuously bite and sting him until the Day of Judgment. The dragons are defined as the largest snakes. The wisdom of the number ninety-nine is that it corresponds to the number of God's beautiful names (al-asma' al-husna), which the disbeliever rejected. The author then mentions another punishment: the pressing of the grave (daghṭat al-qabr), which is the meeting of its two sides. The earth squeezes the deceased so tightly that the ribs interlock. This punishment applies to everyone—whether righteous or wicked, young or old—with the sole exception of the prophets. Thus the passage emphasizes the severity and universality of the punishment.

Key Terms
تنين
ضغطة القبر
الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the punishment of the grave is only spiritual and not physical.
Correction: This passage shows that the punishment includes physical torment: dragons biting and stinging, and the grave pressing the body so that ribs interlock.

Checkpoint

A) All believers
B) Prophets only
C) Martyrs only
D) No one is exempt

Key Takeaway

The Reality of Punishment of the Grave: Body and Soul Together
Ibn al-Murshidi defends the reality of punishment of the grave, clarifying its scope and the body-soul union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave affects both body and soul, applies to every deceased person Allah intends to punish regardless of their physical state or burial, and that this is the consensus of Ahl al-Haqq despite a dissenting opinion.

Core Idea
Punishment of the grave is real for body and soul, extending beyond burial.

This lesson unpacks the doctrine of grave punishment as explained by Ibn al-Murshidi. While often associated solely with burial, he clarifies that Allah's punishment reaches any deceased person, no matter how they died or were disposed. The central debate concerns whether only the body or both body and soul are punished—a point of consensus among Ahl al-Haqq, with notable dissent from al-Tabari and Ibn Karram.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scope of punishment
Note that punishment is not limited to those buried in a grave; any dead person Allah intends to punish will be punished, even if cremated, eaten, or drowned.
The phrase 'عذاب القبر' is a general term for the dominant case.
2
Identify the consensus of Ahl al-Haqq
Ahl al-Haqq agree that both body and soul are punished together. This is the orthodox position.
3
Recognize the dissenting view
Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari and Abdullah ibn Karram claimed only the body is punished, with Allah creating special perception in it.
This view is rejected by the author.
4
Learn the categories and duration
Punishment applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and sinful believers. It is perpetual for the first two, but may cease for some sinners, especially those with light sins, and can be lifted by supplication or charity.
Those not questioned in the grave (e.g., children, insane) are not punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثُمَّ عَذَابُ القَبْرِ) عطف على قوله : (سؤالنا)، لمشاركته له في حكمه الآتي وهو الوجوب، وإنما أضيف إلى القبر لأنه الغالب، وإلا فكل ميت أراد الله تعذيبه عُذْبَ، قبر أو لم يُقبر، ولو صلب أو غرق في بحر أو أكلته الدواب أو أحرق حتى صار رماداً وذُريَ في الريح، ولا يمنع من ذلك كون الميت تفرقت أجزاؤه، والمعذب البدن والروح جميعاً باتفاق أهل الحق، وخالف محمد بن جرير الطبري وعبد الله بن کرام وطائفةٌ فقالوا : المعذب البدن فقط، ويخلق الله فيه إدراكاً بحيث يسمع ويعلم ويلتذ ويتألم . ويكون للكافر والمنافق وعصاة المؤمنين، ويدوم على الأولين، وينقطع عن بعض عصاة المؤمنين؛ وهو من خفت جرائمهم من العصاة فإنهم يعذبون بحسبها، وقد يُرفع عنهم بدعاء أو صدقةٍ أو غير ذلك، كما قاله ابن القيم وكل من كان لا يُسأل في قبره لا يُعذب فيه أيضاً .
His saying: 'Then the punishment of the grave' is conjuncted to his saying: 'our questioning', due to its sharing with it in its upcoming ruling which is obligation. It is attributed to the grave because it is the dominant case. Otherwise, every dead person whom Allah intends to punish is punished, whether buried or not, even if crucified, drowned in the sea, eaten by beasts, burned until ashes and scattered in the wind. The fact that the dead person's parts have separated does not prevent that. The punished is the body and the soul together by consensus of the people of truth. Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari and Abdullah ibn Karram and a group opposed, saying: The punished is the body alone, and Allah creates in it perception such that it hears, knows, takes pleasure, and feels pain. And it is for the disbeliever, the hypocrite, and disobedient believers. It continues for the first two, and ceases for some disobedient believers. It is for those of the disobedient whose crimes are light: they are punished according to them, and it may be lifted from them by supplication, charity, or other than that, as Ibn al-Qayyim said. And whoever is not questioned in his grave is not punished in it either.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the line 'ثُمَّ عَذَابُ القَبْرِ' from the poem Jawharat al-Tawhid. The author, Ibn al-Murshidi, begins by clarifying the grammatical and legal connection between punishment of the grave and the earlier mentioned questioning. He notes that it is called 'punishment of the grave' because burial is the most common case, but in reality any dead person Allah intends to punish is punished regardless of their state — buried, crucified, drowned, eaten, or cremated. The disintegration of the body does not prevent punishment. The key doctrinal point is that both body and soul are punished together, which is the position of Ahl al-Haqq. He then reports the contrary view of Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari and Abdullah ibn Karram (and a group) who claim only the body is punished and that Allah creates in it a special perception. The author then specifies that punishment applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and sinful believers. It is perpetual for disbelievers and hypocrites but may cease for some sinful believers — those with light sins are punished proportionally, and punishment can be removed by supplication or charity, as stated by Ibn al-Qayyim. Finally, he notes that those who are not questioned in the grave (e.g., children, the insane) are not punished.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
البدن والروح
محمد بن جرير الطبري
عبد الله بن كرام
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the body is punished in the grave.
Correction: Ahl al-Haqq affirm that both body and soul are punished together, as stated in the passage.

Checkpoint
According to the author, who among the following holds the view that only the body is punished in the grave?
A) Ibn al-Qayyim
B) Ibn Jarir al-Tabari and Ibn Karram
C) The consensus of Ahl al-Haqq
D) The author himself

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is a reality for body and soul, extending to all deceased whom Allah intends to punish, regardless of their physical state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the punishment of the grave is real for both body and soul, even if your body is burned to ashes. Are you living today as if that reality is certain? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that every sin you commit now could affect your state immediately after death?
?
The passage says that punishment may be lifted by supplication, charity, or other good deeds. When was the last time you sincerely made dua for a deceased Muslim, or gave charity with the intention of easing their punishment? If you haven't, what is stopping you from doing so right now?
?
The dissenting view of al-Tabari and Ibn Karram held that only the body is punished, and Allah creates perception in it. This lesson affirms the consensus that both body and soul are punished together. Do you accept this doctrine as truth, or does your heart harbor any doubt? Examine yourself: are you fully convinced, or do you need to strengthen your faith in the unseen matters of the grave?

The 99 Dragons in the Grave
Hadith on 99 dragons tormenting the disbeliever in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about 99 dragons tormenting the disbeliever in the grave and the wisdom behind the number 99.

Core Idea
The disbeliever's denial of 99 names leads to torment by 99 dragons.

This lesson presents a frightening hadith about the punishment of the grave specifically for disbelievers. The author narrates a report from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri describing 99 dragons that bite and sting the disbeliever until the Hour. We also learn the linguistic meaning of 'tinnin' and the connection to the 99 beautiful names of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic narration and its translation once to get the overall meaning. Notice the specific number '99' and the description of the dragons' effect.
2
Understand the linguistic note
The author explains the word 'tinnin' (dragon) – its pronunciation and meaning as the largest snake. Consider why this word is used.
3
Reflect on the wisdom of the number
The author states that the number 99 corresponds to the 99 beautiful names of Allah which the disbeliever denied. Connect the punishment to the sin.
This links theology to eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عذاب القبر ما أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة وابن ماجه عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه قال : سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : يُسلّط الله على الكافر في قبره تسعةً وتسعين تنيناً، تنهشُهُ وتلدغُهُ حتى تقوم الساعة، ولو أن تنيناً منها نفخ على الأرض ما أنبتت خضراء» ، والتنين : بكسر المثناة الفوقية وتشديد النون؛ وهو أكبر الثعابين قيل : وحكمة هذا العدد أنه كفر بأسماء الله الحسنى، وهي تسعة وتسعون . ومن عذابه أيضاً ضغطته، وهي التقاء حافتيه، وورد أن الأرض تضمه حتى تختلف أضلاعُه ، ولا ينجو منها أحد ولو صغيراً ؛ سواء كان صالحاً أو طالحاً إلا الأنبياء، وإلا فاطمة بنت أسد، وإلا من قرأ سورة الإخلاص في مرضه، ولو نجا منها أحد، لنجا منها سعد بن معاذ الذي اهتز عرش الرحمن لموته .
And from the punishment of the grave is what Ibn Abi Shayba and Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, say: 'Allah will set upon the disbeliever in his grave ninety-nine dragons, which will bite and sting him until the Hour is established. If one of them were to blow on the earth, it would not produce any green.' The dragon (al-tinnin) is with a kasra on the second letter and a shadda on the noon; it is the largest of snakes. It was said: The wisdom of this number is that he disbelieved in the beautiful names of Allah, which are ninety-nine. And from its punishment also is its pressure (dughta), which is the meeting of its two sides. It is reported that the earth presses him until his ribs become interlocked. And no one escapes it, even a small child, whether righteous or wicked, except the prophets, except Fatima bint Asad, and except the one who recited Surat al-Ikhlas during his illness. And if anyone were to escape it, Sa'd ibn Mu'adh would have escaped it, he whose death made the Throne of the Merciful tremble.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the discussion on punishments of the grave. The author first presents a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri regarding ninety-nine dragons that torment the disbeliever in his grave until the Day of Judgment. He explains the linguistic form of the word 'tinnin' and a possible wisdom for the number ninety-nine — corresponding to the disbeliever's denial of Allah's ninety-nine beautiful names. Then he moves to another punishment, the 'pressure of the grave' (dughtat al-qabr), defined as the two sides of the grave squeezing together. He reports that the earth presses the dead person until his ribs interlock. Importantly, this pressure spares no one — not even small children — except three categories: prophets, Fatima bint Asad (the mother of Ali), and those who recited Surat al-Ikhlas while ill. The author then notes that even Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, despite his high rank and the Throne trembling at his death, did not escape it, implying that these exceptions are specific by divine will.

Key Terms
تنين
أسماء الله الحسنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the punishment of dragons is literal in a physical sense.
Correction: The hadith is authentic and describes a real but unseen punishment; the 'dragon' here is a created being that causes torment in the grave.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The 99 dragons in the grave symbolize a punishment proportionate to the disbeliever's rejection of Allah's 99 names.

The Pressure of the Grave and Its Exceptions
Description of grave pressure and list of exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pressure of the grave (dughtat al-qabr) and which individuals are exempt from it according to the text.

Core Idea
The grave's pressure afflicts all except prophets, Fatima bint Asad, and those who recited Ikhlas at death.

This lesson covers another punishment of the grave: the pressure (dughta) that compresses the dead person until their ribs interlock. The author lists exceptions to this universal torment, including prophets, a specific companion, and those who recite Surah al-Ikhlas in their final illness. A note about Sa'd ibn Mu'adh underscores the severity of this pressure.
