The Bliss of the Grave: Sensory Rewards for Believers
Ibn al-Murshidi describes the bliss of the grave for believers with sensory details and textual evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the bliss of the grave is a real, sensory experience for believers, described in detail through mass-transmitted revelations, and that it includes expansion, a window to Paradise, fragrant basil, and illumination.

Core Idea
The bliss of the grave is a tangible gift from Allah, vividly described in revelation.

This lesson begins the section on sam'iyyat — matters known only through divine revelation. The author explains that the bliss of the grave is for believers, based on mass-transmitted texts. He then enumerates four specific sensory details of this bliss, showing that it is a real, physical experience, not merely spiritual.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the sam'iyyat context
Understand that this passage deals with matters of the unseen that must be accepted based on revelation. The author is commenting on a line from a poem.
The term 'sam'iyyat' refers to matters known only through hearing (revelation).
2
Identify the scope of the bliss
Note that while called 'bliss of the grave,' it is not limited to those buried in graves or to this specific community. The author clarifies that it is attributed to the grave because that is the most common case.
3
Enumerate the four blessings
Find and list the four features: expansion to seventy cubits, a window to Paradise, filled with fragrant basil, and a garden with a lamp that illuminates like the full moon.
Each feature emphasizes sensory experience.
4
Reflect on the sensory nature
Consider why these details are given — to affirm the reality and physicality of the afterlife rewards. This counters purely spiritual interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات . قوله : : (نَعِيْمُهُ) أي: ونعيم القبر، فهو معطوف على ما تقدم بإسقاط حرف العطف، ويكون للمؤمنين لما ورد في ذلك من النصوص البالغة مبلغ التواتر، وإنما أضيف إلى القبر لأنه الغالب وإلا فلا يختص بالمقبور ولا يختص بمؤمني هذه الأمة ولا بالمكلفين ومن نعيمه توسيعه سبعين ذراعاً عرضاً وكذا طولاً، ومنه أيضاً فتح طاقة فيه من الجنة، وامتلاؤه بالريحان، وجعله روضة من رياض الجنة، وجعلُ قنديل، بفتح القاف، فيه فينور له قبره كالقمر ليلة البدر.
The sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation). His saying: 'Its bliss' — that is, the bliss of the grave. It is conjuncted to what preceded, omitting the conjunction particle, and it is for the believers due to the texts that have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission) that have come concerning that. It is attributed to the grave because it is the dominant case; otherwise it is not specific to the buried, nor specific to the believers of this nation, nor to the legally responsible. And from its bliss is its expansion to seventy cubits in width and likewise in length, and also the opening of a window into it from Paradise, and its being filled with fragrant basil, and its being made a garden from the gardens of Paradise, and the placing of a lamp, with fatha on the qaf, in it, so that his grave is illuminated for him like the moon on the night of the full moon.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage introduces the 'sam'iyyat' section, which deals with matters known only through revelation. The author comments on the poem's line 'نَعِيْمُهُ' meaning the bliss of the grave. He explains that it is conjoined to the previous clause, and that this bliss is for believers, based on numerous texts that are mutawatir (mass-transmitted). He clarifies that while it is called 'bliss of the grave', it is not exclusive to those buried in a grave, nor to believers of this specific community, nor to those who are legally responsible (mukallaf). Then he details four aspects of this bliss: (1) expansion of the grave to seventy cubits in both width and length; (2) opening a window from Paradise into the grave; (3) the grave being filled with fragrant basil; (4) the grave being turned into a garden from the gardens of Paradise, and a lamp being placed there that illuminates the grave like the full moon. The note about 'قنديل' with fatha on qaf is a linguistic remark indicating the correct pronunciation.

Key Terms
نعيم القبر
السمعيات
توسيع القبر
طاقة من الجنة
ريحان
روضة من رياض الجنة
قنديل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The bliss of the grave is only for those who are actually buried in a grave.
Correction: The author clarifies it is not specific to the buried, nor to believers of this nation, nor to the legally responsible.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a feature of the bliss of the grave in this passage?
A) Expansion to seventy cubits
B) Opening a window to Paradise
C) Filled with fruits from Paradise
D) Illumination like the full moon

Key Takeaway
The bliss of the grave is a real, sensory experience for believers, affirmed by mass-transmitted texts, and includes expansion, a window to Paradise, fragrance, and light.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your grave were to be expanded to seventy cubits tonight, would your heart feel spacious with faith or constricted with regret? What one thing can you do today to ensure it is the former?
?
The lamp in the grave shines like the full moon—but only for those who believed. When you are alone in the dark, will you have that light? What are you relying on to illuminate your grave?
?
Fragrant basil and a garden from Paradise replace the earth of the grave for believers. Are you living now in a way that your final resting place becomes a garden, or are you planting thorns with your daily choices?

Definition and Basis of Grave Bliss
Definition and general ruling on grave bliss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the bliss of the grave is, whom it is for, and why it is affirmed based on tawatur.

Core Idea
Grave bliss is a literal reality for believers, firmly established by mass-transmitted texts.

The commentator begins by clarifying the term 'na'eemuhu' from the poem, linking it to the bliss of the grave. This lesson unpacks the definition, the evidential basis from mutawatir texts, and the scope of who receives this bliss, setting the foundation for understanding its concrete manifestations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'na'eemuhu'
Learn that 'na'eemuhu' refers to the bliss of the grave, conjoined to previous phrases. Notice the grammatical construction.
2
Identify the textual basis
Recognize that the bliss is affirmed by texts reaching the level of tawatur, meaning they are mass-transmitted and certain.
3
Clarify the scope of recipients
Note that the bliss is for believers generally, not limited to the buried, this nation, or the legally responsible.
4
Grasp the literal interpretation
Understand that the commentator affirms the literal reality of these descriptions, not metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (نَعِيْمُهُ) أي: ونعيم القبر، فهو معطوف على ما تقدم بإسقاط حرف العطف، ويكون للمؤمنين لما ورد في ذلك من النصوص البالغة مبلغ التواتر، وإنما أضيف إلى القبر لأنه الغالب وإلا فلا يختص بالمقبور ولا يختص بمؤمني هذه الأمة ولا بالمكلفين ومن نعيمه توسيعه سبعين ذراعاً عرضاً وكذا طولاً، ومنه أيضاً فتح طاقة فيه من الجنة، وامتلاؤه بالريحان، وجعله روضة من رياض الجنة، وجعلُ قنديل بفتح القاف فيه فينور له قبره كالقمر ليلة البدر . وقد ورد أن الله تعالى أوحى إلى موسى : تعلم الخير وعلمه الناس، فإني منوِّرُ لمعلم العلم ومتعلمه قبورهم حتى لا يستوحشوا لمكانهم، وعن عمر مرفوعاً: «مَنْ نور في مساجد الله نور الله له في قبره، وكل هذا محمول على حقيقته عند العلماء.
His statement: 'His bliss' means the bliss of the grave. It is conjoined to what preceded by dropping the conjunction, and it is for the believers due to the texts that have reached the level of tawatur. It is only attributed to the grave because it is the predominant case; otherwise it is not specific to the buried, nor specific to the believers of this nation, nor to the legally responsible. Among its bliss are: expanding it seventy cubits in width and likewise length, and also opening a window in it to Paradise, filling it with basil, making it a garden from the gardens of Paradise, and making a lamp in it that illuminates his grave like the moon on the night of the full moon. And it has been reported that Allah Almighty revealed to Moses: 'Learn good and teach it to people, for I will illuminate the graves of the teacher of knowledge and the learner so that they will not feel lonely in their place.' And from Umar as a marfu' hadith: 'Whoever lights up the mosques of Allah, Allah will light up his grave for him.' And all of this is understood literally according to the scholars.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the term 'na'eemuhu' (His bliss) from the poem. The commentator clarifies that it refers to the bliss of the grave, which is conjoined to previous statements. He establishes that this bliss is for believers based on abundant textual evidence reaching the level of mutawatir. He then notes that the attribution to the grave is merely because it is the typical context, but the bliss is not exclusive to those buried in graves, nor to believers of this specific nation, nor to those who are legally responsible. He enumerates several specific aspects of this bliss: expansion of the grave to seventy cubits in width and length, a window opened to Paradise, filling with basil, becoming a garden of Paradise, and a lamp that illuminates the grave like a full moon. He then cites additional reports: a divine revelation to Moses promising illumination of graves for teachers and learners of knowledge, and a hadith from Umar promising light in the grave for those who illuminate mosques. He concludes that all these descriptions are to be understood literally by the scholars, affirming their reality.

نعيم القبر
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A single hadith
B) The consensus of scholars
C) Texts that have reached the level of tawatur
D) Logical deduction

Key Takeaway
The bliss of the grave is a real, literally understood reward for believers, established by mass-transmitted texts and not limited by burial or legal responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says grave bliss is not limited to those buried or to the legally responsible. Does this widen your hope in Allah's mercy? Or does it make you more aware of the need for faith?
?
How would your daily actions change if you truly believed with certainty that the bliss of the grave is awaiting you? Is there a fear or a hope that you are not living out?

Specific Manifestations of Grave Bliss

After establishing the general reality of grave bliss, the commentator enumerates specific blessings described in Islamic texts. These include physical expansion of the grave, a view of Paradise, pleasant scents, and divine illumination. He enumerates several specific aspects of this bliss: expansion of the grave to seventy cubits in width and length, a window opened to Paradise, filling with basil, becoming a garden of Paradise, and a lamp that illuminates the grave like a full moon. He then cites additional reports: a divine revelation to Moses promising illumination of graves for teachers and learners of knowledge, and a hadith from Umar promising light in the grave for those who illuminate mosques. He concludes that all these descriptions are to be understood literally by the scholars, affirming their reality.

Key Terms

القنديل

Correction: The passage explicitly says all descriptions are understood literally by scholars.

A) Expansion to seventy cubits

Key Takeaway
The bliss of the grave includes tangible, literal physical experiences such as expansion, light, and fragrance, as clearly stated in revealed texts.

Belief in Grave Matters is Obligatory
The commentator states the ruling of belief in the three grave matters as wajib sam'iy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the three matters concerning the grave are obligatory to believe according to Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
What is possible and reported by the truthful one is obligatory to believe.

Before diving into the details of the questioning in the grave, its bliss and punishment, the commentator first establishes the ruling: belief in these matters is obligatory. This short but decisive passage gives the logical basis for that obligation and identifies the groups that accept or reject it. The reasoning is simple yet foundational for all sam'iyyat.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the strict definition of 'wajib' being introduced.
The passage is compact but carries a complete argument.
2
Identify the reasoning chain
The commentator gives a logical sequence: these matters are possible → reported by the truthful one → therefore obligatory. See how he uses 'kullu ma huwa kadhalika' to generalise the rule.
This is a key principle in Islamic theology: possibility + truthful report = obligation to believe.
3
Note the sectarian landscape
Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of Mu'tazila agree on this obligation, while the Mulhida deny all three. Reflect on why this classification matters for later debates.
The Mulhida's denial is a rejection of the prophetic reports, not a disagreement about reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (واجب) بسكون الباء للوزن، وهو خبر قوله : (سؤالنا)، وما عطف عليه، فكلُّ واحدٍ من الثلاثة المذكورة واجب سمعاً ؛ لأنه أمر ممكن أخبر به الصادق، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو واجب، وهذا ما عليه أهل السنة وجمهور المعتزلة، وأنكرت الملحدة كُلا هذه الثلاثة .
His statement: 'Wajib' with a sukun on the 'ba' for meter. It is the predicate of his statement 'our questioning' and what is conjoined to it. So each one of the three mentioned is obligatory by hearing (sam'an) because it is a possible matter reported by the truthful one, and everything that is so is obligatory. This is the position of Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila, and the Mulhida deny all three.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage explains the term 'wajib' (obligatory) from the poem. The commentator notes that it is the predicate of 'sualuna' (our questioning) and its conjunctions. He states that each of the three matters (questioning, bliss, punishment of the grave) is wajib sam'iy (obligatory by transmitted evidence). The reasoning: these matters are possible (mumkin) in themselves, and they have been reported by the truthful one (al-sadiq, i.e., the Prophet). Whatever is possible and confirmed by truthful report is obligatory to believe. He then notes that this is the position of Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila, while the Mulhida (atheists or deniers) reject all three. This establishes the doctrinal consensus on the obligation of this belief.

المعتزلة

B) They are possible and reported by the truthful one

D) They are derived from analogy

Key Takeaway
Belief in the questioning, bliss, and punishment of the grave is obligatory because these are possible matters confirmed by truthful prophetic reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Mulhida deny all three grave matters out of rejection of prophecy. Examine your own heart: Is there any area where you resist a prophetic teaching because it seems difficult or inconvenient? Confess it and seek Allah's help to submit fully.

Resurrection and the Identity of the Body
The commentator defines resurrection and defends the identity of the resurrected body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of bodily resurrection, including the definition of ba'th, the concept of original parts, and the theological defense of the identity of the resurrected body.

Core Idea
Bodily resurrection is real, and the same body returns through its lasting original parts.

This lesson delves into one of the central beliefs of Islam: the resurrection of the body. The commentator explains resurrection as the reviving of the dead after gathering their original parts, and then defends, through al-Subki's argument, that the resurrected body is identical to the worldly one despite changes in size. Understanding this helps clarify why bodily resurrection is both rational and consistent with divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the definition of ba'th and the key term 'original parts'.
2
Understand the definition of ba'th
Identify how the commentator defines resurrection and what 'original parts' means. These are parts that persist from birth to death, unlike nails or hair.
3
Follow al-Subki's objection and response
The passage presents two objections: (1) original parts are too few to reconstitute the body; (2) adding new parts would break identity. See how al-Subki answers each.
The first answer: God adds created parts to achieve size. The second: identity is based on original parts.
4
Grasp the concept of 'identity' (ʿayniyya)
Understand that identity of the resurrected body is preserved through the original parts, not through the total size or added parts. This ensures reward and punishment apply to the same person.
The passage argues that without this view, the punished or rewarded would not be the same person who died.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب اعتقادِ الحشر والنشر قوله: (كَبَعْثِ الحَشْرِ) أي: بعث الناس للحشر؛ فالإضافة على معنى اللام والتشبيه في الوجوب . والبعثُ عبارةٌ عن إحياء الموتى وإخراجهم من قبورهم بعد جمع الأجزاء الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، ولو قطعت قبل موته بخلاف التي ليس من شأنها ذلك ؛ كالظُّفُر . قال الشيخ تاج الدين السبكي في شرحه لـ «عقيدة ابن الحاجب : لا يقال : الأجزاء الأصلية لا يفي مقدارها بمقدار ما يكون عليه الإنسان من المقدار عند الموت، مع أن المعلوم قطعاً بالإجماع هو أنه لا بد أن تكون الإعادة على الهيئة التي فارق الإنسان عليها الدنيا ؛ لأنا نقول : الأجزاء الأصلية هي المعادة، لكن القادر المختار كما أنه بقدرته مد مقدار الإنسان بزيادة تلك الأجزاء الغذائية في الدنيا ، فهو قادر على أن يمد مقداره يوم القيامة بأجزاء اختراعية حتى تحصل الهيئة . فإن قيل : الشيء مع الشيء غيره مع شيء آخر، وعلى ما ذكر لا يكون البدن المعاد هو بعينه الكائن يوم الفراق، بل هو مثله لا عينه مع أن الإجماع على إعادة العين . قلنا : مثله هو ، من حيث المقدار، عينه باعتبار تلك الأجزاء الأصلية، وهو المراد بالعينية؛ إذ لو لم يُرد بالعينية ذلك .. لم يكن المعذب والمنعم هو عين الإنسان المفارق، بل مثله، لما ثبت أن -
The obligation of believing in resurrection and spreading. His statement: 'Like the resurrection of the gathering' means the raising of people for the gathering. The annexation is for the meaning of 'lam' and comparison in obligation. 'Ba'th' is reviving the dead and bringing them out of their graves after gathering the original parts, which are those that persist from the beginning of life to its end, even if cut off before death, unlike those that are not like that, such as the nail. Shaykh Taj al-Din al-Subki said in his commentary on 'Aqida Ibn al-Hajib: It cannot be said: 'The original parts do not suffice in quantity for what the human being's size is at death, while it is definitively known by consensus that the return must be in the form that the person left the world' — for we say: The original parts are what is returned, but the Omnipotent and Free Chosen, just as He by His power extended the human's size by adding those nutritive parts in the world, so He is able to extend his size on the Day of Resurrection by created parts until the form is attained. If it is said: 'A thing with another thing is different from a different thing, and on what is mentioned, the body that is returned is not the very same as the one on the day of parting, but rather it is its likeness, not its identity, while there is consensus on the return of identity.' We say: It is its likeness in terms of size, and its identity in consideration of those original parts, and that is what is meant by identity. For if identity were not meant by that, the punished and rewarded would not be the very same person who departed, but his likeness, because it is established that —.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation of believing in resurrection (ba'th al-hashr). It begins by glossing the poem's phrase 'kaba'th al-hashr' and explains that 'ba'th' means reviving the dead and bringing them out of their graves after gathering their 'ajza' al-ashiyya' (original parts). These parts are defined as those that persist from the beginning of life to its end, even if they are severed before death, unlike transitory parts like nails. The commentator then quotes Taj al-Din al-Subki's commentary, which presents and resolves an objection. The objection is that the original parts are insufficient in quantity to reconstitute the body's full size at death, and yet there is consensus that the resurrected body must have the same form as at death. Al-Subki answers: The original parts themselves are what are returned, but God, being omnipotent, can add newly created parts (ajza' ikhtira'iyya) to achieve the proper size. A further objection is raised: If new parts are added, the returned body is not identical to the original but merely similar, contradicting the consensus that the very same body (ayn) is returned. The answer is that the body is identical with respect to the original parts, while it is similar in size. Identity ('ayniyya) is understood in terms of those permanent parts; otherwise the same person would not be rewarded or punished. The passage concludes with an argument that without this understanding, the reward and punishment would not pertain to the very same person. The text cuts off, but the argument is essentially complete.

الحشر
الأجزاء الأصلية
الأجزاء الاختراعية
العينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection is only spiritual or the resurrected body is not the same as the worldly body.
Correction: The passage affirms that resurrection involves the very same body, with identity preserved through the original parts that persist throughout life.

Checkpoint
According to al-Subki's argument, what makes the resurrected body identical to the worldly body?
A) The same nutritive parts are returned
B) The original parts are returned
C) The body has the same size
D) God creates a perfect likeness

Key Takeaway
Bodily resurrection is real and the returned body is identical through its lasting original parts, by God's power to add form-appropriate parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your body in resurrection is the same body you have now because of its original parts, how does that change how you treat your body and its actions today? What does it mean for you that every physical deed will be resurrected with you?
?
The passage says identity is tied to the original parts that persist from beginning to end. What are the 'original parts' of your faith—the core beliefs and commitments that must remain unchanged? Are you guarding those, or letting them be replaced by transient 'nutritive' concerns?
?
God will add new parts to restore your body’s form at resurrection. In what area of your life—your character, relationships, or worship—are you resisting God's power to 'add' and reshape you for the better, even if it means a change from your current form?

The Definition of Baʿth and the Original Parts
Al-Bajuri defines baʿth as reviving the dead after collecting their original parts, briefly contrasting with temporary parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of baʿth (resurrection) according to classical Ashʿari theology and the concept of original parts (al-ajzāʾ al-aṣliyya) that are collected for resurrection.

Core Idea
Resurrection means reviving the dead after gathering their original, permanent body parts.

This lesson introduces one of the foundational samʿiyyāt (revealed matters) in Islamic creed: the resurrection of bodies. Al-Bajuri, in his commentary on al-Jawhara, defines baʿth precisely, distinguishing between the original parts of the body that persist throughout life and those that are temporary, like nails and hair. Understanding this distinction is key to the Islamic doctrine of bodily resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Al-Bajuri uses a very precise definition.
2
Understand the definition of baʿth
Focus on the key phrase: 'al-baʿthu ʿibāratun ʿan iḥyāʾ al-mawtā wa-ikhrājihim min qubūrihim baʿda jamʿi al-ajzāʾ al-aṣliyya.' This is the core definition.
The definition includes both reviving and bringing out of graves.
3
Distinguish original vs. non-original parts
Identify the two categories: original parts (al-ajzāʾ al-aṣliyya) that persist from birth to death, and non-original parts like nails (al-ẓufur). The passage contrasts them explicitly.
Original parts remain even if cut off before death.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Ask yourself why this distinction matters. It ensures the identity of the resurrected body is tied to its permanent components, not transient ones.
This connects to the broader debate about bodily resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (كَبَعْثِ الحَشْرِ) أي: بعث الناس للحشر؛ فالإضافة على معنى اللام والتشبيه في الوجوب . والبعثُ عبارةٌ عن إحياء الموتى وإخراجهم من قبورهم بعد جمع الأجزاء الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، ولو قطعت قبل موته بخلاف التي ليس من شأنها ذلك ؛ كالظُفُر .
His saying (ka-baʿthi al-ḥashri) means: raising the people for the gathering; so the genitive construction has the meaning of lām and likeness in obligation. And al-baʿth (resurrection) is an expression for reviving the dead and bringing them out of their graves after collecting the original parts, which are those that are characterized by remaining from the beginning of life to its end, even if they were cut off before his death, unlike those that are not characterized by that, like the nail.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage defines the term baʿth (resurrection) as used in the poem. The phrase 'ka-baʿthi al-ḥashri' means 'like the resurrection of the gathering.' The genitive construct (iḍāfa) here indicates that the resurrection is for the purpose of the gathering (ḥashr), and the comparison is in terms of obligation. The author then gives a technical definition: al-baʿth is the act of giving life to the dead and removing them from their graves after gathering the original parts (al-ajzāʾ al-aṣliyya). These original parts are those that remain from the beginning of a person's life to the end; they persist even if removed before death (like a limb that is cut off), unlike non-original parts such as fingernails and hair, which do not have this permanence. This distinction is important for understanding the identity of the resurrected body.

Key Terms
البعث
الأجزاء الأصلية
الحشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any part of the body is resurrected.
Correction: Only the original parts that persist from birth to death are collected for resurrection, not temporary parts like nails.

Checkpoint

A) All parts of the body including hair and nails
B) Only the original parts that persist from birth to death
C) The parts present at the moment of death
D) The soul only

Key Takeaway
Baʿth is the reviving of the dead after gathering their original, permanent body parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Definition of Hashr and the Gathering of All Creatures
Al-Bajuri defines hashr and presents a dispute on which beings are gathered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of hashr (gathering) and the scholarly dispute over whether all creatures or only those who will be judged are gathered.

Core Idea
Hashr is the driving of all creatures to the standing-place for judgment.

Al-Bajuri begins by defining the term hashr and describing the location of the gathering. He then addresses a key dispute: are all beings gathered, or only those who will be recompensed? This passage establishes the foundational understanding of the resurrection assembly.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of hashr
Notice that hashr is described as 'driving them all' to a specific location called al-mawqif, which is the changed land of Jerusalem.
The description of the land as one where Allah was not disobeyed is significant.
2
Identify the two groups mentioned
The passage distinguishes between those who are recompensed (humans, jinn, angels) and those who are not (animals and wild beasts).
3
Understand the two scholarly opinions
One opinion holds that all creatures are gathered, even those not recompensed. Another opinion restricts gathering to only those who will be judged.
Al-Nawawi confirmed the first opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحشرُ عبارة عن سوقهم جميعاً إلى الموقف، وهو الموضع الذي يقفون فيه من أرض القدس المبدَّلة التي لم يُعصَ الله عليها لفصل القضاء بينهم، ولا فرق في ذلك بين من يُجازى وهم الإنس والجن والملك، وبين من لا يُجازى كالبهائم والوحوش على ما ذهب إليه المحققون، وصحَّحه النووي، وذهبت طائفة إلى أنه لا يُحشر إلا من يُجازى، وهذا ظاهر في الكامل، وأما السِّقْط وهو الذي لم تتم له ستة أشهر؛ فإن أُلقي بعد نفخ الروح فيه أعيد بروحه، ويصير عند دخوله الجنة كأهلها في الجمال والطول، وإن أُلقي قبل نفخ الروح فيه كان كسائر الأجسام التي لا روح فيها كالحجر، فيُحشر ثم يصير تراباً . وأوَّلُ مَنْ تنشقُ عنه الأرض نبينا ﷺ، فهو أوَّلُ مَنْ يبعث وأوَّلُ وارد المحشر، كما أنه أوَّلُ داخل الجنة، وبعده سيدنا نوح ، وبعده سيدنا نوح كما ورد لكن ورد أن بعده أبا بكر (٣) ، وحُمل على أنه بعد الأنبياء.
And al-ḥashr (gathering) is an expression for driving them all to the standing-place (al-mawqif), which is the place where they stand in the changed land of Jerusalem (al-Quds), in which Allah was not disobeyed, for the final judgment between them. And there is no difference in that between those who are recompensed—and they are humans, jinn, and angels—and those who are not recompensed, like beasts and wild animals, according to what the investigators (al-muḥaqqiqūn) hold, and al-Nawawī confirmed it. And a group held that only those who are recompensed will be gathered, and this is apparent in al-Kāmil. As for the miscarried fetus (al-siqṭ), which is one for whom six months have not been completed: if it is expelled after the blowing of the spirit into it, it is returned with its spirit, and upon entering Paradise it becomes like its inhabitants in beauty and stature. But if expelled before the blowing of the spirit into it, it becomes like other bodies without a spirit, like stone, so it is gathered then becomes dust. And the first from whom the earth splits is our Prophet ﷺ, so he is the first to be resurrected and the first to arrive at the gathering-place, just as he is the first to enter Paradise. After him is our master Noah, and after him is our master Noah as reported, but it is reported that after him is Abū Bakr, and it is interpreted as after the prophets.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage defines ḥashr and provides several important details. First, ḥashr is the act of driving all creatures to the standing-place (al-mawqif), which is described as the changed land of Jerusalem where no sin was committed, serving as the location for judgment. The author notes a scholarly difference: some say all creatures are gathered, including animals (beasts and wild animals), but only humans, jinn, and angels are recompensed; others say only those who are recompensed are gathered. The first opinion is supported by the investigators and al-Nawawī. Second, regarding a miscarried fetus (al-siqṭ, less than six months gestation), if it was expelled after the spirit was blown into it (at 120 days according to other sources), it is resurrected with its spirit and upon entering Paradise becomes like its inhabitants. If expelled before the spirit entered, it is like other bodies without a soul (e.g., a stone), so it will be gathered only to become dust. Third, the Prophet Muhammad is the first whose grave splits open, the first to be resurrected, the first to arrive at the gathering-place, and the first to enter Paradise. After him comes Noah, and then after Noah there is a tradition that Abū Bakr follows, but it is understood that he follows after the prophets.

الموقف
الإنس
الجن

Correction: The passage states that all creatures—including animals and jinn—are gathered, though only humans, jinn, and angels are recompensed.

The Miscarried Fetus and the Resurrection
Al-Bajuri explains the fate of a miscarried fetus based on the timing of the spirit's blowing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on the miscarried fetus based on whether the spirit was blown into it before expulsion.

Core Idea
A miscarried fetus is resurrected with its spirit if the spirit was blown; otherwise it becomes dust.

After discussing the general gathering, Al-Bajuri addresses a specific case: the miscarried fetus (al-siqṭ). This answers a common question about the fate of beings who did not complete gestation. The ruling hinges on whether the spirit (ruh) was blown into the fetus, which occurs at 120 days according to other sources.

Guided Path
1
Define al-siqṭ
Al-siqṭ refers to a fetus expelled before completing six months of gestation.
2
Identify the two cases
The passage distinguishes between expulsion after the spirit is blown and expulsion before the spirit is blown.
The spirit is blown at 120 days (outside this text, but relevant).
3
Understand the outcomes
If after spirit: the fetus is resurrected with spirit and enters Paradise. If before: it is gathered and becomes dust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحشرُ عبارة عن سوقهم جميعاً إلى الموقف، وهو الموضع الذي يقفون فيه من أرض القدس المبدَّلة التي لم يُعصَ الله عليها لفصل القضاء بينهم، ولا فرق في ذلك بين من يُجازى وهم الإنس والجن والملك، وبين من لا يُجازى كالبهائم والوحوش على ما ذهب إليه المحققون، وصحَّحه النووي، وذهبت طائفة إلى أنه لا يُحشر إلا من يُجازى، وهذا ظاهر في الكامل، وأما السِّقْط وهو الذي لم تتم له ستة أشهر؛ فإن أُلقي بعد نفخ الروح فيه أعيد بروحه، ويصير عند دخوله الجنة كأهلها في الجمال والطول، وإن أُلقي قبل نفخ الروح فيه كان كسائر الأجسام التي لا روح فيها كالحجر، فيُحشر ثم يصير تراباً . وأوَّلُ مَنْ تنشقُ عنه الأرض نبينا ﷺ، فهو أوَّلُ مَنْ يبعث وأوَّلُ وارد المحشر، كما أنه أوَّلُ داخل الجنة، وبعده سيدنا نوح ، وبعده سيدنا نوح كما ورد لكن ورد أن بعده أبا بكر (٣) ، وحُمل على أنه بعد الأنبياء.
And al-ḥashr (gathering) is an expression for driving them all to the standing-place (al-mawqif), which is the place where they stand in the changed land of Jerusalem (al-Quds), in which Allah was not disobeyed, for the final judgment between them. And there is no difference in that between those who are recompensed—and they are humans, jinn, and angels—and those who are not recompensed, like beasts and wild animals, according to what the investigators (al-muḥaqqiqūn) hold, and al-Nawawī confirmed it. And a group held that only those who are recompensed will be gathered, and this is apparent in al-Kāmil. As for the miscarried fetus (al-siqṭ), which is one for whom six months have not been completed: if it is expelled after the blowing of the spirit into it, it is returned with its spirit, and upon entering Paradise it becomes like its inhabitants in beauty and stature. But if expelled before the blowing of the spirit into it, it becomes like other bodies without a spirit, like stone, so it is gathered then becomes dust. And the first from whom the earth splits is our Prophet ﷺ, so he is the first to be resurrected and the first to arrive at the gathering-place, just as he is the first to enter Paradise. After him is our master Noah, and after him is our master Noah as reported, but it is reported that after him is Abū Bakr, and it is interpreted as after the prophets.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage defines ḥashr and provides several important details. First, ḥashr is the act of driving all creatures to the standing-place (al-mawqif), which is described as the changed land of Jerusalem where no sin was committed, serving as the location for judgment. The author notes a scholarly difference: some say all creatures are gathered, including animals (beasts and wild animals), but only humans, jinn, and angels are recompensed; others say only those who are recompensed are gathered. The first opinion is supported by the investigators and al-Nawawī. Second, regarding a miscarried fetus (al-siqṭ, less than six months gestation), if it was expelled after the spirit was blown into it (at 120 days according to other sources), it is resurrected with its spirit and upon entering Paradise becomes like its inhabitants. If expelled before the spirit entered, it is like other bodies without a soul (e.g., a stone), so it will be gathered only to become dust. Third, the Prophet Muhammad is the first whose grave splits open, the first to be resurrected, the first to arrive at the gathering-place, and the first to enter Paradise. After him comes Noah, and then after Noah there is a tradition that Abū Bakr follows, but it is understood that he follows after the prophets.

Key Terms
السِّقْط
نفخ الروح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think a miscarried fetus is not resurrected at all.
Correction: The passage states that if the spirit was blown, the fetus is resurrected with its spirit and enters Paradise.

Checkpoint
What happens to a miscarried fetus that is expelled after the blowing of the spirit?
A) It becomes dust immediately
B) It is resurrected with its spirit and enters Paradise
C) It is not resurrected
D) It is gathered but does not enter Paradise

Key Takeaway
A miscarried fetus is resurrected and enters Paradise if the spirit was blown; otherwise it becomes dust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to lose a child before birth, how would this teaching shape your trust in Allah's mercy? What would you say to yourself about that child's fate?
?
Do you live each day as though your spirit—which distinguishes you from lifeless matter—will be resurrected? What one change can you make today to prepare for that resurrection?
?
The miscarried fetus that had a spirit becomes like the inhabitants of Paradise in beauty. How does this reality challenge how you view human dignity, even in the womb? What action can you take this week to honor that dignity?

The Prophet's Precedence in Resurrection
Al-Bajuri states the Prophet's priority in resurrection and gathering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Prophet Muhammad is the first to be resurrected, the first at the gathering place, and the first to enter Paradise.

Core Idea
The Prophet is foremost in resurrection, gathering, and entering Paradise.

The passage concludes with a tremendous honor for the Prophet Muhammad. He is the first whose grave splits open, the first resurrected, the first to arrive at the gathering place, and the first to enter Paradise. Then it mentions the order of Noah and a tradition about Abu Bakr, showing the high rank of the Prophet.

The text repeats 'after him our master Noah' possibly due to scribal duplication.
3
Understand the interpretation
Abu Bakr's precedence is interpreted as being after the prophets, not before them.

Definition of al-Hashr and Its Universal Scope
Defines al-Hashr and discusses the scope of gathering including animals and miscarriages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-Hashr as the gathering of all creatures for judgment, including animals and miscarriages, and the differing scholarly opinions on who is gathered.

Core Idea
Al-Hashr gathers all beings—recompensed and non-recompensed—to the Standing Place.

The commentator opens by defining al-Hashr as the driving of all creatures to the Mawqif. He then addresses a key question: are only responsible beings gathered, or does this include animals and even miscarriages? The answer shapes our understanding of divine justice and mercy on the Day of Resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Hashr
Focus on the phrase 'عبارة عن سوقهم جميعاً إلى الموقف'. Notice the word 'جميعاً', which implies universality.
The Mawqif is the place of standing in a changed Jerusalem.
2
Identify the dispute about who is gathered
The text presents two views: the majority (including al-Nawawi) holds that all creatures are gathered, while a minority limits it to those who are recompensed. Find the arguments for each.
3
Understand the case of the miscarriage
The passage distinguishes between a miscarriage that had a soul (after four months) and one that did not. Trace the two scenarios and their outcomes.
This reinforces the principle that ensoulment determines resurrection.
4
Reflect on the teaching
Ask yourself: why does this inclusiveness matter? It emphasizes that all creation will witness the judgment, even if not judged themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحشر عبارة عن سوقهم جميعاً إلى الموقف، وهو الموضع الذي يقفون فيه من أرض القدس المبدَّلة التي لم يُعصَ الله عليها لفصل القضاء بينهم، ولا فرق في ذلك بين من يُجازى وهم الإنس والجن والملك، وبين من لا يُجازى كالبهائم والوحوش على ما ذهب إليه المحققون، وصحَّحه النووي، وذهبت طائفة إلى أنه لا يُحشر إلا من يُجازى، وهذا ظاهر في الكامل، وأما السِّقْط وهو الذي لم تتم له ستة أشهر؛ فإن أُلقي بعد نفخ الروح فيه أعيد بروحه، ويصير عند دخوله الجنة كأهلها في الجمال والطول، وإن أُلقي قبل نفخ الروح فيه كان كسائر الأجسام التي لا روح فيها كالحجر، فيُحشر ثم يصير تراباً . وأوَّلُ مَنْ تنشقُ عنه الأرض نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم، فهو أوَّلُ مَنْ يبعث وأوَّلُ وارد المحشر، كما أنه أوَّلُ داخل الجنة، وبعده سيدنا نوح عليه السلام، كما ورد لكن ورد أن بعده أبا بكر، وحُمل على أنه بعد الأنبياء. ومراتب الناس في الحشر متفاوتة؛ فمنهم الراكب وهو المتقي، ومنهم الماشي على رجليه؛ وهو قليل العمل، ومنهم الماشي على وجهه؛ وهو الكافر وهذا الحشر المذكور هنا هو أحد أنواع الحشر من حيث هو . ثانيها : صرفُ الناس من الموقف إلى الجنة أو النار، وهذان النوعان في الآخرة. ثالثها : إخراجُ اليهود من جزيرة العرب إلى الشام وهو المذكور في قوله تعالى : ﴿هُوَ الَّذِى أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَبِ مِن دِيَارِهِم لِأَوَّلِ الحَشْرِ﴾ [الحشر: ٢]. رابعها : سَوْقُ النار التي تخرجُ من أرض عدن باليمن للكفار وغيرهم من كلِّ حَيٍّ قُرْبَ قيام الساعة إلى المحشر، فتبيتُ معهم حيث باتوا ، وتقيل معهم حيث قالوا، فتدور الدنيا كلها، وتطير ولها دويٌّ كدوي الرعد القاصف، وحكمتها الامتحان والاختبار، فمن عَلِمَ أنها مرسلة من عند الله وانساق معها سلم منها، ومن لم يكن كذلك أحرقته وأكلته، وبعد سوقها لهم إلى المحشر يموتون بالنفخة الأولى بعد مدة، وهذان النوعان في الدنيا، فأنواع الحشر أربعة وجعلها الشيخ محيي الدين كثيرة جدا، وعدَّ منها حشر الذرِّ يوم الدَّرِّ يوم ﴿أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] وغير ذلك.
And al-Hashr (the Gathering) is an expression for driving them all to the Mawqif (the Standing Place), which is the place where they stand in the land of Jerusalem, the changed one, in which Allah was not disobeyed, for the separation of judgment among them. There is no difference in that between those who are recompensed—they are humans, jinn, and angels—and those who are not recompensed, like beasts and wild animals, according to what the verifiers have held and al-Nawawi has declared sound. A group held that only those who are recompensed will be gathered, and this is apparent in 'al-Kamil'. As for the miscarriage—the one not yet six months old—if it is expelled after the blowing of the spirit into it, it is returned with its spirit, and when it enters Paradise it becomes like its inhabitants in beauty and height. If it is expelled before the blowing of the spirit into it, it is like other bodies without a spirit, like stone; it will be gathered then become dust. And the first one from whom the earth will split open is our Prophet (peace be upon him), so he is the first to be resurrected and the first to arrive at the Gathering Place, just as he is the first to enter Paradise. After him is our master Nuh (peace be upon him), as has come in reports, but it has also come that after him is Abu Bakr, and it was interpreted as being after the prophets. And the ranks of people in the Gathering vary: among them is the rider—he is the pious; among them is the walker on his feet—he is the one of little deed; among them is the walker on his face—he is the disbeliever. And this Gathering mentioned here is one of the types of Gathering in terms of itself. Its second type: the directing of people from the Standing Place to Paradise or the Fire, and these two types are in the Hereafter. Its third type: the expulsion of the Jews from the Arabian Peninsula to Syria, and it is mentioned in His statement, the Exalted: 'It is He who expelled those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering' (Al-Hashr: 2). Its fourth type: the driving of the Fire that comes out from the land of Aden in Yemen for the disbelievers and others, from every living being near the establishment of the Hour, to the Gathering Place, so it spends the night with them wherever they spend the night, and takes a midday rest with them wherever they take a midday rest. It traverses the entire world, flying, and it has a buzzing like the buzzing of a thunderbolt. Its wisdom is trial and test: whoever knows that it is sent from Allah and goes along with it is safe from it, and whoever is not so, it burns him and consumes him. After it drives them to the Gathering Place, they die with the first blast after a period. These two types are in this world. So the types of Gathering are four, and Shaykh Muhyi al-Din made them very many, and he counted among them the Gathering of the atoms on the Day of the Covenant, the day of 'Am I not your Lord?' (Al-A'raf: 172), and others.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage defines al-Hashr (the Gathering) and enumerates its types. It begins by stating that al-Hashr is the driving of all creatures to the Mawqif (the Standing Place) on the Day of Judgment, specifying that this place is in a changed land of Jerusalem where sin was absent, for final judgment. The author notes that there is no distinction in being gathered between those who are recompensed (humans, jinn, angels) and those not (animals), as held by verified scholars and al-Nawawi, though a minority limit gathering to recompensed beings. A detailed discussion follows on the miscarriage (al-siqṭ): if it had a soul (after four months), it is resurrected with soul and enters Paradise beautiful and tall; if not, it is like a stone, gathered then turned to dust. The author then states that the Prophet Muhammad is the first to be resurrected and to enter Paradise, followed by Nuh, though a report places Abu Bakr after the prophets. Next, the varying ranks of people on the Day of Resurrection are described: riders (the pious), walkers (those of little deed), and those crawling on faces (disbelievers). The passage then clarifies that the gathering described so far is one type (gathering to the Stand). It lists four types in total: (1) gathering to the Stand (in the Hereafter), (2) directing people from the Stand to Paradise or Fire (Hereafter), (3) expulsion of Jews from Arabia to Syria (worldly), and (4) the driving of a fire from Yemen that gathers people near the Hour, testing those who resist (worldly). The author notes that Muhyi al-Din expanded these types to include the gathering of atoms at the primordial covenant. The commentary proceeds in the author's order, explaining each element without external addition.

Key Terms
الحشر
الموقف
السقط
نفخ الروح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only human beings are gathered on the Day of Judgment; animals cease to exist.
Correction: The text states that all creatures, including beasts and wild animals, are gathered to the Mawqif, though they are not recompensed for deeds.

Checkpoint
According to the majority view cited in the passage, which of the following are gathered on the Day of Resurrection?
A) Only humans
B) Only humans, jinn, and angels
C) All creatures including animals
D) Only those who are recompensed

Key Takeaway
Al-Hashr encompasses all of creation, highlighting the comprehensive nature of the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You will be gathered with every being you have encountered. Does the way you treat animals, nature, and even the unborn reflect the seriousness of that day? What is one concrete change you will make today because of this truth?
?
If a miscarriage with a soul is resurrected perfect in beauty and height, what does that reveal about Allah's mercy and justice? How does this knowledge affect your view of life's fragility and the value of every soul?
?
The Standing Place is a location where Allah was never disobeyed. Does your heart yearn for that place? What are you doing right now to ensure that your standing before Allah will be one of hope rather than regret?

Order of Resurrection and Ranks on the Day of Gathering
States the order of resurrection and ranks of people in the Gathering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Prophet Muhammad is the first to be resurrected and the first to enter the Gathering Place, followed by other prophets, and that people are gathered in three ranks based on their deeds.

Core Idea
The Prophet leads the resurrection, and people's ranks reflect their piety.

After defining al-Hashr, the commentator turns to the sequence of resurrection and the varying states of people on that day. He emphasizes the superiority of the Prophet and then categorizes the gathered into three distinct groups, each corresponding to their spiritual state in this world.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first resurrected
The text states that our Prophet is the first from whom the earth splits open. Find the phrase and note that he is also the first to enter Paradise.
2
Note the order after the Prophet
Nuh is mentioned next, but there is also a report about Abu Bakr. Understand that Abu Bakr is after the prophets.
This shows the high rank of the Prophet and the prophets, then the companions.
3
Understand the three ranks
The passage lists: rider (pious), walker on feet (little deed), and walker on face (disbeliever). Reflect on what these symbolic states imply.
4
Connect ranks to deeds
Ask yourself: how does one become a 'rider' in the gathering? The text links it to piety (متقي). This teaches that our actions now affect our state then.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحشر عبارة عن سوقهم جميعاً إلى الموقف، وهو الموضع الذي يقفون فيه من أرض القدس المبدَّلة التي لم يُعصَ الله عليها لفصل القضاء بينهم، ولا فرق في ذلك بين من يُجازى وهم الإنس والجن والملك، وبين من لا يُجازى كالبهائم والوحوش على ما ذهب إليه المحققون، وصحَّحه النووي، وذهبت طائفة إلى أنه لا يُحشر إلا من يُجازى، وهذا ظاهر في الكامل، وأما السِّقْط وهو الذي لم تتم له ستة أشهر؛ فإن أُلقي بعد نفخ الروح فيه أعيد بروحه، ويصير عند دخوله الجنة كأهلها في الجمال والطول، وإن أُلقي قبل نفخ الروح فيه كان كسائر الأجسام التي لا روح فيها كالحجر، فيُحشر ثم يصير تراباً . وأوَّلُ مَنْ تنشقُ عنه الأرض نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم، فهو أوَّلُ مَنْ يبعث وأوَّلُ وارد المحشر، كما أنه أوَّلُ داخل الجنة، وبعده سيدنا نوح عليه السلام، كما ورد لكن ورد أن بعده أبا بكر، وحُمل على أنه بعد الأنبياء. ومراتب الناس في الحشر متفاوتة؛ فمنهم الراكب وهو المتقي، ومنهم الماشي على رجليه؛ وهو قليل العمل، ومنهم الماشي على وجهه؛ وهو الكافر وهذا الحشر المذكور هنا هو أحد أنواع الحشر من حيث هو . ثانيها : صرفُ الناس من الموقف إلى الجنة أو النار، وهذان النوعان في الآخرة. ثالثها : إخراجُ اليهود من جزيرة العرب إلى الشام وهو المذكور في قوله تعالى : ﴿هُوَ الَّذِى أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَبِ مِن دِيَارِهِم لِأَوَّلِ الحَشْرِ﴾ [الحشر: ٢]. رابعها : سَوْقُ النار التي تخرجُ من أرض عدن باليمن للكفار وغيرهم من كلِّ حَيٍّ قُرْبَ قيام الساعة إلى المحشر، فتبيتُ معهم حيث باتوا ، وتقيل معهم حيث قالوا، فتدور الدنيا كلها، وتطير ولها دويٌّ كدوي الرعد القاصف، وحكمتها الامتحان والاختبار، فمن عَلِمَ أنها مرسلة من عند الله وانساق معها سلم منها، ومن لم يكن كذلك أحرقته وأكلته، وبعد سوقها لهم إلى المحشر يموتون بالنفخة الأولى بعد مدة، وهذان النوعان في الدنيا، فأنواع الحشر أربعة وجعلها الشيخ محيي الدين كثيرة جدا، وعدَّ منها حشر الذرِّ يوم الدَّرِّ يوم ﴿أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] وغير ذلك.
And al-Hashr (the Gathering) is an expression for driving them all to the Mawqif (the Standing Place), which is the place where they stand in the land of Jerusalem, the changed one, in which Allah was not disobeyed, for the separation of judgment among them. There is no difference in that between those who are recompensed—they are humans, jinn, and angels—and those who are not recompensed, like beasts and wild animals, according to what the verifiers have held and al-Nawawi has declared sound. A group held that only those who are recompensed will be gathered, and this is apparent in 'al-Kamil'. As for the miscarriage—the one not yet six months old—if it is expelled after the blowing of the spirit into it, it is returned with its spirit, and when it enters Paradise it becomes like its inhabitants in beauty and height. If it is expelled before the blowing of the spirit into it, it is like other bodies without a spirit, like stone; it will be gathered then become dust. And the first one from whom the earth will split open is our Prophet (peace be upon him), so he is the first to be resurrected and the first to arrive at the Gathering Place, just as he is the first to enter Paradise. After him is our master Nuh (peace be upon him), as has come in reports, but it has also come that after him is Abu Bakr, and it was interpreted as being after the prophets. And the ranks of people in the Gathering vary: among them is the rider—he is the pious; among them is the walker on his feet—he is the one of little deed; among them is the walker on his face—he is the disbeliever. And this Gathering mentioned here is one of the types of Gathering in terms of itself. Its second type: the directing of people from the Standing Place to Paradise or the Fire, and these two types are in the Hereafter. Its third type: the expulsion of the Jews from the Arabian Peninsula to Syria, and it is mentioned in His statement, the Exalted: 'It is He who expelled those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering' (Al-Hashr: 2). Its fourth type: the driving of the Fire that comes out from the land of Aden in Yemen for the disbelievers and others, from every living being near the establishment of the Hour, to the Gathering Place, so it spends the night with them wherever they spend the night, and takes a midday rest with them wherever they take a midday rest. It traverses the entire world, flying, and it has a buzzing like the buzzing of a thunderbolt. Its wisdom is trial and test: whoever knows that it is sent from Allah and goes along with it is safe from it, and whoever is not so, it burns him and consumes him. After it drives them to the Gathering Place, they die with the first blast after a period. These two types are in this world. So the types of Gathering are four, and Shaykh Muhyi al-Din made them very many, and he counted among them the Gathering of the atoms on the Day of the Covenant, the day of 'Am I not your Lord?' (Al-A'raf: 172), and others.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage defines al-Hashr (the Gathering) and enumerates its types. It begins by stating that al-Hashr is the driving of all creatures to the Mawqif (the Standing Place) on the Day of Judgment, specifying that this place is in a changed land of Jerusalem where sin was absent, for final judgment. The author notes that there is no distinction in being gathered between those who are recompensed (humans, jinn, angels) and those not (animals), as held by verified scholars and al-Nawawi, though a minority limit gathering to recompensed beings. A detailed discussion follows on the miscarriage (al-siqṭ): if it had a soul (after four months), it is resurrected with soul and enters Paradise beautiful and tall; if not, it is like a stone, gathered then turned to dust. The author then states that the Prophet Muhammad is the first to be resurrected and to enter Paradise, followed by Nuh, though a report places Abu Bakr after the prophets. Next, the varying ranks of people on the Day of Resurrection are described: riders (the pious), walkers (those of little deed), and those crawling on faces (disbelievers). The passage then clarifies that the gathering described so far is one type (gathering to the Stand). It lists four types in total: (1) gathering to the Stand (in the Hereafter), (2) directing people from the Stand to Paradise or Fire (Hereafter), (3) expulsion of Jews from Arabia to Syria (worldly), and (4) the driving of a fire from Yemen that gathers people near the Hour, testing those who resist (worldly). The author notes that Muhyi al-Din expanded these types to include the gathering of atoms at the primordial covenant. The commentary proceeds in the author's order, explaining each element without external addition.

Key Terms
الراكب
الماشي
المتقي
الكافر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is described as the first to be resurrected in the passage?
A) Prophet Nuh
B) Prophet Muhammad
C) Abu Bakr
D) All prophets together

Key Takeaway
The Prophet is foremost in resurrection, and each person's state in the gathering reflects their faith and deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
On the Day of Resurrection, will you be among the rider, the walker, or the one crawling on your face? Look at your deeds today—which category describes your current state, and what change must you make before that Day arrives?
?
The Prophet ﷺ is the first to be resurrected and the first to enter Paradise. If you truly love him, how does his precedence inspire you to follow his sunnah more closely, starting from this moment?
?
Abu Bakr’s rank is after the prophets. How does this knowledge challenge your own pride and remind you that true honor lies in faith and action, not worldly status? What one deed can you perfect today to raise your rank?

The Four Types of al-Hashr
Enumerates the four types of al-Hashr with details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four distinct types of al-Hashr: two occurring in the Hereafter (gathering to the Stand and directing to Paradise/Fire) and two in this world (expulsion of Jews and the driving of the Fire).

Core Idea
Al-Hashr is not a single event; it encompasses four types, two in this life and two in the next.

After describing the gathering itself, the commentator clarifies that the term 'al-Hashr' applies to multiple events. He enumerates four types, explaining that two take place in the Hereafter and two in this world. This broader understanding prevents confusion and highlights the many ways divine power assembles creation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first type
The passage previously described the gathering to the Stand. Recognize this as the first type. Note that it is a Hereafter event.
2
Understand the second type
This is the directing of people from the Stand to their final abodes: Paradise or Fire. Also in the Hereafter.
This type is sometimes called 'al-Hashr al-Thani'.
3
Learn the third type
The expulsion of the Jews from Arabia to Syria, mentioned in Surah al-Hashr. This is a worldly event.
The Quranic reference confirms this type.
4
Study the fourth type
A terrifying fire from Yemen that drives all living beings to the Gathering Place near the Hour. This fire tests people's faith.
The fire's behavior and purpose are detailed.
5
Reflect on the wisdom
Ask: why does the author list these four together? They show the comprehensive meaning of 'hashr' and tie together eschatological and historical events.

?

Belief in the Reassembly of Bodies After Death
States the obligation to believe in bodily resurrection from non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in the physical resurrection of bodies from absolute non-existence, not merely from disintegrated parts.

Core Idea
Bodily resurrection is a new creation from nothing, not a reassembly of old parts.

This lesson addresses the Islamic creed regarding the resurrection of bodies after death. The passage from Jawharat al-Tawhid affirms that bodies are returned from non-existence (ʿadam), countering the view that they are simply reassembled from scattered parts. The commentary clarifies that this belief must be held internally and expressed externally.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic heading and verse once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms: إعادة الأجسام, النشر, العدم, التفريق.
2
Understand the doctrinal distinction
Identify the two views mentioned: 'from non-existence' and 'from disintegration'. The passage affirms the former as the correct belief.
The phrase 'وقيل: عن تفريق' indicates a reported weaker opinion.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'say' (qul)
The commentary explains that 'qul' means a statement matching your belief, either mental or spoken. This underscores the integration of internal conviction and outward expression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ اعتقادِ إعادة الأجسام بأعيانها عند النشر - وقُلْ : يُعادُ الجِسْمُ بِالتَّحْقِيقِ عَنْ عَدَمٍ وقِيلَ: عَنْ تَفْرِيقِ - قوله : (وقُلْ) أي: قولاً نفسياً أو عقليا كما قاله في «كبيره»، وقال الشارح: قولاً مطابقاً لاعتقادك. انتهى
The obligation of believing in the reassembly of bodies in their very selves at the time of the Resurrection - And say: The body is truly returned from non-existence, and it is said: from disintegration - His statement: 'And say' i.e., a mental or intellectual saying as he said in his 'large [work]', and the commentator said: a saying matching your belief. End.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation to believe in the physical resurrection of bodies (iʿādat al-ajsām bi aʿyānihā) at the time of al-nashr (the spreading forth). It cites the poetic line from Jawharat al-Tawhid: 'And say: The body is truly returned from non-existence, and it is said: from disintegration.' The commentator explains that the imperative 'say' (qul) means to utter a statement that is either mental (nafsī) or intellectual (ʿaqlī), as the author stated in his larger commentary. Then the commentator adds that it means a statement in accordance with your belief. Thus the passage emphasizes that the correct doctrine is that bodies are recreated from absolute nothingness (ʿan ʿadam), not merely from scattered parts (ʿan tafrīq), and that one must affirm this belief internally and externally.

Key Terms
إعادة الأجسام
النشر
العدم
التفريق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think bodily resurrection means reassembling the same scattered particles.
Correction: The correct belief is that bodies are created anew from absolute non-existence, not merely reconstituted from disintegrated parts.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct belief about the reassembly of bodies?
A) From disintegration of parts
B) From non-existence
C) Both are equally valid
D) From nothing, but it is a metaphor

Key Takeaway
The essential point is that bodily resurrection is from absolute non-existence, affirming Allah's absolute power to create anew.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of your own death, do you truly believe that Allah will recreate your body from nothing, or do you secretly hope it's just a reassembly? How does this belief affect your actions today?
?
The verse commands you to say the correct belief. Do you even know what you believe well enough to utter it? What would you say if asked about the resurrection right now?
?
Is your faith in Allah's power to create anew strong enough to make you live without fear of losing this worldly body? Or are you attached to it as if it's the only one you'll ever have?

The Four Types of Gathering (Hash) in Islamic Eschatology
The commentator enumerates the four types of hash with details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four distinct types of al-hashr (the gathering) as classified by the commentator, including their timing, purpose, and the wisdom behind them.

Core Idea
The gathering on the Day of Judgment is only one of four types — some occur in this world.

The commentator begins by describing the varied ranks of people in the gathering, referencing a prophetic tradition. He then provides a systematic classification of four types of hash, spanning both worldly and otherworldly events. This passage clarifies that the term 'gathering' encompasses more than just the final assembly for judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the ranks of people
The opening describes three categories of people in the gathering: riders (pious), walkers (deficient in deeds), and crawlers (disbelievers). Reflect on how this sets the stage for the classification.
This is based on a hadith, though not explicitly quoted here.
2
Identify the four types of hash
The commentator lists four types. Try to list them in order: the first is the gathering from graves to the judgment place; the second is the directing to Paradise or Hell; the third is the expulsion of Jews; the fourth is the driving of the fire.
The first type is mentioned implicitly at the beginning.
3
Distinguish worldly from otherworldly types
Notice that the third and fourth types occur in this world (the expulsion and the fire), while the first two are in the Hereafter. This shows the breadth of the concept.
4
Understand the wisdom of the fire and the broader view
The fire tests believers and disbelievers: those who submit are saved, others are burned. Also note that Shaykh Muhyī al-Dīn (Ibn Arabi) considered many more types, such as the covenant of 'Am I not your Lord?'
The passage invites further study of eschatological events.

ومراتب الناس في الحشر متفاوتة؛ فمنهم الراكب وهو المتقي، ومنهم الماشي (۱) على رجليه؛ وهو قليل العمل، ومنهم الماشي على وجهه؛ وهو الكافر وهذا الحشر المذكور هنا هو أحد أنواع الحشر من حيث هو . ثانيها : صرفُ الناس من الموقف إلى الجنة أو النار، وهذان النوعان في الآخرة. ثالثها : إخراجُ اليهود من جزيرة العرب إلى الشام وهو المذكور في قوله تعالى : ﴿هُوَ الَّذِى أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَبِ مِن دِبَرِهِم لِأَوَّلِ الحَشْرِ) [الحشر: ٢]. رابعها : سَوْقُ النار التي تخرجُ من أرض عدن باليمن للكفار وغيرهم من كلِّ حَيٍّ قُرْبَ قيام الساعة إلى المحشر، فتبيتُ معهم حيث باتوا ، وتقيل معهم حيث قالوا، فتدور الدنيا كلها، وتطير ولها دويٌّ كدوي الرعد القاصف (۲)، وحكمتها الامتحان والاختبار، فمن عَلِمَ أنها مرسلة من عند الله وانساق معها سلم منها، ومن لم يكن كذلك أحرقته وأكلته، وبعد سوقها لهم إلى المحشر يموتون بالنفخة الأولى بعد مدة (۳)، وهذان النوعان في الدنيا، فأنواع الحشر أربعة وجعلها الشيخ محيي الدين كثيرة جدا، وعدَّ منها حشر الذرِّ يوم الدَّرِّ يوم ﴿أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] وغير ذلك، انظر: «اليواقيت للشعراني
The ranks of people in the gathering (al-ḥashr) are varied: among them is the rider, who is the pious; among them is the walker on his feet, who is little in deeds; among them is the walker on his face, who is the disbeliever. And this gathering mentioned here is one type of gathering in terms of itself. The second type: the directing of people from the standing-place to Paradise or Hell, and these two types are in the Hereafter. The third type: the expulsion of the Jews from the Arabian Peninsula to Syria, and it is mentioned in His statement, the Exalted: 'He it is who expelled those who disbelieved among the People of the Scripture from their homes at the first gathering' [al-Hashr 59:2]. The fourth type: the driving of the fire that emerges from the land of Aden in Yemen for the disbelievers and others of every living being near the establishment of the Hour to the gathering-place; then it spends the night with them wherever they spend the night, and takes a midday rest with them wherever they take a midday rest, so it travels the whole world, and it flies while it has a buzzing like the buzzing of a crashing thunderbolt. Its wisdom is trial and testing: whoever knows that it is sent from God and follows along with it is saved from it, and whoever is not like that, it burns and consumes him. And after its driving them to the gathering-place, they die with the first blast after a period. And these two types are in this world. So the types of gathering are four, but Shaykh Muhyī al-Dīn made them very numerous, and included among them the gathering of the atoms on the day of the covenant, the day of 'Am I not your Lord?' [al-A'raf 7:172] and others. See: 'al-Yawāqīt' by al-Sha'rānī.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the different types of al-ḥashr (the gathering) in Islamic eschatology. The commentator begins by noting that people's ranks in the gathering are varied, based on a hadith: some are riders (the pious), some walk (the deficient in deeds), and some crawl on their faces (the disbelievers). This specific gathering is one type. Then he enumerates four types in order. The first type (mentioned first implicitly) is the gathering of people from their graves to the place of judgment. The second type is the directing of people from the standing-place to Paradise or Hell, which occurs in the afterlife. The third type is the historical expulsion of Jews from Arabia to Syria, mentioned in Qur'an 59:2, which is a worldly event. The fourth type is the driving of a fire that appears from Yemen before the Hour, which drives all living beings to the gathering-place, testing them: those who submit are saved, others are burned. This fire then causes death with the first trumpet blast after a period. The commentator concludes that types of hash are four, but notes that Shaykh Muhyī al-Dīn (Ibn Arabi) considered many more, including the pre-eternal covenant. The passage provides a comprehensive doctrinal classification.

Correction: The passage shows that hash includes multiple types: two in this world (expulsion of Jews and the fire) and two in the Hereafter (gathering from graves and directing to Paradise/Hell).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The expulsion of the Jews was a 'gathering' that fulfilled a divine decree. When you see world events like wars or displacements, do you see them as random chaos or as part of Allah's planned gatherings? How would your life change if you truly believed every event is a divine gathering with purpose?

The Exact Restoration of the Body in Resurrection
Commentator explains the proof and two views on resurrection of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the orthodox Sunni doctrine of bodily resurrection: that the exact same body is restored from non-existence, and why this is necessary for justice in reward and punishment.

Core Idea
The resurrected body is the very same, not a copy—otherwise reward or punishment would go to a different person.

The resurrection of bodies is a core article of faith, but what exactly is restored? In this passage, the commentator explains that the body is brought back in its very self, not a replica. Two views are discussed: restoration from complete non-existence (except the tailbone) and from disintegration. The correct view affirms the former, ensuring that the same person who acted is judged.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the full argument.
Notice the structure: a claim, a proof, and a comparison of two views.
2
Identify the key claim: exact restoration
The passage states that the body is restored 'bi-ʿaynihi' (in its very self), not a likeness. Understand why this matters for personal identity.
The consensus argument is that a copy would make the rewarded or punished person different from the one who acted.
3
Distinguish the two views
The first view: restoration from non-existence (after complete annihilation except the tailbone). The second view: restoration from disintegration (reassembly of scattered parts). Note which is correct and why.
The author presents the first view definitively, the second with a sign of weakness.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: How does this doctrine uphold divine justice? The commentary shows that personal identity must persist for just recompense.
This connects to the broader theme of samʿiyyāt (hear-and-believe matters).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ اعتقادِ إعادة الأجسام بأعيانها عند النشر
۹۷ - وقُلْ : يُعادُ الجِسْمُ بِالتَّحْقِيقِ عَنْ عَدَمٍ وقِيلَ: عَنْ تَفْرِيقِ
قوله : (وقُلْ) أي: قولاً نفسياً أو عقليا كما قاله في كبيره»، وقال الشارح: قولاً مطابقاً لاعتقادك. انتهى
ويغني عنه ما تقدَّم، فالمراد بالقول هنا : الاعتقاد.
وقوله : (يُعادُ الجِسْمُ ) أي : يعيده الله تعالى بعينه فالجسم الثاني المعاد هو ، الجسم الأول بعينه لا مثلُه ، وإلا لزم أن المثابَ أو المعذب غيرُ الجسم الذي أطاع أو عصى، وهو باطل بالإجماع. وقوله : (بِالتَّحْقِيقِ) متعلق بـ (قل) أو بـ (يعاد)؛ فالمعنى على الأول: قولاً مُلتبساً بالتحقيق الذي هو إثبات الحكم بالدليل في أشهر إطلاقاته، ففيه إشارة إلى أن هذا القول عن دليل لا من قبيل الرأي. والمعنى على الثاني: إعادة مُلْتَبِسة بالتحقيق ؛ أي: إعادةً مُحقَّقَةٌ لا مشكوك فيها .
وقوله : (عَنْ عَدَمٍ)؛ أي: بعد عدم ؛ فـ (عن) بمعنى (بعد)، وقال الشارح: إعادة ناشئة عن عدم ؛ لكن لا معنى لكون الإعادة ناشئة عن العدم، فيصير الجسم معدوماً بالكلية إلا عجب الذنب، ثم يعيده الله تعالى كما أوجده أولاً، قال تعالى: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تعودُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٩] .
وقوله : (وقيلَ : عَنْ تَفْرِيْقِ)؛ أي: بعد تفريق، فـ (عن) بمعنى (بعد) كما تقدَّم، فعلى القول الأول يُذهب الله العين والأثر جميعاً، ثم يعيد الجسم كما كان، وعلى القول الثاني يُفرِّقُ الله أجزاء الجسم بحيث لا يبقى فيه جوهران فردان على الاتصال، والصحيح القول الأول، ولذا قدَّمه المصنّف جازماً به، وحكى مُقابله بصيغة التمريض.
The obligation of believing in the restoration of bodies in their very selves at the time of resurrection. 97 - And say: The body is restored with certainty from non-existence, and it is said: from disintegration. His statement: (And say) i.e., a mental or intellectual statement as he said in his 'Kabīr', and the commentator said: a statement in accordance with your belief. End. What has preceded suffices for it, so the intended meaning of 'statement' here is belief. And His statement: (The body is restored) i.e., God the Exalted restores it in its very self, so the second body that is restored is the first body in its very self, not a likeness of it; otherwise it would necessarily follow that the rewarded or punished one is not the body that obeyed or disobeyed, and that is invalid by consensus. And His statement: (with certainty) is attached to (say) or to (is restored); so the meaning according to the first is: a statement imbued with certainty, which is the establishment of the ruling by evidence in its most famous usages, and it contains an indication that this statement is from evidence, not from the category of opinion. And the meaning according to the second is: a restoration imbued with certainty; i.e., a certain restoration, not doubtful. And His statement: (from non-existence) i.e., after non-existence; so (from) means (after). And the commentator said: a restoration arising from non-existence; but there is no meaning to the restoration arising from non-existence, so the body becomes completely non-existent except the tailbone, then God the Exalted restores it as He first originated it. He said, the Exalted: 'As He began you, you shall return' [al-A'raf 7:29]. And His statement: (and it is said: from disintegration) i.e., after disintegration, so (from) means (after) as before. So according to the first view, God makes the essence and trace disappear altogether, then restores the body as it was. And according to the second view, God disintegrates the parts of the body so that there remain no two individual atoms in contact. And the correct view is the first, and therefore the author presented it with certainty, and narrated its opposite in the form of indication of weakness.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the resurrection of bodies (iʿādat al-ajsām). It begins by stating the obligation to believe that bodies are restored in their very selves (bi-aʿyānihā). Then it explains the poetic line 97 from Jawharat al-Tawḥīd: 'And say: The body is restored with certainty from non-existence, and it is said: from disintegration.' The commentary then breaks down each part. The word 'qul' (say) means a statement that is mental or intellectual, i.e., belief. The phrase 'yurādu al-jismu' (the body is restored) means God restores the exact same body, not a copy; if it were a copy, the rewarded or punished person would not be the same as the one who obeyed or disobeyed, which is invalid by consensus. The term 'bi-l-taḥqīq' (with certainty) can be attached either to 'qul' (meaning a statement based on proof, not opinion) or to 'yurādu' (meaning the restoration itself is certain). The phrase 'an ʿadam' (from non-existence) means after non-existence; the commentator clarifies that the body becomes completely non-existent except for the tailbone (ʿajb al-dhanab), then God restores it as He first created it, quoting Qur'an 7:29. The alternative view 'an tafrīq' (from disintegration) means after disintegration, i.e., the body's parts are separated but not annihilated, then reassembled. The correct view is the first (restoration from non-existence), and the author (al-Laqqānī) presented it definitively, while mentioning the second view weakly (ṣīghat al-tamrīḍ). The passage thus affirms the orthodox Sunni belief in the resurrection of the exact same body from nothing, against those who say it is merely a reassembly of scattered parts.
