عجب الذنب
تفريق
تحقيق
إعادة من عدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the resurrected body is a new creation similar to the original (mithl), not the exact same body.
Correction: The passage explicitly refutes this, stating that the second body is the first body itself (bi-ʿaynihi), not a likeness. Otherwise, the person rewarded or punished would not be the one who acted, which is invalid by consensus.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the correct view regarding the restoration of the body?
A) It is restored from complete non-existence except the tailbone.
B) It is restored from the disintegration of its parts.
C) It is a new creation similar to the original.
D) The body is not restored at all.

Key Takeaway
The orthodox belief is that the exact same body is restored from non-existence, with the tailbone as a seed, ensuring personal identity for just reward and punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your very same body—every cell, every atom—will be restored to face perfect justice, how does that change the weight you give to your physical actions today? Will you still act as if some deeds are 'just of the body' and therefore less important?
?
You know that after death your body will be completely annihilated except for a tiny seed. Does that thought make you cling to this world or release it? What would it take for you to live today as if you truly believe that only what remains with the tailbone matters?
?
The passage argues that if the resurrected body were a copy, the rewarder would not be you. Are you living as if the person who will face Allah is a different 'you'—or are you preparing that very self for what is to come? What concrete step will you take today to align your body’s obedience with its eternal identity?

The Two Views on Bodily Resurrection
Commentary explains the meaning of bodily resurrection and the two views on its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two views on how the body is returned on the Day of Resurrection: from complete non-existence (except the coccyx) or from dispersal of parts, and why the first view is considered correct.

Core Idea
Bodily resurrection returns the same body—not its likeness—either from non-existence or from dispersion.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid clarifies a crucial aspect of Islamic eschatology: the nature of the resurrected body. The author first affirms that the body that is returned is identical to the one in this life, then explains two interpretations of how the body is recreated. Understanding these views helps us grasp the divine power and justice in rewarding or punishing the very same person who acted.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of 'the body is returned'
Read the initial part of the passage that defines bodily resurrection: it is the same body, not a likeness, based on consensus.
This establishes the identity of the person rewarded or punished.
2
Grasp the two interpretations of 'from non-existence' and 'from dispersal'
Read the later part explaining both views. Note the role of the coccyx in the first view and the notion of total dispersal in the second.
3
Recognize the correct view
Observe that the author presents the first view decisively and mentions the second in a weak form (ṣīghat al-tamrīḍ).
This indicates the preferred position within the tradition.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (يُعادُ الجِسْمُ ) أي : يعيده الله تعالى بعينه فالجسم الثاني المعاد هو ، الجسم الأول بعينه لا مثلُه ، وإلا لزم أن المثابَ أو المعذب غيرُ الجسم الذي أطاع أو عصى، وهو باطل بالإجماع. وقوله : (بِالتَّحْقِيقِ) متعلق بـ (قل) أو بـ (يعاد)؛ فالمعنى على الأول: قولاً مُلتبساً بالتحقيق الذي هو إثبات الحكم بالدليل في أشهر إطلاقاته، ففيه إشارة إلى أن هذا القول عن دليل لا من قبيل الرأي. والمعنى على الثاني: إعادة مُلْتَبِسة بالتحقيق ؛ أي: إعادةً مُحقَّقَةٌ لا مشكوكاً فيها . وقوله : (عَنْ عَدَمٍ)؛ أي: بعد عدم ؛ فـ (عن) بمعنى (بعد)، وقال الشارح: إعادة ناشئة عن عدم ؛ لكن لا معنى لكون الإعادة ناشئة عن العدم، فيصير الجسم معدوماً بالكلية إلا عجب الذنب، ثم يعيده الله تعالى كما أوجده أولاً، قال تعالى: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تَعُودُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٩] . وقوله : (وقيلَ : عَنْ تَفْرِيْقِ ) أي: بعد تفريق، فـ (عن) بمعنى (بعد) كما تقدَّم، فعلى القول الأول يُذهب الله العين والأثر جميعاً، ثم يعيد الجسم كما كان، وعلى القول الثاني يُفرِّقُ الله أجزاء الجسم بحيث لا يبقى فيه جوهران فردان على الاتصال، والصحيح القول الأول، ولذا قدَّمه المصنّف جازماً به، وحكى مُقابله بصيغة التمريض.
And His statement: (The body is returned) meaning: Allah the Exalted returns the same body, so the second body that is returned is the very first body, not its likeness; otherwise it would necessitate that the rewarded or punished one is other than the body that obeyed or disobeyed, and that is invalid by consensus. And His statement: (with certainty [bi-l-tahqīq]) is attached to (say) or to (is returned); so the meaning according to the first: a speech mixed with certainty, which is establishing the ruling by evidence in its most famous usages, so it contains an indication that this statement is based on evidence, not of the type of opinion. And the meaning according to the second: a return mixed with certainty, i.e., a verified return, not doubtful. And His statement: (from non-existence ['an 'adam]) i.e., after non-existence; so ('an) is in the sense of (after). The commentator said: a return arising from non-existence; but there is no meaning for the return arising from non-existence, so the body becomes entirely non-existent except for the tailbone (coccyx), then Allah the Exalted returns it as He first created it. He said the Exalted: {As He began you, you will return} [al-A'raf 7:29]. And His statement: (and it was said: from dispersal) i.e., after dispersal, so ('an) is in the sense of (after) as before. Thus according to the first view, Allah removes both the essence and the trace entirely, then returns the body as it was; and according to the second view, Allah disperses the parts of the body such that no two individual atoms remain in contact. The correct view is the first, and therefore the author [Ibn 'Ata'illah?] presented it decisively, and mentioned its opposite in a weak form.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the line of the poem about bodily resurrection. It first defines what is meant by 'the return' of the body: it is the return of the very same body, not a similar one. This is argued by consensus, because if it were a different body, the person rewarded or punished would not be the same person who did the deeds. Then it explains two phrases in the poem: 'with certainty' is attached either to the speech or to the return, giving two possible nuances. After that, it explains two interpretations of the phrase 'from non-existence' and 'from dispersal'. The first interpretation: the body is reduced to complete non-existence except for the coccyx bone (reported in hadith), then Allah recreates it. The second interpretation: the body is completely disintegrated so that no two atoms are joined, then Allah reassembles it. The correct view, which the author presents decisively, is the first (from non-existence). The author then mentions the opposite view in a weak form (ṣīghat al-tamrīḍ).

D) Resurrection in Paradise vs. resurrection in Hell

Key Takeaway
The body that is resurrected is the same body that lived, returned either from complete non-existence (except the coccyx) or from total dispersal; the first view is correct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The correct view is that Allah annihilates the body entirely and then re-creates it from nothing—except the coccyx. How does this total dependence on Allah's creative power change your understanding of your own existence? Will you humble yourself before Him today, acknowledging that you are re-created every moment?

Restriction of the Resurrection Disagreement to Non-Prophets
Clarification of the restriction of the resurrection disagreement to non-prophets and the list of exempted individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the disagreement about bodily resurrection (non-existence vs dispersal) applies only to ordinary people, not to prophets and certain honored ones whose bodies are preserved by divine decree.

Core Idea
The resurrection disagreement is not universal — prophets and the righteous are exempt.

In the previous lines, the author presented two views on how the body returns: from pure non-existence or pure dispersal. But that disagreement is not absolute. This passage clarifies that the disagreement applies only to ordinary humans; prophets and specially honored individuals are excluded because their bodies do not decay. This lesson explains the terms and the list of those exempted.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'pure' states
Read how the commentary explains that non-existence and dispersal are 'pure' — absolute without any admixture. This refutes a common misconception about conventional non-existence or dispersal.
The purity ensures the views are truly distinct.
2
Recognize the restriction
Note that the disagreement is restricted to non-prophets. The prophets' bodies are not consumed by the earth by consensus.
3
Identify the honored ones
Go through the list: martyrs, muezzins, acting scholars, Quran bearers, and others. Understand that the ruling is based on revelation (tawqīfiyya).
The list is not exhaustive; it includes all explicitly named by the Lawgiver.

Source Text

٩٩ - مَحْضَيْنِ لَكِنْ ذَا الخِلافُ خُمَّا بالأنْبِيا وَمَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ نُمَّا
وقوله : (مَحْضَيْنِ) صفة (عدم وتفريق ) ؛ أي: عدم محض وتفريق محض، فمعنى محضية العدم : خلوصه من شائبة الوجود لجزء ما ومعنى محضية التفريق : خلوصه من شائبة الاتصال في أجزائه .
ودفع المصنف بذلك توهم أن المراد بالعدم عند القائلين به العدم العرفي الصادق بوجود جزء ما من أجزائه وأن المراد بالتفريق عند القائلين به التفريق العرفي الصادق باتصال بعض أجزائه .
قوله : لَكِنْ ذَا الخِلافُ خُمَّا بألف الإطلاق، وهذا استدراك على إطلاق الخلاف السابق ؛ وفي التعبير بالتخصيص تَسَمُّحْ؛ لأنَّ التخصيص من عوارض العموم، والتقييد من عوارض الإطلاق؛ فالمعنى : لكن هذا الخلاف قيد العلماء إطلاقه.
وقوله : (بالأنبيا)؛ أي: بسبب إخراج الأنبياء منه؛ فإن الأرض لا تأكل أجسامهم ولا تُبلي أبدانهم اتفاقاً (۱) ، فالخلاف في غيرهم وغير من أُلحق بهم ممن سيأتي.
وقوله : ( ومَنْ عَلَيهِمْ نُصَّا بألف الإطلاق؛ أي: ومن نصَّ الشارع على أن الأرض لا تأكلُ أجسامهم كالشهداء، والمراد بهم : كلُّ مقتول على الحقِّ، ولو لم يكن من شهداء المعركة، وكالمؤذنين احتساباً ؛ أي: ادخاراً لثواب ذلك عند الله تعالى لا لأُجرة، وكالعلماء العاملين وحملة القرآن الملازمين لتلاوته، العاملين (۲) بما فيه، المعظمين له بضبط لسانهم وطهارتهم وآدابهم (۳) ، إلى غير ذلك مما نُقل عن الشارع، فإن المسألة توقيفية.
99 - Two pure [states], but this disagreement was restricted to the prophets and those who were explicitly named. And His statement: (two pure [maḥḍayn]) is an attribute of (non-existence and dispersal); i.e., pure non-existence and pure dispersal. So the meaning of the purity of non-existence is its being free from any admixture of existence for any part, and the meaning of the purity of dispersal is its being free from any admixture of connection in its parts. And with that, the author repelled the misconception that the intended meaning of non-existence according to its proponents is conventional non-existence, which applies with the existence of some part of it, and that the intended meaning of dispersal according to its proponents is conventional dispersal, which applies with the connection of some of its parts. His statement: (but this disagreement was restricted) with the alif of absolute form (i.e., for the rhyme). And this is a correction of the absolute nature of the previous disagreement. In the expression 'restriction' there is metaphor, because restriction is an accident of generality, and limitation is an accident of absoluteness. So the meaning: but the scholars limited this disagreement from its absolute form. And His statement: (to the prophets) i.e., because of the exclusion of the prophets from it; for the earth does not consume their bodies and does not decay their frames by agreement, so the disagreement is about others and those who are joined to them among those who will come. And His statement: (and those who were explicitly named) with the alif of absolute form; i.e., and those for whom the Lawgiver explicitly stated that the earth does not consume their bodies, such as the martyrs, and by them is meant: everyone killed for the truth, even if they are not from the battlefield martyrs; also the muezzins who call the call to prayer seeking reward (iḥtisāban), i.e., storing up reward for that from Allah, not for a fee; and the knowledgeable who act upon their knowledge, and the bearers of the Qur'an who are constant in reciting it, acting upon it, and venerating it by controlling their tongues and their purification and etiquette; and others besides that which has been transmitted from the Lawgiver, for the matter is based on revelation (tawqīfiyya).
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage explains the poet's line 'Two pure, but this disagreement was restricted to the prophets and those upon whom it was named.' First, it explains that the two views (non-existence and dispersal) are 'pure' — meaning the non-existence is absolute with no remnant of any part, and the dispersal is absolute with no connection between any two atoms. This refutes the misconception that these terms refer only to conventional non-existence or dispersal, which could still allow some existence or connection. Then it corrects the impression that the disagreement applies to all humans: it is actually restricted because prophets and certain others are exempted. The prophets' bodies are not consumed by the earth by consensus. Then it lists others explicitly mentioned by the Lawgiver: martyrs (all killed for the truth), muezzins who call without fee, knowledgeable scholars who act, and carriers of the Qur'an who are constant in recitation and practice. The ruling is based on revelation (tawqīfiyya) — meaning it is known from transmitted texts, not reason.

حملة القرآن

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the disagreement about bodily resurrection applies to all humans, including prophets and saints.
Correction: The passage clarifies that it applies only to ordinary people; prophets and those honored by Allah are exempt because their bodies do not decay.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, who are excluded from the disagreement about whether the body returns from non-existence or dispersal?
A) Prophets only
B) Prophets and martyrs only
C) Prophets, martyrs, muezzins, and other specially honored persons
D) Ordinary believers

Key Takeaway
The resurrection disagreement is restricted to ordinary humans; prophets and those explicitly honored by Allah are exempt, their bodies preserved from decay by divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says the matter is tawqīfiyya—based solely on revelation. In which area of your life do you struggle to submit to divine texts because they defy your reasoning? Will you surrender that area to Allah today?
?
The muezzins are praised for calling without fee. Examine your worship: is there any act you do seeking worldly recognition or reward? Will you purify your intention for Allah alone starting now?

The Disagreement on Bodily Decay Restricted to Non-Prophets
Al-Laqani defines 'two pure ones' and restricts the disagreement to non-prophets and those like them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the disagreement about whether the body becomes pure non-existence or pure separation after death applies only to non-prophets and those not explicitly exempted by revelation.

Core Idea
The debate over bodily decay excludes prophets by consensus.

In this passage, al-Laqani clarifies a key point in the discussion about the fate of the body after death. He first defines the terms 'pure non-existence' and 'pure separation' to avoid ambiguity, then explains that the disagreement between proponents of these views is actually limited to non-prophets. He further expands the exemption to include other groups based on explicit scriptural evidence, emphasizing that the matter is determined by revelation, not reason.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definitions
Read the definitions of 'pure non-existence' (خلوصه من شائبة الوجود لجزء ما) and 'pure separation' (خلوصه من شائبة الاتصال في أجزائه). Notice that both describe a state free from any admixture.
These are technical terms specific to this theological discussion.
2
Recognize the misconception
The author rebuts a potential misunderstanding: that 'non-existence' might mean conventional non-existence (العدم العرفي), which allows some part to exist, and similarly for separation. The terms are to be understood absolutely.
This shows the importance of precise language in theology.
3
Note the restriction to non-prophets
The poem states that the disagreement is 'specified by the prophets' (بالأنبيا). Al-Laqani explains that this means the disagreement applies to others, because prophets' bodies are never consumed by the earth—by consensus.
This restriction is a key doctrinal point.
4
Identify other exempt groups
The passage lists those joined to the prophets: martyrs, muezzins seeking reward, scholars, and Qur'an reciters who act accordingly. These are based on textual evidence (توقيفية).
The matter is ultimately known from revelation, not reason.

وقوله : (مَحْضَيْنِ) صفة (عدم وتفريق )؛ أي: عدم محض وتفريق محض، فمعنى محضية العدم : خلوصه من شائبة الوجود لجزء ما ومعنى محضية التفريق : خلوصه من شائبة الاتصال في أجزائه . دفع المصنف بذلك توهم أن المراد بالعدم عند القائلين به العدم العرفي الصادق بوجود جزء ما من أجزائه وأن المراد بالتفريق عند القائلين به التفريق العرفي الصادق باتصال بعض أجزائه . قوله : لَكِنْ ذَا الخِلافُ خُمَّا بألف الإطلاق، وهذا استدراك على إطلاق الخلاف السابق ؛ وفي التعبير بالتخصيص تَسَمُّحْ؛ لأنَّ التخصيص من عوارض العموم، والتقييد من عوارض الإطلاق؛ فالمعنى : لكن هذا الخلاف قيد العلماء إطلاقه. وقوله : (بالأنبيا)؛ أي: بسبب إخراج الأنبياء منه؛ فإن الأرض لا تأكل أجسامهم ولا تُبلي أبدانهم اتفاقاً، فالخلاف في غيرهم وغير من أُلحق بهم ممن سيأتي. وقوله : ( ومَنْ عَلَيهِمْ نُصَّا بألف الإطلاق؛ أي: ومن نصَّ الشارع على أن الأرض لا تأكلُ أجسامهم كالشهداء، والمراد بهم : كلُّ مقتول على الحقِّ، ولو لم يكن من شهداء المعركة، وكالمؤذنين احتساباً ؛ أي: ادخاراً لثواب ذلك عند الله تعالى لا لأُجرة، وكالعلماء العاملين وحملة القرآن الملازمين لتلاوته، العاملين بما فيه، المعظمين له بضبط لسانهم وطهارتهم وآدابهم، إلى غير ذلك مما نُقل عن الشارع، فإن المسألة توقيفية.
His statement: (two pure ones) is a description of (non-existence and separation); i.e., pure non-existence and pure separation. The meaning of the pureness of non-existence is its being free from any admixture of existence for any part, and the meaning of the pureness of separation is its being free from any admixture of connection in its parts. By that, the author repelled the misconception that what is meant by non-existence according to its proponents is conventional non-existence, which is true if some of its parts exist, and that what is meant by separation according to its proponents is conventional separation, which is true if some of its parts are connected. His statement: 'but this disagreement is specified' with an alif of absolute application, and this is a rectification of the absolute nature of the previous disagreement. In the expression 'specification' there is a looseness, because specification is an accident of generality, and restriction is an accident of absoluteness. So the meaning is: but this disagreement, the scholars restricted its absoluteness. His statement: (by the prophets) means: because of the exclusion of the prophets from it; for the earth does not eat their bodies nor cause their bodies to decay, by consensus. So the disagreement concerns others and those who are joined to them, who will come later. His statement: (and those upon whom it is textually established) with an alif of absolute application means: those whom the Lawgiver has textually established that the earth does not eat their bodies, like the martyrs, and by them is meant: everyone killed for the truth, even if he is not of the battlefield martyrs, and like the muezzins seeking reward, i.e., storing up reward for that with God, not for payment, and like the knowledgeable scholars and the bearers of the Qur'an who are constant in its recitation, acting according to it, venerating it by controlling their tongues, purity, and manners, and other such things that have been transmitted from the Lawgiver, for the matter is based on revealed texts.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of the word 'محضين' (two pure ones) in the poem and clarifies that the disagreement about whether the body becomes pure non-existence or pure separation is restricted to non-prophets. The author first defines the terms: 'pure non-existence' means the body is completely devoid of any existence in any part, and 'pure separation' means its parts are completely disconnected. He then notes that the author of the poem used this to rebut a possible misunderstanding: some might think that those who affirm non-existence after death mean conventional non-existence (i.e., the body is not completely non-existent but still has some trace), and similarly for separation. The poem then states that this disagreement is specifically restricted to prophets and those like them, because according to consensus, the earth does not consume the bodies of prophets. Thus, the disagreement only applies to others. Those included with the prophets are specified by revealed texts: martyrs (everyone killed for the truth), muezzins seeking reward, knowledgeable scholars, and Qur'an reciters who act accordingly—these are also protected from bodily decay. The passage ends by emphasizing that this matter is based solely on revelation (توقيفية), not on reason.

Two Opinions on Re-creating Accidents on the Day of Judgment
Al-Laqani presents two opinions on re-creating accidents and explains the first opinion's details and an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions on whether accidents are re-created on the Day of Judgment, and the reasoning behind the first opinion.

Core Idea
On Judgment Day, accidents are either re-created or replaced—the majority view favors re-creation.

Having established that bodies will be re-created, scholars differed on whether the accidents that clung to them in this life are also restored. This passage presents the two main positions and explores the details of the first opinion, including how different types of accidents are handled and an objection about incompatible properties.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing to analyse. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the two opinions
Locate where the first opinion begins and where the second opinion starts. Note the key difference: re-creation vs. replacement of accidents.
3
Examine the objection and answer
Find the objection about incompatible accidents (e.g., length and shortness) and how the first opinion responds by affirming gradual re-creation.
The response uses the principle that Allah is powerful over all things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
[ إعادة الأعراض والأزمانِ الخِلافُ في ذلك]
٩٩ - وفي إِعَادَةِ العَرَضُ قَوْلانِ ورُجْحَتْ إِعَادَةُ الأَعْيَانِ قوله: (وفي إِعَادَةِ العَرَضُ قَوْلانِ لما اختلف القائلون بإعادة الجسم في إعادة العرض الذي كان قائماً به في الدنيا، أشار إلى ذلك الاختلاف بقوله : (وفي إعادة العرض قولان:
فالقول الأول : وهو مذهب الأكثرين، وإليه مال إمامنا الأشعري أنه يُعاد حين إعادة الجسم، لا فرق في ذلك بين العَرَض الذي يطول بقاؤه كالبياض؛ وبين غيره كالصوت، ولا فرق في ذلك أيضاً بين ما هو مقدور للعبد كالضرب وبين غيره كالعلم، ولا يلزم أن تكون إعادته بالتلبس به كما كان في الدنيا، بل ما كان من الأعراض الملازمة للذات من بياض ونحوه وطول ونحوه، فإنه يُعاد متعلقاً بها، وما كان من غير ذلك كضرب وكفر وبقية المعاصي، وصلاة وصوم وبقية الطاعات، فإنه يُعاد مُصوّراً بصورة جسميةٍ، لكن الحسنات في صورة حسنة، والسيئات في صورة قبيحة، هذا هو الظاهر، والتفويض في مثل هذه المواطن أحسن.
فإن قيل : يلزمُ على ذلك اجتماع المتنافيات ؛ كالطول والقصر والكبر والصغر، أجيب بأن إعادة العَرَض ليست دُفعيةٌ بل على التدريج، حسبما كانت في الدنيا، لكن يمرُّ عليه جميع الأعراض في لمح البصر ، وربُّك على كلِّ شيءٍ قدير . والقولُ الثاني : امتناع إعادته مطلقاً، فيوجد الجسم بعرض آخر، فإنه لا ينفك عن عرض، وإلى هذا ذهب بعض أصحابنا أيضاً. قوله : (ورُجُحَتْ إِعَادَةُ الأَعْيَانِ أي ورجّح جماعةٌ من العلماء إعادة الأعراض : بأعيانها ; أي بأشخاصها وأَنْفُسها، فالمراد بالأعيان الأشخاص والأَنْفُس ; أي: شخص العَرّض ونفسه فيعاد العَرّض الذي كان في الدنيا، لا عَرَضُ آخر مغاير له، عقلاً بل يُعاد بعينه .
The matters heard (al-samiyyat)
[The re-creation of accidents and times, and the disagreement concerning that]
99 - And concerning the re-creation of the accident there are two opinions, and the re-creation of the very entities (al-a'yan) is deemed preponderant. His statement: (And concerning the re-creation of the accident there are two opinions) — when those who affirm the re-creation of the body differed about the re-creation of the accident that subsisted in it in this world, he pointed to that difference with his statement: (And concerning the re-creation of the accident there are two opinions):
The first opinion: it is the doctrine of the majority, and our Imam al-Ash'ari inclined to it, that it (the accident) is re-created at the time of the re-creation of the body. There is no difference in that between the accident that lasts long, like whiteness, and others like sound. There is also no difference in that between what is within the power of the servant, like striking, and others like knowledge. It is not necessary that its re-creation be by being attached as it was in this world. Rather, what were of the accidents inherent in the essence, like whiteness and the like, and length and the like, are re-created attached to it. And what were other than that, like striking, disbelief, and the rest of sins, and prayer, fasting, and the rest of acts of obedience, are re-created as a bodily form, but good deeds in a good form, and evil deeds in an ugly form. This is the apparent view, and consigning the knowledge (to God) is better in such places.
If it is said: This entails the coexistence of incompatibles, like length and shortness, bigness and smallness; the answer is that the re-creation of the accident is not instantaneous but gradual, according to how it was in this world, but all accidents pass over it in the blink of an eye, and your Lord is powerful over all things.
The second opinion: absolute impossibility of its re-creation; rather, the body is brought into existence with another accident, for it is never free from an accident. This was also the view of some of our companions.
His statement: (and the re-creation of the very entities is deemed preponderant) means: a group of scholars deemed preponderant the re-creation of accidents in their very identities (a'yan), i.e., as their individuals and selves. So by 'a'yan' is meant individuals and selves, i.e., the individual accident and itself, so the accident that was in this world is re-created, not another accident different from it, rationally, but it is re-created identically.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage presents two opinions on the re-creation of accidents (أعراض) on the Day of Judgment. It begins by noting that after affirming the re-creation of bodies, scholars differed on whether the accidents that originally inhered in those bodies are also re-created. The poem states there are two opinions and that the re-creation of the very entities (الأعيان) is deemed preponderant.

The first opinion, which is the majority view and the inclination of Imam al-Ash'ari, holds that accidents are re-created at the time the body is re-created. There is no distinction between accidents that last long (like whiteness) and fleeting ones (like sound), nor between those within human power (like striking) and those not (like knowledge). However, the manner of re-creation differs: accidents that are inseparable from the essence (e.g., whiteness, length) are re-created as attached to the essence; other accidents (e.g., acts of obedience or disobedience) are re-created as bodily forms—good deeds in a good form, sins in an ugly form. The author remarks that this is the apparent view, but consigning detailed knowledge to God is better.

An objection is raised: re-creating incompatible accidents (e.g., length and shortness, big and small) in the same body would be contradictory. The answer is that re-creation is not instantaneous but gradual, just as it was in this world, but all accidents pass through it swiftly.

The second opinion denies re-creation entirely; instead, the body is created anew with different accidents.

Finally, the author explains that 'رجحت إعادة الأعيان' means some scholars favored re-creating the very same individual accidents (أعيانها) that existed in the world, not different ones.

Key Terms
إعادة العرض
قولان
مذهب الأكثرين
الأشعري
الملازمة للذات
المتنافيات
التدريج
الأعيان
أعيان الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That incompatible accidents cannot coexist even in gradual re-creation, or that accidents are never re-created at all.
Correction: The first opinion holds that re-creation is gradual, so incompatibles do not coexist simultaneously; Allah's power makes it possible.

Checkpoint
According to the first opinion, how are acts of obedience and disobedience re-created?
A) They are re-created as attached to the essence.
B) They are re-created as bodily forms, with good deeds in a good form and sins in an ugly form.
C) They are not re-created at all.
D) They are re-created only if they are permanent accidents.

Key Takeaway
On Judgment Day, accidents are re-created alongside bodies according to the majority view, with good and evil deeds taking physical forms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your deeds are re-created as bodily forms on Judgment Day, what shape do you fear your sins might take? What change in your daily actions does this thought demand of you right now?
?
The passage says even fleeting accidents like every word you speak will be re-created. Does this truth make you more mindful of what comes out of your mouth? What will you do to guard your tongue starting today?
?
The objection about incompatible accidents is answered by the fact that all accidents pass in a blink of an eye. How does the suddenness of that re-creation affect your sense of urgency in repenting and preparing for that moment? What is one concrete step you will take today to ensure your deeds take a good form then?

Two Opinions on Restoring Accidents
Sanusi presents two opinions on accident restoration and defends the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major opinions on whether accidents are restored in the afterlife, the reasoning behind the majority view (including the objection about incompatibles and its answer), and the meaning of 'restoration of the very entities'.

Core Idea
Accidents are restored gradually, not simultaneously, avoiding contradiction.

After affirming that bodies are restored in the afterlife, theologians debated whether the accidents that once inhered in them are also restored. This passage presents the two main opinions, explains the first in detail (including a response to a logical objection), and clarifies a phrase from the poem. Understanding this debate illuminates how Ash'ari theology balances divine power with rational coherence.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the reason for disagreement
Start by reading the Arabic verse (line 99) and the commentator's explanation of why the disagreement arose: those who affirm bodily restoration differed on the restoration of accidents.
Note the phrase 'وفي إعادة العرض قولان' sets up the two opinions.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find the two opinions: the first (majority, incl. al-Ash'ari) affirms restoration at the time of body's restoration; the second denies restoration absolutely. Notice the distinctions made within the first opinion.
The first opinion includes details about how different types of accidents are restored (inherent vs. voluntary acts).
3
Examine the objection and answer
Read the objection: restoring incompatible accidents (e.g., length and shortness) would be contradictory. Then read the answer: restoration is gradual, not instantaneous, so no contradiction arises.
This shows how Ash'ari theology handles apparent rational difficulties.
4
Understand 'restoration of the very entities'
The commentator explains the verse phrase: it means the identical accident (its very self) is restored, not a different one. This is the preponderant view.
This concludes the passage by clarifying a key term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٩٩ - وفي إِعَادَةِ العَرَضِ قَوْلانِ ورُجْحَتْ إِعَادَةُ الأَعْيَانِ قوله: (وفي إِعَادَةِ العَرَضِ قَوْلانِ) لما اختلف القائلون بإعادة الجسم في إعادة العرض الذي كان قائماً به في الدنيا، أشار إلى ذلك الاختلاف بقوله : (وفي إعادة العرض قولان: فالقول الأول : وهو مذهب الأكثرين، وإليه مال إمامنا الأشعري أنه يُعاد حين إعادة الجسم، لا فرق في ذلك بين العَرَض الذي يطول بقاؤه كالبياض؛ وبين غيره كالصوت، ولا فرق في ذلك أيضاً بين ما هو مقدور للعبد كالضرب وبين غيره كالعلم، ولا يلزم أن تكون إعادته بالتلبس به كما كان في الدنيا، بل ما كان من الأعراض الملازمة للذات من بياض ونحوه وطول ونحوه، فإنه يُعاد متعلقاً بها، وما كان من غير ذلك كضرب وكفر وبقية المعاصي، وصلاة وصوم وبقية الطاعات، فإنه يُعاد مُصوّراً بصورة جسميةٍ، لكن الحسنات في صورة حسنة، والسيئات في صورة قبيحة، هذا هو الظاهر، والتفويض في مثل هذه المواطن أحسن. فإن قيل : يلزمُ على ذلك اجتماع المتنافيات ؛ كالطول والقصر والكبر والصغر، أجيب بأن إعادة العَرَض ليست دُفعيةٌ بل على التدريج، حسبما كانت في الدنيا، لكن يمرُّ عليه جميع الأعراض في لمح البصر ، وربُّك على كلِّ شيءٍ قدير . والقولُ الثاني : امتناع إعادته مطلقاً، فيوجد الجسم بعرض آخر، فإنه لا ينفك عن عرض، وإلى هذا ذهب بعض أصحابنا أيضاً. قوله : (ورُجُحَتْ إِعَادَةُ الأَعْيَانِ) أي ورجّح جماعةٌ من العلماء إعادة الأعراض : بأعيانها ؛ أي بأشخاصها وأَنْفُسها، فالمراد بالأعيان الأشخاص والأَنْفُس ؛ أي: شخص العَرَض ونفسه فيعاد العَرَض الذي كان في الدنيا، لا عَرَضُ آخر مغاير له، عقلاً بل يُعاد بعينه.
99 - And concerning the restoration of the accident there are two opinions, and the restoration of the very entities is preponderant. He said: (And concerning the restoration of the accident there are two opinions) because those who affirm the restoration of the body differed regarding the restoration of the accident that inhered in it in this world, and he pointed to that difference by his saying: (And concerning the restoration of the accident there are two opinions): The first opinion – and it is the way of the majority, and our Imam al-Ash‘ari inclined towards it – is that it is restored at the time of the restoration of the body. There is no distinction in that between the accident that lasts a long time like whiteness and others like sound, nor is there a distinction between what is within the ability of the servant like striking and others like knowledge. It is not necessary that its restoration be by inherence as it was in this world. Rather, those accidents that are inseparable from the essence, like whiteness and its like, and length and its like, are restored attaching to it. And what is other than that, like striking, disbelief, the rest of sins, prayer, fasting, and the rest of acts of obedience, are restored represented in a bodily form. However, good deeds are in a good form, and evil deeds in an ugly form. This is the apparent view, and delegating knowledge (tafwīḍ) in such matters is better. If it is said: This entails the combination of incompatibles such as length and shortness, bigness and smallness; it is answered that the restoration of the accident is not instantaneous but gradual, just as it was in this world, but all the accidents pass over it in the blink of an eye, and your Lord is capable of all things. The second opinion: the impossibility of its restoration absolutely, so the body occurs with another accident, for it is not free from an accident. Some of our companions also went to this. He said: (And the restoration of the very entities is preponderant) i.e., a group of scholars preponderated the restoration of accidents in their very entities, i.e., their individuals and selves. So by 'entities' (a‘yān) is meant individuals and selves, i.e., the individual accident itself, so the accident that existed in this world is restored, not another accident different from it, rationally, but it is restored in its very self.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on verse 99 of the poem, addressing the theological question of whether accidents (a‘rāḍ) that inhered in bodies in this world are restored in the afterlife. The text begins by stating the verse, then proceeds to explain it. It first presents the reason for the disagreement, then enumerates two opinions. The first opinion, held by the majority including Imam al-Ash‘arī, affirms the restoration of accidents at the time of the restoration of the body. No distinction is made between lasting and transient accidents, or between those within human power and those not. The manner of restoration differs: inseparable accidents like whiteness are restored as inherent qualities, while voluntary acts like prayer or sin are restored in a bodily form, good deeds appearing beautiful and evil deeds ugly. The author notes that the apparent view is as stated, but tafwīḍ (delegating knowledge to God) is better. An objection is raised: restoring incompatible accidents (e.g., length and shortness simultaneously) entails contradiction. The answer is that the restoration is not instantaneous but gradual, passing through all states in a moment by divine power. The second opinion denies the restoration of accidents absolutely; the body is recreated with a different accident. Finally, the verse's phrase 'the restoration of the very entities is preponderant' is explained, meaning that some scholars prefer the restoration of the identical accident itself (bi‘aynihi), not a replacement.

Key Terms
إعادة
العرض
قولان
إعادة الأعيان
اجتماع المتنافيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Restoring incompatible accidents would entail contradiction (e.g., a body cannot be both long and short at the same time).
Correction: The restoration is not simultaneous but gradual; the body passes through all states in a single moment, so no contradiction occurs.

Checkpoint
ما هو جواب المعترض على إعادة الأعراض المتضادة؟
A) الإعادة تكون دفعة واحدة بقدرة الله
B) الإعادة تكون على التدريج وليس دفعة
C) الأعراض المتضادة لا يمكن جمعها أبداً
D) الإعادة تكون بجسم جديد

Key Takeaway
Accidents are restored at the time of bodily restoration, but gradually to avoid contradiction; the preferred view is that the identical accident is restored.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your deeds—every sin and every good deed—will be restored in a bodily form on the Day of Judgment. Are you prepared to see that form? What will it look like? Imagine the shame of seeing your sins manifested. How does that motivate you to change today?
?
The text says that good deeds are restored in a good form, and evil deeds in an ugly form. If your deeds were to be represented bodily right now, what would they look like? Would you be proud or ashamed? What specific action can you take today to ensure your deeds appear beautiful?
?
The restoration of accidents happens gradually but in a moment. Your entire life's accidental deeds will pass before you in an instant. Does this thought terrify you or comfort you? How does it affect your repentance and your hope in God's mercy?

Two Opinions on the Restoration of Time
The commentator presents two opinions on the restoration of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions regarding the restoration of time in the afterlife and the reasoning behind each opinion.

Core Idea
The restoration of time is debated: one view affirms it gradually for witness, another denies it to avoid logical contradictions.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks a line from the poem that states there are two opinions concerning time in the afterlife. This is a subtle but important issue in eschatology: will the moments we lived through be recreated to serve as witnesses? The text presents both sides and explains how the stronger opinion resolves the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its explanation
Start by reading the verse line and the commentator's explanation. Note that the verse simply says 'And concerning time there are two opinions' and the commentator clarifies that this refers to the restoration of time.
The verse itself is a placeholder; the real content is in the commentary.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find the first opinion (al-arjaḥ) which holds that all times of the bodies are restored so that they may bear witness. Then find the second opinion that denies restoration because it would combine incompatibles like past, present, and future.
The first opinion is called 'preponderant' (al-arjaḥ).
3
Understand the objection and the reply
The second opinion's objection is based on logical contradiction. The reply from the first opinion is that restoration is not instantaneous but gradual, thus no contradiction arises. The reply emphasizes the quickness but gradualness of the process.
This shows how theological reasoning handles apparent paradoxes.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the restoration of time matters: it allows the very moments of our lives to testify for or against us on the Day of Judgment. This underscores the comprehensiveness of divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٠٠ - وَفِي الزَّمَنِ قَوْلانِ والحِسَابُ حَقٌّ وَمَا فِي حَقٌّ ارْتِيابُ قوله : (وَفِي الزَّمَنِ قَوْلانِ) أي: وفي إعادة الزمن قولان: أحدهما : وهو الأرجح أنه يُعاد جميع أزمنة الأجسام التي مرت عليها في الدنيا، لتشهد للإنسان وعليه بما وقع فيها من الطاعات والآثام. وثانيهما : امتناع إعادته ؛ لاجتماع المتنافيات كالماضي والحال والاستقبال. وأجاب عن ذلك القائلون بالقول الأول بأن إعادته ليست دُفْعِيَّةٌ ، بل على التدريج حسبما كانت عليه في الدنيا، لكن في أسرع وقت.
100 - And concerning time there are two opinions, and the reckoning is true, and there is no doubt concerning it. He said: (And concerning time there are two opinions) i.e., concerning the restoration of time there are two opinions: The first – and it is the preponderant – is that all the times of the bodies that passed in this world are restored, so that they may bear witness for and against the human being regarding what occurred in them of acts of obedience and sins. And the second: the impossibility of its restoration due to the combination of incompatibles such as past, present, and future. And those holding the first opinion replied to that by saying that its restoration is not instantaneous, but rather gradual as it was in this world, but in the quickest time.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage comments on part of verse 100 of the poem. It discusses the issue of time (zamān) in the afterlife: whether the moments that passed in this world will be recreated. The verse is quoted, followed by an explanation. The commentator states that there are two opinions regarding the restoration of time. The first, which is preponderant (arjaḥ), holds that all times of the bodies are restored, so that they can serve as witnesses for or against the person concerning the deeds performed in them. The second opinion deems restoration impossible because it would combine incompatibles: the same moment cannot be past, present, and future simultaneously. The reply from the proponents of the first opinion is that the restoration is not instantaneous but gradual, just as time originally passed, but it occurs in the briefest span.

Key Terms
الزمن
إعادة الزمن
أزمنة الأجسام
اجتماع المتنافيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the objection based on incompatibles is unanswerable, making the first opinion invalid.
Correction: The reply shows that gradual restoration avoids the contradiction, so the first opinion remains valid.

Checkpoint
For what purpose are the times of bodies restored in the afterlife according to the preponderant opinion?
A) As evidence of God's power
B) To bear witness for and against the human being
C) For the person to know his age
D) To fill Paradise and Hell

Key Takeaway
The preponderant opinion holds that time is restored gradually in the afterlife to serve as a witness for or against each person's deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The time you spend in every act of obedience or sin will be recreated to testify for or against you. Are you living today with the awareness that every moment is being recorded for that testimony? What would you change if you truly believed that your past will literally speak against you?
?
The preponderant opinion says time is restored gradually. How would your daily actions change if you knew that even the fastest moment (faster than the blink of an eye) will be brought back to witness for you? Are you using your time as if it matters eternally?
?
If you could re-live one past moment, would it testify for you or against you? What concrete steps can you take today to ensure that the next moment will be a witness for you, not against you?

The Reality and Definition of the Reckoning
The commentator affirms the reality of the reckoning and defines it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the reckoning is a true event established by the Quran, Sunna, and consensus, and you will know its definition and scope.

Core Idea
The reckoning is true: God will inform every person of all their deeds in detail.

The commentator begins by affirming the reality of the reckoning, grounding it in three authoritative sources: the Quran, the Sunna, and the consensus of scholars. He then provides a clear definition both linguistically and technically, and clarifies who will be subject to this reckoning. Let's read his words to grasp this foundational belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow from affirmation to definition to scope.
The passage includes a hadith that illustrates the exception to the reckoning.
2
Identify the three proofs for the reckoning
The commentator mentions three sources that establish the truth of the reckoning: a Quranic verse, a Prophetic hadith, and the consensus of the Muslim community. Find each one in the text.
The Quranic verse is 'swift in reckoning' from Surah ar-Ra'd.
3
Understand the technical definition
The reckoning is defined terminologically as 'God's informing people of their deeds in detail after they receive their books.' Note the elements: who, what, when, and how.
The definition includes both good and evil deeds, sayings and actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والحِسَابُ حَقٌّ) أي : ثابت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، ففي الكتاب سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ [الرعد: ٤١]، وفي السنة: «حاسبوا أنفسكم قبل أن تحاسبوا (۱) وأجمع المسلمون عليه، وهو لغة: العدد واصطلاحاً: توقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم ؛ خيراً كانت أو شرا قولاً كانت أو فعلاً تفصيلاً بعد أخذهم كتبها . ويكون للمؤمن والكافر إنساً وجنا إلا مَنِ استثني منهم، ففي الحديث: «يدخلُ الجنة من أمتي سبعون ألفاً ليس عليهم حساب، فقيل له : هلا استزدت ربَّك؟ فقال: استزدته فزادني مع كلّ واحدٍ مِنَ السبعين ألفاً سبعين ألفاً ، فقيل له : هلا استزدت ربَّك ؟ فقال : استزدته فزادني ثلاثَ حَنَياتٍ بيده الكريمةِ ) (۳) أو كما ورد؛ والثلاث
He said: (And the reckoning is true) i.e., it is established by the Book, the Sunna, and consensus. For in the Book: 'swift in reckoning' [ar-Ra‘d 41], and in the Sunna: 'Take yourselves to account before you are taken to account' (1) and the Muslims have agreed upon it. And it is linguistically: counting, and terminologically: God's informing people of their deeds – good or evil, sayings or actions – in detail after they have been given their books. And it is for the believer and the disbeliever, human and jinn, except those who are exempted from them. For in the hadith: 'Seventy thousand of my community will enter Paradise without being called to account.' It was said to him: 'Will you not ask for more from your Lord?' He said: 'I asked Him for more, and He gave me with every single one of the seventy thousand another seventy thousand.' It was said to him: 'Will you not ask for more from your Lord?' He said: 'I asked Him for more, and He gave me three handfuls with His generous hand' (3) or as was reported; and the three...
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage explains the part of verse 100 concerning the reckoning (al-ḥisāb). The commentator begins by affirming that the reckoning is true (ḥaqq), meaning established by three sources: the Quran (citing the verse 'swift in reckoning' from Surah ar-Ra‘d), the Sunna (citing the hadith 'Take yourselves to account before you are taken to account'), and consensus (ijmā‘) of the Muslim community. Then he provides a definition: linguistically, ḥisāb means counting; terminologically, it is God's informing people of all their deeds—good and evil, sayings and actions—in detail after they receive their books of deeds. He notes that this reckoning applies to both believers and disbelievers, humans and jinn, except those specifically exempted, such as the seventy thousand (and additional multitudes) who enter Paradise without being called to account, as mentioned in the hadith. The hadith is quoted, showing the Prophet’s intercession for extra numbers. The passage ends abruptly at 'and the three...' indicating the continuation of the hadith.

Key Terms
الحساب
توقيف الله
كتب الأعمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the reckoning is only for certain people, not all.
Correction: The passage states the reckoning is for believer and disbeliever, human and jinn, except those explicitly exempted by Allah.

B) توقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم تفصيلاً
C) محاسبة النفس

Key Takeaway
The reckoning is a true event in which God will inform all people of their deeds, established by the Quran, Sunna, and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said, 'Take yourselves to account before you are taken to account.' Tonight, before you sleep, will you honestly review your day as if it were being presented to Allah? What one moment from today would you most want to change?

You will be informed of every word you spoke and every intention you harbored. Which secret thought or word are you most afraid of being exposed? What does that fear tell you about the state of your heart?

Seventy thousand will enter Paradise without reckoning—by sheer mercy. Are you banking on that mercy or on your own deeds? If you were to die tonight, would you rather be among those exempted or would you insist on facing the reckoning? What choice does that compel you to make now?

The Reckoning is True: Evidence and Definition
Sanusi establishes the truth of the Reckoning with textual evidence and defines it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Reckoning is a confirmed truth of Islam, established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, and you will know its linguistic and technical definition.

Core Idea
The Reckoning is a certainty confirmed by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

This passage begins by asserting the truth of the Reckoning (al-hisab). It then provides the foundational proofs for this belief and defines the term both linguistically and technically. Understanding this definition is crucial for the subsequent discussion on its interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author cites three sources of evidence before giving the definition.
The definition is given in two parts: linguistic and technical.
2
Identify the three proofs
The author mentions the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. Find each reference and reflect on why each is authoritative.
The Quranic verse is 'Swift in reckoning' (al-Ra'd 41).
3
Understand the definition
The technical definition is 'God’s making people aware of their deeds in detail after receiving their books.' Notice the key concepts: tawqif, deeds, detail.
This definition sets the stage for later interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والحِسَابُ حَقٌّ) أي : ثابت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، ففي الكتاب سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ [الرعد: ٤١]، وفي السنة: «حاسبوا أنفسكم قبل أن تحاسبوا» وأجمع المسلمون عليه، وهو لغة: العدد واصطلاحاً: توقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم ؛ خيراً كانت أو شرا قولاً كانت أو فعلاً تفصيلاً بعد أخذهم كتبها . ويكون للمؤمن والكافر إنساً وجنا إلا مَنِ استثني منهم، ففي الحديث: «يدخلُ الجنة من أمتي سبعون ألفاً ليس عليهم حساب، فقيل له : هلا استزدت ربَّك؟ فقال: استزدته فزادني مع كلّ واحدٍ مِنَ السبعين ألفاً سبعين ألفاً ، فقيل له : هلا استزدت ربَّك ؟ فقال : استزدته فزادني ثلاثَ حَنَياتٍ بيده الكريمةِ أو كما ورد؛ والثلاث حثيات ثلاث دفعات من غير عددٍ فهؤلاء يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب، وإذا كان من المؤمنين من يكون أدنى إلى الرحمة فيدخل الجنة من غير حساب، وإذا كان من الكافرين من يكون أدنى إلى الغضب فيدخل النار من غير حساب، فطائفة تدخل الجنة بلا حساب وطائفةٌ تدخل النار بلا حساب وطائفةٌ توقف للحساب، فلا تنافي بين النصوص في مثل ذلك. وقد اختلف في المراد بتوقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم : فقيل : المراد به أن يخلق الله في قلوبهم علوماً ضرورية بمقادير أعمالهم من الثواب والعقاب، وهذا قول الفخر . وقيل : المراد به أن يوقفهم بين يديه ويؤتيهم كتب أعمالهم فيها سيئاتهم وحسناتهم؛ فيقول: هذه سيئاتكم وقد تجاوزتُ عنها، وهذه حسناتكم وقد ضاعفتها لكم؛ وهذا القول نُقل عن ابن عباس، وفيه قصور ؛ لأن الحساب غير قاصر على هذا المقدار، وقد ورد أن الكافر ينكر فتشهد جوارحه. وقيل : المراد به أن يكلمهم في شأن أعمالهم وكيفية ما لها من الثواب، وما عليها من العقاب فيُسمعهم كلامه القديم، وهذا هو الذي تشهد له الأحاديث الصحيحة، ولا يشغله تعالى محاسبة أحدٍ عن أحد، بل يُحاسب الناس جميعاً معاً، حتى إن كلَّ أحد يرى أنه المحاسب وحده. وكيفيته مختلفة : فمنه اليسير ،والعسير ،والسر ،والجهر، والتوبيخ والفضل والعدل . وحكمتُهُ : إظهار تفاوتِ المراتب في الكمال وفضائح أهل النقص؛ ففيه ترغيب الحسنات، وزَجْرٌ عن السيئات. قوله : (وَمَا فِي حَقٌّ ارْتِبابُ) أي: وليس في وقوع حق شَكٍّ؛ أي: لا ينبغي أن يقع فيه ذلك .
His saying: 'And the Reckoning is true' — i.e., it is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. In the Book: 'Swift in reckoning' [al-Ra'd 41], and in the Sunnah: 'Call yourselves to account before you are called to account' and the Muslims have agreed upon it. Linguistically it is counting; terminologically it is God's making people aware of their deeds, good or evil, words or actions, in detail after they receive their books. And it applies to the believer and the disbeliever, human and jinn, except those who are excluded from them. In the hadith: 'Seventy thousand of my community will enter Paradise without reckoning.' It was said to him: 'Will you not ask your Lord for more?' He said: 'I asked Him and He gave me with every one of the seventy thousand seventy thousand more.' It was said: 'Will you not ask for more?' He said: 'I asked and He gave me three handfuls with His generous hand' — or as it was related; and the three handfuls are three unnumbered pourings. So these enter Paradise without reckoning. And if among the believers there are some who are closer to mercy, they enter Paradise without reckoning, and if among the disbelievers there are some who are closer to wrath, they enter the Fire without reckoning. So a group enters Paradise without reckoning, a group enters the Fire without reckoning, and a group is stopped for reckoning. There is no contradiction between the texts in such matters. And there is disagreement concerning the intended meaning of 'God's making people aware of their deeds': it is said that the intended meaning is that He creates in their hearts necessary knowledges of the measures of their deeds of reward and punishment — this is the opinion of al-Fakhr. And it is said that the intended meaning is that He stops them before Him and gives them the books of their deeds containing their sins and good deeds, saying: 'These are your sins and I have pardoned them, and these are your good deeds and I have multiplied them for you' — this opinion is transmitted from Ibn 'Abbas, but it is deficient because the reckoning is not confined to this extent, and it has been reported that the disbeliever denies and his limbs testify against him. And it is said that the intended meaning is that He speaks to them concerning their deeds and how they have reward and punishment, making them hear His eternal speech — and this is what the authentic hadiths attest to, and He is not distracted by the accounting of one from another, but rather He accounts all people together, so that each one sees that he alone is being accounted. And its modality varies: some is easy, some difficult, some secret, some open, some rebuke, some favor, some justice. And its wisdom is to manifest the difference of ranks in perfection and the scandals of the deficient, for it contains encouragement of good deeds and deterrence from evil deeds. His saying: 'And concerning the truth there is no doubt' — i.e., there is no doubt concerning the occurrence of the truth; i.e., it should not occur.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Reckoning (al-hisab). It begins by asserting that the Reckoning is true (haqq), established by Quran (swift in reckoning), sunna (call yourselves to account), and consensus. Then it defines it linguistically as counting and terminologically as God making people aware (tawqif) of their deeds after receiving their books. It applies to all, with exceptions as per hadith. The author then cites the famous hadith about seventy thousand entering Paradise without account, along with additions, clarifying that some enter without account, some are stopped, and there is no contradiction. Next, he presents three interpretations of 'tawqif': (1) al-Fakhr's view: God creates necessary knowledge of reward/punishment; (2) transmitted from Ibn 'Abbas: God stands people before Him with their books, saying He pardoned sins and multiplied good deeds — but this is deficient because it does not cover all cases (e.g., the disbeliever's limbs testify); (3) the correct view: God speaks to them with His eternal speech (kalam qadim), making them hear it, as attested by sound hadiths. He adds that God is not distracted, accounting all simultaneously. Then he notes the various modalities of the account (easy, difficult, secret, open, etc.) and its wisdom: to show differences in degrees of perfection and to encourage good and deter evil. Finally, he comments on the phrase 'and concerning the truth there is no doubt' (wa ma fi haqq iritiyab), meaning that the occurrence of the truth (the Reckoning) should not be doubted.

Key Terms
الحساب
الحق
التوقيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT mentioned as evidence for the truth of the Reckoning?
A) The Quran
B) The Sunnah
C) Rational proof
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
The Reckoning is an established reality, proven by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, defined as God's making people aware of their deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You will stand before God and be made aware of every action and word. Which habit—good or bad—have you been ignoring, thinking it doesn't matter? Starting today, what will you begin to change?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded: 'Call yourselves to account before you are called to account.' When you lie down tonight, will you honestly review your day? What is one thing you can change tonight?
?
The Reckoning includes both good and evil, and even the smallest good deed counts. Which small good act have you been neglecting that you can revive with the intention of meeting your Lord with a fuller record?

Interpretations of God's Making People Aware of Their Deeds
Sanusi presents the hadith of the seventy thousand and the three interpretations of tawqif.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly interpretations of how God makes people aware of their deeds on the Day of Judgment, and why the third interpretation is preferred.

Core Idea
Three interpretations of the Reckoning exist; the soundest is that God speaks to them with His eternal speech.

After establishing the truth of the Reckoning, the text delves into the nature of how God will make people aware of their deeds. There are three opinions, each with its own basis. The passage evaluates these, pointing out the strengths and weaknesses of each.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith about exceptions
The passage begins by stating that the Reckoning applies to all except those exempt, citing a hadith about seventy thousand entering Paradise without account.
This shows that not everyone undergoes the same process.
2
Examine the first two interpretations
The first says God creates necessary knowledge in hearts (al-Fakhr). The second says God shows them their books and pardons (Ibn Abbas). Note the criticism of the second: it is deficient.
The second interpretation does not cover cases like the disbeliever's denial.
3
Study the third interpretation
The third says God speaks to them with His eternal speech. The author indicates this is the correct view, supported by authentic hadiths.
This interpretation also clarifies that God accounts all simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والحِسَابُ حَقٌّ) أي : ثابت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، ففي الكتاب سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ [الرعد: ٤١]، وفي السنة: «حاسبوا أنفسكم قبل أن تحاسبوا» وأجمع المسلمون عليه، وهو لغة: العدد واصطلاحاً: توقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم ؛ خيراً كانت أو شرا قولاً كانت أو فعلاً تفصيلاً بعد أخذهم كتبها . ويكون للمؤمن والكافر إنساً وجنا إلا مَنِ استثني منهم، ففي الحديث: «يدخلُ الجنة من أمتي سبعون ألفاً ليس عليهم حساب، فقيل له : هلا استزدت ربَّك؟ فقال: استزدته فزادني مع كلّ واحدٍ مِنَ السبعين ألفاً سبعين ألفاً ، فقيل له : هلا استزدت ربَّك ؟ فقال : استزدته فزادني ثلاثَ حَنَياتٍ بيده الكريمةِ أو كما ورد؛ والثلاث حثيات ثلاث دفعات من غير عددٍ فهؤلاء يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب، وإذا كان من المؤمنين من يكون أدنى إلى الرحمة فيدخل الجنة من غير حساب، وإذا كان من الكافرين من يكون أدنى إلى الغضب فيدخل النار من غير حساب، فطائفة تدخل الجنة بلا حساب وطائفةٌ تدخل النار بلا حساب وطائفةٌ توقف للحساب، فلا تنافي بين النصوص في مثل ذلك. وقد اختلف في المراد بتوقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم : فقيل : المراد به أن يخلق الله في قلوبهم علوماً ضرورية بمقادير أعمالهم من الثواب والعقاب، وهذا قول الفخر . وقيل : المراد به أن يوقفهم بين يديه ويؤتيهم كتب أعمالهم فيها سيئاتهم وحسناتهم؛ فيقول: هذه سيئاتكم وقد تجاوزتُ عنها، وهذه حسناتكم وقد ضاعفتها لكم؛ وهذا القول نُقل عن ابن عباس، وفيه قصور ؛ لأن الحساب غير قاصر على هذا المقدار، وقد ورد أن الكافر ينكر فتشهد جوارحه. وقيل : المراد به أن يكلمهم في شأن أعمالهم وكيفية ما لها من الثواب، وما عليها من العقاب فيُسمعهم كلامه القديم، وهذا هو الذي تشهد له الأحاديث الصحيحة، ولا يشغله تعالى محاسبة أحدٍ عن أحد، بل يُحاسب الناس جميعاً معاً، حتى إن كلَّ أحد يرى أنه المحاسب وحده. وكيفيته مختلفة : فمنه اليسير ،والعسير ،والسر ،والجهر، والتوبيخ والفضل والعدل . وحكمتُهُ : إظهار تفاوتِ المراتب في الكمال وفضائح أهل النقص؛ ففيه ترغيب الحسنات، وزَجْرٌ عن السيئات. قوله : (وَمَا فِي حَقٌّ ارْتِبابُ) أي: وليس في وقوع حق شَكٍّ؛ أي: لا ينبغي أن يقع فيه ذلك .

Commentary

?

The Varieties of the Reckoning and Its Wisdom
Sanusi outlines the varieties of the Reckoning and its wisdom, then affirms its certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Reckoning has various modalities (easy, difficult, etc.) and a profound wisdom, and that its occurrence is absolutely certain without doubt.

Core Idea
The Reckoning's different forms manifest divine wisdom and its truth is beyond doubt.

The final part of the passage describes the different ways the Reckoning can occur, emphasizing divine wisdom behind it. It then closes by affirming that there can be no doubt concerning its truth, reinforcing the certainty of this article of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of modalities
The passage lists various pairs: easy and difficult, secret and open, rebuke, favor, justice. Reflect on why these variations exist.
These modalities reflect the diversity of deeds and divine wisdom.
2
Understand the wisdom
The wisdom is to show differences in ranks and to expose faults, encouraging good and deterring evil.
This shows the pedagogical purpose of the Reckoning.
3
Absorb the concluding certainty
The final statement affirms that there is no doubt in the truth of the Reckoning. This is a strong emphasis on certainty.
This counters any skepticism about the reality of the account.

?

?

The Afterlife Account: Three Groups and Interpretations
The author enumerates three groups and three interpretations of divine reckoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three groups of people in the afterlife (those entering Paradise or Hell without account, and those stopped for account) and the preferred interpretation of divine reckoning as direct speech with God's eternal word.

Core Idea
God's reckoning is just, merciful, and simultaneously universal yet personal.

This passage from the matn clarifies how different groups face judgment after death. It first describes three categories based on closeness to mercy or wrath, then delves into the meaning of 'stopping for account,' presenting three interpretations. The author weighs them and affirms that God's reckoning is both perfectly just and beyond human limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get an overall sense. Notice the flow from the three groups to the interpretations and then to the wisdom.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three groups
Find where the author lists the three groups: those entering Paradise without account, those entering Hell without account, and those stopped for account. Note the reasoning based on closeness to mercy or wrath.
The author stresses there is no contradiction between texts on this matter.
3
Compare the three interpretations
The passage presents three views on 'stopping for account.' The first is al-Fakhr's (necessary knowledge), the second is from Ibn 'Abbas (showing the book), and the third is direct speech with God's eternal word. Understand why the author prefers the third view.
The author criticizes the second as insufficient and notes the third is supported by authentic hadiths.
4
Reflect on the wisdom and modalities
The author explains that God reckons everyone simultaneously yet each person feels alone. The modalities vary (easy, hard, secret, public) and the wisdom is to manifest differences in perfection and deter evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
حثيات ثلاث دفعات من غير عددٍ فهؤلاء يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب، وإذا كان من المؤمنين من يكون أدنى إلى الرحمة فيدخل الجنة من غير حساب، وإذا كان من الكافرين من يكون أدنى إلى الغضب فيدخل النار من غير حساب، فطائفة تدخل الجنة بلا حساب وطائفةٌ تدخل النار بلا حساب وطائفةٌ توقف للحساب، فلا تنافي بين النصوص في مثل ذلك.
وقد اختلف في المراد بتوقيف الله الناس على أعمالهم : فقيل : المراد به أن يخلق الله في قلوبهم علوماً ضرورية بمقادير أعمالهم من الثواب والعقاب، وهذا قول الفخر .
وقيل : المراد به أن يوقفهم بين يديه ويؤتيهم كتب أعمالهم فيها سيئاتهم وحسناتهم؛ فيقول: هذه سيئاتكم وقد تجاوزتُ عنها، وهذه حسناتكم وقد ضاعفتها لكم؛ وهذا القول نُقل عن ابن عباس، وفيه قصور ؛ لأن الحساب غير قاصر على هذا المقدار، وقد ورد أن الكافر ينكر فتشهد جوارحه.
وقيل : المراد به أن يكلمهم في شأن أعمالهم وكيفية ما لها من الثواب، وما عليها من العقاب فيُسمعهم كلامه القديم، وهذا هو الذي تشهد له الأحاديث الصحيحة (١) ، ولا يشغله تعالى محاسبة أحدٍ عن أحد، بل يُحاسب الناس جميعاً معاً، حتى إن كلَّ أحد يرى أنه المحاسب وحده. وكيفيته مختلفة : فمنه اليسير ،والعسير ،والسر ،والجهر، والتوبيخ والفضل والعدل .
وحكمتُهُ : إظهار تفاوتِ المراتب في الكمال وفضائح أهل النقص؛ ففيه ترغيب الحسنات، وزَجْرٌ عن السيئات.
قوله : (وَمَا فِي حَقٌّ ارْتِبابُ) أي: وليس في وقوع حق شَكٍّ؛ أي: لا ينبغي أن يقع فيه ذلك .
The things heard: Three groups without number enter Paradise without account. If among the believers there is one who is closer to mercy, he enters Paradise without account. If among the disbelievers there is one who is closer to wrath, he enters the Fire without account. So a group enters Paradise without account, a group enters the Fire without account, and a group is stopped for account. There is no contradiction between the texts in such matters. There is disagreement about the meaning of God stopping people for their deeds. It is said: meaning that God creates in their hearts necessary knowledge of the amounts of their deeds of reward and punishment—this is the opinion of al-Fakhr. It is said: meaning that He stops them before Him and gives them their books of deeds containing their evil deeds and good deeds, saying: 'These are your evil deeds, and I have overlooked them; these are your good deeds, and I have multiplied them for you'—this opinion is transmitted from Ibn 'Abbas, but it is insufficient because the account is not limited to this measure, and it has been narrated that the disbeliever denies, so his limbs testify against him. It is said: meaning that He speaks to them concerning the matter of their deeds and the nature of what reward they have and what punishment they incur, making them hear His eternal speech—this is what the authentic hadiths testify to. The Almighty is not occupied by the reckoning of one over another; rather, He reckons all people together, so that each one sees that he alone is being reckoned. Its modality varies: some is easy, some difficult, some secret, some public, some rebuke, some favor, and some justice. Its wisdom is to manifest the difference in degrees of perfection and the disgrace of those deficient; thus it encourages good deeds and deters from evil deeds. His saying: 'And there is no doubt concerning the truth' means: there is no doubt about the occurrence of the truth; i.e., it should not occur.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the afterlife reckoning. It begins by describing three groups: those who enter Paradise without account (the pious), a subset of believers who enter without account due to closeness to mercy, and a subset of disbelievers who enter Hell without account due to closeness to wrath; a third group is stopped for account. The author asserts that there is no contradiction among scriptural texts on this. He then presents three interpretations of 'stopping for account.' The first (attributed to al-Fakhr) holds that God creates necessary knowledge in the hearts. The second (from Ibn 'Abbas) involves showing the book of deeds and divine forgiveness and multiplication. The author criticizes this as insufficient because the account includes more, and limbs testify. The third (preferred) is that God speaks to them directly with His eternal speech, supported by authentic hadiths. The author adds that God's reckoning is simultaneous for all, yet each feels alone. Its modalities vary (easy, hard, secret, public, etc.) and its wisdom is to show differences in merit and deter evil. Finally, he glosses the line 'And there is no doubt concerning the truth' as affirming certainty of the truth.

Key Terms
سمعيات
حساب
توقيف
كلام قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The different interpretations of 'stopping' for account are contradictory and cannot be reconciled.
Correction: The author presents them as differing interpretations, not contradictions. The third view is supported by authentic hadiths, and the others are not dismissed outright but are evaluated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred interpretation of 'stopping people for their deeds'?
A) God creates necessary knowledge in hearts.
B) God shows them their books and forgives sins.
C) God speaks to them directly with His eternal speech.
D) God makes them forget their deeds.

Key Takeaway
God's reckoning is just and merciful; He speaks directly to each person with His eternal word, and no one is treated unfairly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to be stopped for a detailed reckoning right now, what specific deed would you be most ashamed to have exposed publicly? Will you repent from it today, or wait until it's too late?
?
The passage says God will speak to each person directly during the reckoning. If you heard God's voice addressing you about your life, what would surprise you most about what He says? How does that possibility change your priorities for tomorrow?
?
The reckoning can be easy or difficult. Based on your current habits of worship and sin, which do you honestly expect? What one change can you make today to tip the balance toward ease?
