The Two Groups on the Bridge: Safe and Perishing
Al-Bajuri differentiates between those who are safe from the fire and those who perish, including temporary perishing for sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two basic categories of people crossing the bridge (as-sirat) and the difference in their ultimate fate.

Core Idea
On the bridge, people are either saved from the fire or lost in it.

After establishing the reality of the bridge, Al-Bajuri explains that not everyone crosses it the same way. The poem's two phrases 'their passing is different' and 'one is safe and one is perishing' form the basis for a crucial distinction. This lesson unpacks that distinction, showing how believers and disbelievers, and even sinful believers, have different outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the two groups
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the contrast between 'salim' and 'multalif'.
2
Identify the two groups
Identify the two groups: those who are safe from the fire and those who perish by falling into it.
3
Understand the subcategories of perishing
Note that perishing can be eternal for disbelievers and hypocrites, or temporary for sinful believers who later are saved.
4
Recognize what qualifies as safe
The safe group includes those free from sins and those whose good deeds outweigh, specially favored by Allah.
5
Reflect on the principle
Consider how this distinction sets the stage for varying speeds of crossing, discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فالعِبادُ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُرُورُهُم) أي: إذا علمت أن الصراط واجب فاعلم أن العباد متفاوت مرورهم عليه في سرعة النجاة وعدمها فليسوا في المرور عليه على سواء. وقوله : (فَسَالِمٌ ومُنْتَلِفٌ) أي: فمنهم فريقٌ سالمٌ من الوقوع في نار جهنم، ومنهم فريقٌ مُنتلف بالوقوع فيها ؛ إما على الدوام والتأبيد كالكفار والمنافقين، وإما إلى مدة يريدها الله تعالى ثم ينجو كبعض عصاة المؤمنين ممن قضى الله عليهم بالعذاب والفريق الأوّل هم السالمون من السيئات وأهل رجحان الأعمال الصالحة ممن خصهم الله بسابقة الحسنى، وهؤلاء يجوزون كطرف العين وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالبرق الخاطف، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالريح العاصف، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالطير، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالجواد السابق، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون سعياً ومشياً، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون حبواً، وتفاوتهم في المرور بحسب تفاوتهم في الإعراض عن حرمات الله تعالى؛ فمن كان منهم أسرع إعراضاً عما حرَّم الله كان أسرع مروراً في ذلك اليوم، والحكمة في مرورهم على الصراط ظهور النجاة من النار، وأن يتحشَرَ الكفار بفوز المؤمنين بعد اشتراكهم في المرور.
His saying: 'So the servants, their passing is different' — i.e., when you know that the Bridge is obligatory, then know that the servants differ in their passing over it in speed of deliverance and lack thereof, so they are not equal in passing over it. And his saying: 'So one is safe and one is perishing' — i.e., among them is a group safe from falling into the Fire of Hell, and among them is a group perishing by falling into it, either permanently and eternally like the disbelievers and hypocrites, or for a period Allah wills then they are saved like some sinful believers whom Allah has decreed punishment. The first group are those safe from bad deeds and those whose good deeds outweigh, whom Allah has specially favored with a prior good fate. These pass like the blinking of an eye, then after them those who pass like a flash of lightning, then after them those who pass like a strong wind, then after them those who pass like a bird, then after them those who pass like a swift horse, then after them those who pass running and walking, then after them those who pass crawling. Their difference in passing is according to their difference in avoiding the prohibitions of Allah; so whoever among them is quicker in avoiding what Allah has forbidden is quicker in passing on that day. The wisdom in their passing over the Bridge is the manifestation of deliverance from the Fire, and that the disbelievers will be distressed by the success of the believers after their shared passing.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage explains the diversity in how people cross the bridge (as-sirat) based on their deeds. The author interprets the phrases from the original poem: 'the servants, their passing is different' and 'so one is safe and one is perishing.' It begins by asserting that since the bridge is an obligation of belief, one must know that people differ in speed of deliverance. There are two main groups: those safe from falling (salm) and those who fall (multalif). The perishing group includes eternal fall for disbelievers and hypocrites, and temporary fall for sinful believers who eventually are saved. The safe group comprises those free from sins and those with righteous deeds outweighing, favored by Allah. The passage then describes seven categories of crossing speed: like the blink of an eye, lightning, wind, bird, swift horse, running/walking, and crawling. The speed is directly proportional to how quickly each person avoided Allah's prohibitions (i.e., their level of piety). The wisdom behind crossing the bridge is to manifest deliverance from Hell and to cause distress to the disbelievers by witnessing the believers' success after both groups crossed together.

Key Terms
سالم
منتلف
الكفار والمنافقين
عصاة المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All believers cross the bridge without ever falling into the fire.
Correction: Some sinful believers fall into the fire for a period before being saved.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Bajuri, which two main groups are there among those crossing the bridge?
A) Fast and slow
B) Safe and perishing
C) Believers and disbelievers
D) Pious and sinful

Key Takeaway
On the bridge, people are divided into two groups: those safe from the fire and those who perish, with perishing being either eternal for disbelievers or temporary for sinful believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Considering that even some believers may fall temporarily into the Fire, what sins in your own life are you currently ignoring or minimizing, assuming Allah's mercy will cover them without consequence? What will you do today to sincerely repent and change?
?
On the Day of Judgment, if Allah were to judge you according to your deeds alone without His mercy, would you be among the safe or the perishing? Be honest: are you living in a way that reflects the reality of this crossing, or have you become complacent?
?
The passage describes the perishing group as including those who fall 'for a period Allah wills then are saved.' Does knowing that Allah alone determines that period give you comfort or fear? How should this affect the urgency of your obedience and the sincerity of your reliance on His mercy?

The Seven Speeds of Crossing and the Wisdom of the Bridge
Al-Bajuri enumerates seven speeds of crossing and explains that they correspond to one's avoidance of sins, concluding with the wisdom of the bridge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the speed of crossing the bridge varies according to one's avoidance of sins and the wisdom behind this test.

Core Idea
The quicker you avoid sin, the quicker you cross the bridge.

After establishing the two basic categories, Al-Bajuri elaborates on the safe group by describing seven different speeds of crossing, from the blink of an eye to crawling. This lesson explores these speeds and the principle that they correspond to how quickly a person avoided Allah's prohibitions. The wisdom underlying the entire crossing is also revealed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing the seven speeds
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting the sequence of comparisons.
2
Note the first speed
The most pious cross like the blink of an eye — this sets the fastest pace.
3
Identify the sequence from fastest to slowest
Find each speed: blink, lightning, wind, bird, swift horse, running/walking, crawling.
4
Understand the principle
Speed depends on how quickly one avoided Allah's prohibitions; faster avoidance leads to faster crossing.
5
Grasp the wisdom
The bridge manifests deliverance from the fire and causes disbelievers distress by witnessing the believers' success.

The Reality and Evidence of the Sirat
Defines the sirat, its evidence, and differences of interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the sirat is a literal bridge over Hell, affirmed by Quran and Sunnah, and that Ahl al-Sunnah take it literally while the Mu'tazila interpret it metaphorically.

Core Idea
The sirat is a real bridge, not just a symbol.

This lesson introduces one of the key 'heard matters' (al-sam'iyyat): the sirat, the bridge stretched over Hell. The passage grounds belief in the sirat through Quranic verse and prophetic hadith, and clarifies the difference between the Sunni literal acceptance and the Mu'tazilite metaphorical interpretation. As you read, focus on the evidence and the two main views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the sirat's reality
Start with the Arabic text from 'السمعيات' to the end of the angel description. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Sha'rani's statement sets the tone.
The passage begins by citing al-Sha'rani that one cannot reach the true reality but only its meadow.
2
Identify the Quranic and hadith evidence
Find the verse (36:66) and the hadith about the sirat stretched between the sides of Hell. Notice that the hadith emphasizes the Prophet and his community being first to cross.
The evidence is presented compactly.
3
Compare the two interpretations
The passage notes agreement on the sirat in general, but a disagreement: Ahl al-Sunnah keep it literal; many Mu'tazila interpret it as the road to Paradise and Hell. There is also an opinion that it refers to clear proofs with angels questioning.
This shows the importance of adhering to the literal meaning according to Sunni theology.

العباد متفاوت مرورهم عليه في سرعة النجاة ،وعدمها فليسوا في المرور عليه على
سواء.
وقوله : (فَسَالِمٌ ومُنْتَلِفٌ) أي: فمنهم فريقٌ سالمٌ من الوقوع في نار جهنم، ومنهم فريقٌ مُنتلف بالوقوع فيها ؛ إما على الدوام والتأبيد كالكفار والمنافقين، وإما إلى مدة يريدها الله تعالى ثم ينجو كبعض عصاة المؤمنين ممن قضى الله عليهم بالعذاب والفريق الأوّل هم السالمون من السيئات وأهل رجحان الأعمال الصالحة ممَّن خصهم الله بسابقة الحسنى، وهؤلاء يجوزون كطرف العين وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالبرق الخاطف، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالريح العاصف، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالطير، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون كالجواد السابق، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون سعياً ومشياً، وبعدهم الذين يجوزون حبواً، وتفاوتهم في المرور بحسب تفاوتهم في الإعراض عن حرمات الله تعالى؛ فمن كان منهم أسرع إعراضاً عما حرَّم الله كان أسرع مروراً في ذلك اليوم، والحكمة في مرورهم على الصراط ظهور النجاة من النار، وأن يتحشَرَ الكفار بفوز المؤمنين بعد اشتراكهم في المرور.
The matters heard (al-sam'iyyat). And al-Sha'rani stated that one does not arrive at its reality, rather one arrives at its meadow which contains the descending stairway leading to it. He said: And a table is placed for them there. He said: And one of them stands and takes from what dangles there of the fruits of Paradise. And the Book has reported it: Almighty said: 'Then they raced to the path' (Ya Sin 66). And the Sunnah: He said: 'The sirat is stretched between the two sides of Hell, and I and my community will be the first to cross it.' And the word agreed upon it in general; that is, irrespective of keeping it upon its apparent meaning as is the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah, or interpreting it away from it, as is the madhhab of many of the Mu'tazila; for they went that what is meant by it is the road to Paradise and the road to Hell. And it was said: What is meant by it is the clear proofs, and Jibril at its beginning and Mika'il at its middle, asking people about their lifespan in what they spent it, and about their youth in what they [؟] used it, and about their knowledge what they acted upon it, and on its sides are hooks suspended, commanded to take whom they are commanded. His saying: 'So the servants differ in their passage' meaning: If you know that the sirat is obligatory, then know that the servants vary in their passage upon it in the speed of salvation and its absence, so they are not equal in passing upon it. And His saying: 'So a safe one and a perishing one' meaning: There is a group safe from falling into the fire of Hell, and a group perishing by falling into it; either permanently and eternally like the disbelievers and hypocrites, or for a period that Allah Almighty wants then they escape, like some of the disobedient believers whom Allah has decreed punishment upon. And the first group are those safe from evil deeds and the people of preponderance of righteous deeds whom Allah has distinguished with the prior favor. These pass like the blink of an eye; after them those who pass like the flashing lightning; after them those who pass like the violent wind; after them those who pass like the bird; after them those who pass like the swift horse; after them those who pass running and walking; after them those who pass crawling. And their variance in passage is according to their variance in turning away from the sanctities of Allah Almighty; so whoever among them was quicker in turning away from what Allah has forbidden was quicker in passage on that day. And the wisdom in their passage upon the sirat is the manifestation of salvation from the Fire, and that the disbelievers will be distressed by the success of the believers after their sharing in the passage.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is part of al-sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation) and discusses the sirat (the bridge over Hell). It begins by citing al-Sha'rani's statement that one cannot reach its true reality but rather arrives at its meadow. Then it provides evidence from the Quran (36:66) and Sunnah (the hadith that the sirat is stretched between the sides of Hell and the Prophet will be the first to cross with his community). The passage notes that there is general agreement on the sirat's existence, though there is disagreement on interpretation: Ahl al-Sunnah take it literally, while many Mu'tazila interpret it as the road to Paradise and Hell. Another opinion says it refers to clear proofs, with angels at its ends questioning people about their lives. The commentary then explains a line from the poem: 'So the servants differ in their passage,' meaning people vary in speed of crossing. Another line: 'So a safe one and a perishing one' divides people into two groups: those who are safe from falling into Hell (the righteous) and those who fall (disbelievers, hypocrites, and some sinful believers who will be punished for a time). The passage then describes seven categories of people based on the speed of their crossing, from those who cross like the blink of an eye to those who crawl. The speed is according to how quickly they turned away from forbidden things. The wisdom behind crossing the sirat is to manifest salvation and to cause the disbelievers to grieve at the success of the believers.

Key Terms
السمعيات
الصراط
المسألة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sirat is only a metaphor or a figurative representation of one's deeds.
Correction: The passage affirms the sirat as a literal bridge that will be physically placed over Hell, based on Quran and Sunnah, and Ahl al-Sunnah adhere to its apparent meaning.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding the sirat?
A) They interpret it as the road to Paradise and Hell.
B) They keep it upon its apparent meaning as a literal bridge.
C) They say it refers to clear proofs.
D) They deny its existence.

Key Takeaway
The sirat is a literal bridge over Hell, affirmed by Quran and Sunnah, and Ahl al-Sunnah accept its apparent meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you stand before Jibril and Mika'il on the sirat and are asked about your lifespan, your youth, and your knowledge, what will you answer? What have you actually spent these gifts on today?
?
The hooks on the sirat are commanded to take specific people. Are you living today as one who will be snatched away by those hooks, or as one who will cross to Paradise? What change must you make right now to be among the saved?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) will be the first to cross, but only with his community. Do you have any guarantee that you are truly part of his community in heart and deed, or are you simply assuming it while your actions say otherwise?

The Varying States of Crossing the Sirat
Describes the varying speeds of crossing the sirat and their causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that people cross the sirat at different speeds according to their piety, and that the crossing manifests salvation for believers and distress for disbelievers.

Core Idea
Crossing speed reflects one's turning away from sin.

Having established the reality of the sirat, this lesson focuses on how people actually cross it. The passage describes seven categories of people based on crossing speed, from the blink of an eye to crawling, and links this speed to how quickly they turned away from forbidden things. The wisdom behind the crossing is also explained.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the varying passage
Read from 'قوله : (فالعِبادُ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُرُورُهُم)' to the end. Notice the phrase 'فالعِبادُ مُخْتَلِفٌ مُرُورُهُم' and how the commentary unpacks it.
This part is a commentary on lines from the poem.
2
Identify the two main groups: safe and perishing
The passage divides people into a group safe from falling into Hell (the righteous) and a group that falls (disbelievers, hypocrites, and sinful believers who are punished temporarily).
3
List the seven categories of crossing speed
Find the seven descriptions: blink of an eye, lightning, wind, bird, swift horse, running/walking, crawling. Understand that these are metaphorical comparisons.
The order is from fastest to slowest.
4
Understand the cause and wisdom
The passage states that the speed of crossing is according to how quickly one turned away from Allah's sanctities. The wisdom is to manifest salvation and make the disbelievers grieved at the believers' success.

?
Imagine yourself on the sirat. What specific sin in your life are you most hesitant to abandon, and what does that tell you about your crossing speed?
?

How long did it take you to turn away? Did you hesitate, dwell, or indulge? What will you do today to shorten that hesitation so your crossing is faster?
?
One group crosses 'like the blink of an eye.' Can you honestly say you desire that speed more than you desire the sin you are clinging to? If your answer convicts you, what concrete step will you take this week to 'turn away' faster from that particular prohibition?

Belief in the Throne (al-Arsh)
Defines the Throne and its attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Throne as described in Sunni theology and the importance of refraining from dogmatic specification of its substance.

Core Idea
The Throne is a luminous dome above the world, carried by angels, not spherical.

Sanusi explains the obligation to believe in the Throne, one of the greatest creations. He describes its physical attributes and warns against being overly confident about its exact substance, as true knowledge belongs to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the poem line first, then the detailed commentary on the Throne.
The passage begins with the obligation of belief in the five entities, then focuses on the Throne.
2
Identify key descriptions
List the descriptions given for the Throne: its substance (light, chrysolite, ruby), shape (dome, not spherical), pillars, and the angels carrying it.
3
Understand the advice to refrain
The commentator advises against being decisive about the Throne's exact reality. Why? Because we lack certain knowledge.
This principle of refraining from dogmatism appears repeatedly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ الإيمان بالعرشِ والكرسي والقلم والكاتبينَ واللوح
۱۰۷ - والعَرْسُ والكُرْسِيُّ ثُمَّ القَلَمُ وَالكَاتِبُونَ اللَّوْحُ كُلّ حِكَمُ
قوله : (والعَرْشُ) وهو جسم عظيمٌ نوراني علوي .
(1).
1
قيل : من نور، وقيل: من زبرجدة خضراء، وقيل: من ياقوتة حمراء، والأولى الإمساك عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته ؛ لعدم العلم بها والتحقيق أنه ليس كرويا، بل هو قبَّةٌ فوق العالم، ذات أعمدة أربعة تحمله الملائكة؛ في الدنيا أربعة، الدنيا أربعةٌ، وفي الآخرة ثمانٍ لزيادة الجلال والعظمة في الآخرة ) ، رؤوسهم عند العرش في السماء السابعة، وأقدامهم في الأرض السفلى، وقرونهم كقرون الوعل ؛ أي بقر الوحش ما بين أصل قرن أحدهم إلى منتهاه خمس مئة عام . وقيل : إنه كروي محيط بجميع الأجسام، وهذا خلاف التحقيق.
وقوله : ( الكُرْسِيُّ) معطوف على العرش، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني تحت العرش ملتصق به به، فوق السماء السابعة، بينه وبينها مسيرة خمس مئة عام، كما نقل عن ابن ،عباس والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته لعدم العلم بها، وهو غير العرش خلافاً للحسن البصري. وقوله : (ثُمَّ القَلَمُ) معطوف على الكرسي، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني خلقه الله ، وأمره بكتب ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، قيل: هو من اليراع؛ وهو القَصَب؛ والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته .
وقوله : (وَالكَاتِنُونَ) معطوف على القلم، وأقسامهم ثلاثة :
الكاتبونَ على العباد أعمالهم في الدنيا .
والكاتبونَ من اللوح المحفوظ ما في صحف الملائكة الموكلين بالتصرف في العالم
كُل عام.
والكاتبون من صحف الملائكة كتاباً يُوضع تحت العرش.
وقوله : (اللَّوْحُ) معطوف على ما قبله بتقدير حرف العطف، فهو مرفوع، وليس
(1) قال تعالى: ﴿وَعَمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَذٍ غَنِيَةٌ ) [الْحَاقَّة: ١٧] .
The obligation of belief in the Throne (al-arsh), and the Footstool (al-kursi), then the Pen (al-qalam), and the Writers (al-katibun), the Tablet (al-lawh), all are wisdom. His saying: (And the Throne) and it is a great luminous heavenly body. (1). 1 It was said: of light, and it was said: of green chrysolite, and it was said: of red ruby, and the better course is to refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality due to lack of knowledge of it. And the verified truth is that it is not spherical, rather it is a dome above the world, having four pillars which the angels carry; in this world four, in this world four, and in the Hereafter eight, for increase of majesty and grandeur in the Hereafter. Their heads are at the Throne in the seventh heaven, and their feet in the lowest earth, and their horns like the horns of the mountain goat; that is, the wild ox, between the base of a horn of one of them and its end is five hundred years. And it was said: It is spherical encompassing all bodies, and this is contrary to the verified truth. And His saying: (The Footstool) is conjoined to the Throne, and it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne attached to it, above the seventh heaven, between it and it is a distance of five hundred years' journey, as transmitted from Ibn Abbas. And the better course is that we refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality due to lack of knowledge of it, and it is other than the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan al-Basri. And His saying: (Then the Pen) is conjoined to the Footstool, and it is a great luminous body which Allah created and commanded to write what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection. It was said: it is of the reed; that is, the cane; and the better course is that we refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality. And His saying: (And the Writers) is conjoined to the Pen, and their categories are three: The writers upon the servants their deeds in this world. And the writers from the Preserved Tablet what is in the scrolls of the angels entrusted with disposal in the world every year. And the writers from the scrolls of the angels a book which is placed beneath the Throne. And His saying: (The Tablet) is conjoined to what precedes by supplying the conjunction, so it is nominative, and not ... (1) Almighty said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that day by eight [angels]' (Al-Haqqah 17).
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation of belief in five created entities mentioned in the poem line: al-arsh (the Throne), al-kursi (the Footstool), al-qalam (the Pen), al-katibun (the Writers), and al-lawh (the Tablet). The commentator defines each. For the Throne: it is a great luminous heavenly body, not spherical but a dome above the world with four pillars carried by angels (four in this world, eight in the Hereafter). He mentions various opinions about its substance (light, chrysolite, ruby) but advises refraining from definitive specification due to lack of knowledge. For the Footstool: it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne, above the seventh heaven, five hundred years away, and distinct from the Throne. For the Pen: it is a great luminous body created by Allah and commanded to write all that will happen until the Day of Judgment. For the Writers: they are divided into three categories: those who record deeds, those who transcribe from the Preserved Tablet into the scrolls of angels managing the world, and those who write a book placed under the Throne. For the Tablet: it is conjoined to the previous items. The passage emphasizes refraining from being dogmatic about the exact nature of these entities, as their true reality is not fully known to humans.

Key Terms
العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Throne is spherical.
Correction: The Throne is a dome above the world, not spherical.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many pillars does the Throne have, and how many angels carry it in the Hereafter?
A) Four pillars, eight angels
B) Eight pillars, four angels
C) Four pillars, four angels
D) Eight pillars, eight angels

Key Takeaway
The Throne is a great luminous dome above the world, not spherical, and we should not be dogmatic about its substance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author advises us to refrain from being decisive about the reality of the Throne due to lack of knowledge. Is there an area of your faith where you have been overly confident in your own speculation rather than submitting to what has been revealed? What would it mean for you to adopt a posture of intellectual humility before the unseen?
?
The angels carry the Throne with immense size and strength, yet they are utterly obedient to Allah. How does the reality of creatures greater than you in power and devotion challenge your own pride or your excuses for not submitting fully to Allah?
?
The source tells us that the Throne is a dome above the world, not spherical. This is a truth we accept without sensory evidence. In what areas of your life are you tempted to demand sensory proof before believing? How might this lesson call you to trust Allah's word over your own perception?

Belief in the Footstool (al-Kursi)
Describes the Footstool and its distinction from the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Footstool and that it is distinct from the Throne.

Core Idea
The Footstool is beneath the Throne, a great luminous body, distinct from it.

After describing the Throne, Sanusi turns to the Footstool. He clarifies its position and warns against confusing it with the Throne, as some have done.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the Footstool. Note that it is conjoined to the Throne.
2
Identify key details
Find where the Footstool is located: beneath the Throne, above the seventh heaven, five hundred years away.
3
Understand the distinction
The commentator emphasizes that the Footstool is other than the Throne, contrary to Hasan al-Basri's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ الإيمان بالعرشِ والكرسي والقلم والكاتبينَ واللوح
۱۰۷ - والعَرْسُ والكُرْسِيُّ ثُمَّ القَلَمُ وَالكَاتِبُونَ اللَّوْحُ كُلّ حِكَمُ
قوله : (والعَرْشُ) وهو جسم عظيمٌ نوراني علوي .
(1).
1
قيل : من نور، وقيل: من زبرجدة خضراء، وقيل: من ياقوتة حمراء، والأولى الإمساك عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته ؛ لعدم العلم بها والتحقيق أنه ليس كرويا، بل هو قبَّةٌ فوق العالم، ذات أعمدة أربعة تحمله الملائكة؛ في الدنيا أربعة، الدنيا أربعةٌ، وفي الآخرة ثمانٍ لزيادة الجلال والعظمة في الآخرة ) ، رؤوسهم عند العرش في السماء السابعة، وأقدامهم في الأرض السفلى، وقرونهم كقرون الوعل ؛ أي بقر الوحش ما بين أصل قرن أحدهم إلى منتهاه خمس مئة عام . وقيل : إنه كروي محيط بجميع الأجسام، وهذا خلاف التحقيق.
وقوله : ( الكُرْسِيُّ) معطوف على العرش، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني تحت العرش ملتصق به به، فوق السماء السابعة، بينه وبينها مسيرة خمس مئة عام، كما نقل عن ابن ،عباس والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته لعدم العلم بها، وهو غير العرش خلافاً للحسن البصري. وقوله : (ثُمَّ القَلَمُ) معطوف على الكرسي، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني خلقه الله ، وأمره بكتب ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، قيل: هو من اليراع؛ وهو القَصَب؛ والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته .
وقوله : (وَالكَاتِنُونَ) معطوف على القلم، وأقسامهم ثلاثة :
الكاتبونَ على العباد أعمالهم في الدنيا .
والكاتبونَ من اللوح المحفوظ ما في صحف الملائكة الموكلين بالتصرف في العالم
كُل عام.
والكاتبون من صحف الملائكة كتاباً يُوضع تحت العرش.
وقوله : (اللَّوْحُ) معطوف على ما قبله بتقدير حرف العطف، فهو مرفوع، وليس
(1) قال تعالى: ﴿وَعَمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَذٍ غَنِيَةٌ ) [الْحَاقَّة: ١٧] .
The obligation of belief in the Throne (al-arsh), and the Footstool (al-kursi), then the Pen (al-qalam), and the Writers (al-katibun), the Tablet (al-lawh), all are wisdom. His saying: (And the Throne) and it is a great luminous heavenly body. (1). 1 It was said: of light, and it was said: of green chrysolite, and it was said: of red ruby, and the better course is to refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality due to lack of knowledge of it. And the verified truth is that it is not spherical, rather it is a dome above the world, having four pillars which the angels carry; in this world four, in this world four, and in the Hereafter eight, for increase of majesty and grandeur in the Hereafter. Their heads are at the Throne in the seventh heaven, and their feet in the lowest earth, and their horns like the horns of the mountain goat; that is, the wild ox, between the base of a horn of one of them and its end is five hundred years. And it was said: It is spherical encompassing all bodies, and this is contrary to the verified truth. And His saying: (The Footstool) is conjoined to the Throne, and it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne attached to it, above the seventh heaven, between it and it is a distance of five hundred years' journey, as transmitted from Ibn Abbas. And the better course is that we refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality due to lack of knowledge of it, and it is other than the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan al-Basri. And His saying: (Then the Pen) is conjoined to the Footstool, and it is a great luminous body which Allah created and commanded to write what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection. It was said: it is of the reed; that is, the cane; and the better course is that we refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality. And His saying: (And the Writers) is conjoined to the Pen, and their categories are three: The writers upon the servants their deeds in this world. And the writers from the Preserved Tablet what is in the scrolls of the angels entrusted with disposal in the world every year. And the writers from the scrolls of the angels a book which is placed beneath the Throne. And His saying: (The Tablet) is conjoined to what precedes by supplying the conjunction, so it is nominative, and not ... (1) Almighty said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that day by eight [angels]' (Al-Haqqah 17).
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation of belief in five created entities mentioned in the poem line: al-arsh (the Throne), al-kursi (the Footstool), al-qalam (the Pen), al-katibun (the Writers), and al-lawh (the Tablet). The commentator defines each. For the Throne: it is a great luminous heavenly body, not spherical but a dome above the world with four pillars carried by angels (four in this world, eight in the Hereafter). He mentions various opinions about its substance (light, chrysolite, ruby) but advises refraining from definitive specification due to lack of knowledge. For the Footstool: it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne, above the seventh heaven, five hundred years away, and distinct from the Throne. For the Pen: it is a great luminous body created by Allah and commanded to write all that will happen until the Day of Judgment. For the Writers: they are divided into three categories: those who record deeds, those who transcribe from the Preserved Tablet into the scrolls of angels managing the world, and those who write a book placed under the Throne. For the Tablet: it is conjoined to the previous items. The passage emphasizes refraining from being dogmatic about the exact nature of these entities, as their true reality is not fully known to humans.

Key Terms
الكرسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Footstool is the same as the Throne.
Correction: The Footstool is distinct, beneath the Throne.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where is the Footstool located?
A) Above the Throne
B) Beneath the Throne, above the seventh heaven
C) On the earth
D) Inside the Throne

Key Takeaway
The Footstool is a great luminous body beneath the Throne, distinct from it, and we should not be dogmatic about its exact nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to accept that there are truths about Allah's creation that you will never fully understand in this life? Does this realization humble you or frustrate you, and how will you respond today?
?
When you encounter a matter of the unseen that scholars disagree on, do you rush to take a definitive position, or do you practice restraint like the author advises? What would change in your approach if you truly adopted this attitude?
?
The Footstool's reality is unknown to us, yet it is mentioned in the Qur'an. How does your belief in the unseen affect your daily life? Do you live as if these realities are merely theoretical, or do they shape a deeper consciousness of Allah's greatness in your heart right now?

beginner
4 min
Belief in the Pen (al-Qalam)
Defines the Pen and its purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Pen and its role in recording divine decrees.

Core Idea
The Pen is a luminous body created to write all that will happen until Judgment Day.

Sanusi now discusses the Pen, a created entity commissioned to inscribe destiny. He again advises caution in defining its substance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the Pen. Note it is conjoined to the Footstool.
2
Understand its function
The Pen is commanded to write everything that was and will be until the Day of Resurrection. This is its key role.
3
Note the advice to refrain
Again, the commentator advises refraining from being decisive about its reality, as with the previous entities.

Source Text

Checkpoint
What is the primary function of the Pen according to the passage?
A) To write the deeds of angels
B) To write all that was and will be until Judgment Day
C) To write only the Quran
D) To write the laws of nature

Key Takeaway
The Pen is a luminous creation of Allah, tasked with writing everything that occurs until the Day of Resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every event in your life until the Day of Resurrection has already been written by the Pen, how does that change the way you respond to trials and blessings? What one area of your life do you need to surrender to Allah's decree today?
?
Knowing that the Pen is a real created entity, not just a metaphor, do you treat the unseen realities of the Unseen with the same certainty as the visible? What step will you take this week to strengthen your conviction in the sam‘iyyat?
?
The scholars advise us not to be decisive about the exact nature of the Pen. Is there an aspect of your faith where you are trying to know too much, instead of accepting the limits of human knowledge? How can you practice restraint and trust in Allah's wisdom starting now?

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
Belief in the Writers (al-Katibun)
Enumerates three categories of writers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of writers (angels) and their roles.

Core Idea
There are three categories of writers: recorders of deeds, annual transcribers, and those who write a book under the Throne.

Sanusi details the writers, who are angels with specific duties. He enumerates three types, each with a distinct function in the divine decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the Writers. Notice the three categories enumerated.
2
Identify the three categories
List each category: 1) writers of deeds, 2) annual transcribers from the Preserved Tablet, 3) compilers of a book under the Throne.
3
Understand the hierarchy
Note that each category has a different function and source material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many categories of writers are mentioned in the passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
There are three distinct groups of angelic writers, each with a specific function in recording divine decrees.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe that angels are recording your every deed. Does that belief actually change what you do in private moments when no human sees? If not, why not, and what would it take for you to live with that awareness today?
?
The angels transcribe your destiny for each year from the Preserved Tablet. Knowing that your provision, lifespan, and actions are already written, does that make you feel helpless or accountable? How will you respond to that knowledge right now?
?
A book containing the records of all deeds is placed beneath the Throne. When you stand before your Lord, will that book be a source of honor or regret? What is one thing you can change today to make it a book of success?

Belief in the Tablet (al-Lawh)
Mentions the Tablet and advises refraining from dogmatism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in the Tablet as a created entity mentioned in the poem.

Core Idea
The Tablet is a created entity, conjoined to the other items, and its reality is beyond full human knowledge.

Sanusi concludes the list with the Tablet, affirming belief in it as a wisdom from Allah. He provides no detailed description, emphasizing the need to refrain from dogmatic claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the Tablet. Note it is very brief and mainly grammatical.
2
Understand the principle
As with other entities, the commentator does not specify the Tablet's nature. This reinforces the lesson of refraining from speculation.
3
Connect to the overall lesson
The Tablet completes the set of five entities all Muslims must believe in without delving into their exact realities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ الإيمان بالعرشِ والكرسي والقلم والكاتبينَ واللوح
۱۰۷ - والعَرْسُ والكُرْسِيُّ ثُمَّ القَلَمُ وَالكَاتِبُونَ اللَّوْحُ كُلّ حِكَمُ
قوله : (والعَرْشُ) وهو جسم عظيمٌ نوراني علوي .
(1).
1
قيل : من نور، وقيل: من زبرجدة خضراء، وقيل: من ياقوتة حمراء، والأولى الإمساك عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته ؛ لعدم العلم بها والتحقيق أنه ليس كرويا، بل هو قبَّةٌ فوق العالم، ذات أعمدة أربعة تحمله الملائكة؛ في الدنيا أربعة، الدنيا أربعةٌ، وفي الآخرة ثمانٍ لزيادة الجلال والعظمة في الآخرة ) ، رؤوسهم عند العرش في السماء السابعة، وأقدامهم في الأرض السفلى، وقرونهم كقرون الوعل ؛ أي بقر الوحش ما بين أصل قرن أحدهم إلى منتهاه خمس مئة عام . وقيل : إنه كروي محيط بجميع الأجسام، وهذا خلاف التحقيق.
وقوله : ( الكُرْسِيُّ) معطوف على العرش، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني تحت العرش ملتصق به به، فوق السماء السابعة، بينه وبينها مسيرة خمس مئة عام، كما نقل عن ابن ،عباس والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته لعدم العلم بها، وهو غير العرش خلافاً للحسن البصري. وقوله : (ثُمَّ القَلَمُ) معطوف على الكرسي، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني خلقه الله ، وأمره بكتب ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، قيل: هو من اليراع؛ وهو القَصَب؛ والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته .
وقوله : (وَالكَاتِنُونَ) معطوف على القلم، وأقسامهم ثلاثة :
الكاتبونَ على العباد أعمالهم في الدنيا .
والكاتبونَ من اللوح المحفوظ ما في صحف الملائكة الموكلين بالتصرف في العالم
كُل عام.
والكاتبون من صحف الملائكة كتاباً يُوضع تحت العرش.
وقوله : (اللَّوْحُ) معطوف على ما قبله بتقدير حرف العطف، فهو مرفوع، وليس
(1) قال تعالى: ﴿وَعَمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَذٍ غَنِيَةٌ ) [الْحَاقَّة: ١٧] .
The obligation of belief in the Throne (al-arsh), and the Footstool (al-kursi), then the Pen (al-qalam), and the Writers (al-katibun), the Tablet (al-lawh), all are wisdom. His saying: (And the Throne) and it is a great luminous heavenly body. (1). 1 It was said: of light, and it was said: of green chrysolite, and it was said: of red ruby, and the better course is to refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality due to lack of knowledge of it. And the verified truth is that it is not spherical, rather it is a dome above the world, having four pillars which the angels carry; in this world four, in this world four, and in the Hereafter eight, for increase of majesty and grandeur in the Hereafter. Their heads are at the Throne in the seventh heaven, and their feet in the lowest earth, and their horns like the horns of the mountain goat; that is, the wild ox, between the base of a horn of one of them and its end is five hundred years. And it was said: It is spherical encompassing all bodies, and this is contrary to the verified truth. And His saying: (The Footstool) is conjoined to the Throne, and it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne attached to it, above the seventh heaven, between it and it is a distance of five hundred years' journey, as transmitted from Ibn Abbas. And the better course is that we refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality due to lack of knowledge of it, and it is other than the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan al-Basri. And His saying: (Then the Pen) is conjoined to the Footstool, and it is a great luminous body which Allah created and commanded to write what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection. It was said: it is of the reed; that is, the cane; and the better course is that we refrain from being decisive in specifying its reality. And His saying: (And the Writers) is conjoined to the Pen, and their categories are three: The writers upon the servants their deeds in this world. And the writers from the Preserved Tablet what is in the scrolls of the angels entrusted with disposal in the world every year. And the writers from the scrolls of the angels a book which is placed beneath the Throne. And His saying: (The Tablet) is conjoined to what precedes by supplying the conjunction, so it is nominative, and not ... (1) Almighty said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that day by eight [angels]' (Al-Haqqah 17).
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation of belief in five created entities mentioned in the poem line: al-arsh (the Throne), al-kursi (the Footstool), al-qalam (the Pen), al-katibun (the Writers), and al-lawh (the Tablet). The commentator defines each. For the Throne: it is a great luminous heavenly body, not spherical but a dome above the world with four pillars carried by angels (four in this world, eight in the Hereafter). He mentions various opinions about its substance (light, chrysolite, ruby) but advises refraining from definitive specification due to lack of knowledge. For the Footstool: it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne, above the seventh heaven, five hundred years away, and distinct from the Throne. For the Pen: it is a great luminous body created by Allah and commanded to write all that will happen until the Day of Judgment. For the Writers: they are divided into three categories: those who record deeds, those who transcribe from the Preserved Tablet into the scrolls of angels managing the world, and those who write a book placed under the Throne. For the Tablet: it is conjoined to the previous items. The passage emphasizes refraining from being dogmatic about the exact nature of these entities, as their true reality is not fully known to humans.

Key Terms
اللوح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the Tablet?
A) It is the same as the Preserved Tablet
B) It is conjoined to the previous items and we should not be dogmatic
C) It is made of emerald
D) It is carried by angels

Key Takeaway
The Tablet is a created entity that we must believe in, but its exact nature is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truly at peace with the fact that the exact nature of the Tablet is known only to Allah, or does your heart secretly wish to uncover more than He has revealed?
?
Where in your daily life do you find yourself speculating about the unseen matters beyond what Allah has disclosed? Will you consciously restrain that urge as this lesson advises?
?
When you think about the Tablet containing all that will happen, does it fill you with trust in Allah's decree or with anxiety? What does your reaction reveal about your faith?

The Throne and the Footstool: Descriptions and Proper Attitude
Commentator defines and describes the Throne and Footstool, presents variant views, and recommends withholding certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the descriptions of the Throne and Footstool according to the commentator, the different opinions about their nature, and the recommended attitude of withholding definitive judgment when knowledge is lacking.

Core Idea
In matters of the unseen, the best course is often to refrain from certainty when revelation is ambiguous.

The Throne and Footstool are two major entities mentioned in the Quran and hadith. Scholars have offered various descriptions, but the commentator advises caution. In this lesson, we explore what is said about them and why it is better not to claim certainty about their exact nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the content. Note the key terms: العرش and الكرسي.
2
Identify the descriptions and opinions
Look for the different opinions about the substance of the Throne (light, chrysolite, ruby) and the two views on its shape (dome vs. sphere). Also note the description of the angels carrying it.
The commentator rejects the spherical view.
3
Understand the proper attitude
Notice that the commentator twice advises to refrain from definitively determining the reality of these entities due to lack of knowledge. This is a key methodological point in theology of the unseen.
This attitude is recommended for both the Throne and the Footstool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعَرْشُ) وهو جسم عظيمٌ نوراني علوي . قال تعالى: ﴿وَعَمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَذٍ غَنِيَةٌ ) [الْحَاقَّة: ١٧]. قيل : من نور، وقيل: من زبرجدة خضراء، وقيل: من ياقوتة حمراء، والأولى الإمساك عن القطع بتعيين حقيقته ؛ لعدم العلم بها والتحقيق أنه ليس كرويا، بل هو قبَّةٌ فوق العالم، ذات أعمدة أربعة تحمله الملائكة؛ في الدنيا أربعة، الدنيا أربعةٌ، وفي الآخرة ثمانٍ لزيادة الجلال والعظمة في الآخرة ) ، رؤوسهم عند العرش في السماء السابعة، وأقدامهم في الأرض السفلى، وقرونهم كقرون الوعل ؛ أي بقر الوحش ما بين أصل قرن أحدهم إلى منتهاه خمس مئة عام . وقيل : إنه كروي محيط بجميع الأجسام، وهذا خلاف التحقيق. وقوله : ( والكُرْسِيُّ) معطوف على العرش، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني تحت العرش ملتصق به به، فوق السماء السابعة، بينه وبينها مسيرة خمس مئة عام، كما نقل عن ابن ،عباس والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته لعدم العلم بها، وهو غير العرش خلافاً للحسن البصري.
His saying: 'And the Throne' — and it is a great luminous body above. The Exalted said: 'And the throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that day' [Surah Al-Haqqah: 17]. It is said: of light, and said: of green chrysolite, and said: of red ruby, and the best is to refrain from definitively determining its reality due to lack of knowledge of it. The verified truth is that it is not spherical, but rather a dome above the world, having four pillars that the angels carry; in this world four, in the Hereafter eight due to the increase of majesty and greatness in the Hereafter. Their heads are at the Throne in the seventh heaven, their feet in the lowest earth, and their horns like the horns of the mountain goat; meaning wild cows, between the base of one of their horns to its tip is five hundred years. And it is said: It is spherical encompassing all bodies, and this is contrary to the verified truth. And his saying: 'And the Footstool' is conjoined to the Throne, and it is a great luminous body beneath the Throne attached to it, above the seventh heaven, between it and it is a journey of five hundred years, as transmitted from Ibn Abbas. And the best is to refrain from definitively determining its reality due to lack of knowledge of it, and it is other than the Throne contrary to al-Hasan al-Basri.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage defines and explains two entities mentioned in the poem: the Throne and the Footstool. The commentator first describes the Throne as a great luminous body. He mentions multiple opinions about its substance (light, chrysolite, ruby) but advises against claiming certainty about its true reality due to lack of knowledge. He then affirms the verified opinion: it is not a sphere but a dome-shaped structure above the world, supported by four pillars, carried by angels—four in this world and eight in the afterlife. He provides detailed descriptions of the angels carrying it. He also reports a conflicting view that it is spherical, but rejects this. For the Footstool, he states it is a luminous body beneath the Throne and attached to it, above the seventh heaven, with a distance of 500 years. He again advises withholding judgment about its precise nature and clarifies that it is distinct from the Throne, contrary to al-Hasan al-Basri's view. The passage emphasizes the proper approach of not being dogmatic about unseen realities when textual evidence is ambiguous.

Key Terms
العرش
الكرسي
جسم عظيم
نوراني
قبَّة
أعمدة
الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Throne is a sphere or that the Footstool is the same as the Throne.
Correction: The commentator states that the verified truth is that the Throne is a dome, not a sphere, and that the Footstool is a separate entity beneath the Throne.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the correct description of the Throne?
A) A sphere encompassing all bodies
B) A dome above the world with four pillars
C) A flat surface
D) The seventh heaven

Key Takeaway
The Throne is a dome-shaped luminous body above the world, and the Footstool is a separate luminous body beneath it; we should not claim certainty about their exact nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a matter of the unseen that Allah has not made clear, like the exact nature of the Throne, do you feel comfortable saying 'I do not know'? Or do you cling to a specific opinion for security? What would it cost you to admit uncertainty on such matters, and are you willing to pay that price starting today?
?
The commentator advises withholding certainty out of humility for our limited knowledge. Is there an area in your faith where you have been overconfident about something you cannot prove? Will you repent and adopt a posture of 'I entrust its true knowledge to Allah'?
?
Contemplate the immense scale of the Throne—a dome above the world, carried by enormous angels, with distances of 500 years. Does this image fill your heart with awe? How can you intentionally cultivate that awe in your daily worship, so that you are not merely reciting words but truly feeling the majesty of your Lord?

The Pen and the Three Categories of Scribes
Commentary on the Pen and three categories of scribing angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Pen as a great luminous body and the three distinct categories of scribing angels described in the commentary.

Core Idea
The Pen records all destiny, and three orders of scribes record deeds, annual decrees, and the final book.

In this lesson, we delve into the commentary's explanation of the Pen and the scribing angels. The Pen is described as a luminous body created by Allah to write all events from beginning to end, with a caution against dogmatic claims about its substance. Then, the scribes are divided into three categories: those recording human deeds, those transcribing annual decrees from the Preserved Tablet, and those compiling a book under the Throne. This hierarchy reveals the meticulous divine recording system.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text aloud or silently, noting the structure: first the Pen, then the scribes enumerated with 'three'.
Pay attention to the conjunction 'ثُمَّ' (then) and 'وَ' (and).
2
Understand the Pen's description
The Pen is described as a 'great luminous body'. Note the commentator's advice to avoid speculating about its true substance.
The opinion about al-yara' (reed) is mentioned, but not affirmed.
3
Identify the three categories of scribes
Find the three types: (1) recording deeds in this world, (2) transcribing from the Preserved Tablet into angelic scrolls, (3) compiling a book under the Throne.
Each category has a specific role in the divine recording process.
4
Reflect on the hierarchy
Consider how the three categories form a chain: from daily deeds to annual decrees to a final book under the Throne.
This hierarchy shows the comprehensive recording by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (ثُمَّ القَلَمُ) معطوف على الكرسي، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني خلقه الله ، وأمره بكتب ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، قيل: هو من اليراع؛ وهو القَصَب؛ والأولى أن نُمسك عن الجزم بتعيين حقيقته . وقوله : (وَالكَاتِنُونَ) معطوف على القلم، وأقسامهم ثلاثة : الكاتبونَ على العباد أعمالهم في الدنيا . والكاتبونَ من اللوح المحفوظ ما في صحف الملائكة الموكلين بالتصرف في العالم كُل عام. والكاتبون من صحف الملائكة كتاباً يُوضع تحت العرش.
His saying: 'Then the Pen' is conjoined to the Footstool, and it is a great luminous body which Allah created and commanded to write what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection. It is said: it is made of al-yara' (reed) which is al-qasab (cane); and the best is to refrain from definitively determining its reality. His saying: 'And the scribes (al-katibun)' is conjoined to the Pen, and their divisions are three: the scribes over the servants recording their deeds in this world; and the scribes from the Preserved Tablet what is in the scrolls of the angels entrusted with managing the world each year; and the scribes from the scrolls of the angels a book placed under the Throne.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage explains the Pen and the Scribes. The Pen is described as a great luminous body created by Allah to write everything from the beginning of time until the Day of Resurrection. The commentator notes an opinion that it is made of reed (al-yara') but again advises against being certain about its true substance. Then he describes the three categories of scribing angels: first, those who record the deeds of human beings in this world; second, those who transcribe from the Preserved Tablet what is in the scrolls of the angels who are entrusted with managing the affairs of the world on an annual basis; third, those who compile a book from those angelic scrolls and place it under the Throne. This hierarchy shows the meticulous recording of divine decrees and human actions.

Key Terms
القلم
الكاتبون
اليراع
القَصَب
اللوح المحفوظ
صحف الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is only one set of scribing angels.
Correction: The commentator explicitly states there are three distinct categories of scribes, each with a specific role.

Checkpoint
How many categories of scribing angels are mentioned?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Pen is a great luminous body recording all destiny, and the three categories of scribes ensure meticulous recording of earthly deeds, annual decrees, and a final book under the Throne.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are being watched and recorded by angels every moment. If you knew that the scribe over you is writing down your deeds right now, what thought would shame you into change? When did you last feel that weight, and what did you do about it?
?
The Pen wrote your entire destiny before you were born. Does that make you feel trapped or liberated? If you truly believed that every trial and blessing was inscribed by the Pen, how would you respond to your current hardship today—not with words, but with actual patience or gratitude?
?
There are three levels of recording: your daily deeds, your yearly portion, and an eternal book under the Throne. Which of these do you neglect most in your awareness? If you had to look at that final book right now, what single entry would you most want erased—and what concrete step will you take tonight to begin erasing it?

The Tablet: A Luminous Record of Divine Decree
The commentator describes the Tablet's attributes and its function in recording destiny.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Preserved Tablet, its attributes, and why it is a distinct creation of Allah.

Core Idea
The Tablet is a luminous body where the Pen writes all destinies, accepting erasure and change.

The commentator begins by clarifying a grammatical point about the Tablet's status in the list of creations. He then describes the Tablet as a luminous body upon which the Pen writes, by Allah's permission, everything that has happened and will happen. Importantly, he notes that the Tablet accepts erasure and change, and advises against speculating on its true nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage about the Tablet
Note the grammatical clarification that the Tablet is in nominative case, not object of 'scribes'.
This corrects a potential misunderstanding.
2
Identify the description of the Tablet
Find its substance (luminous body), function (where the Pen writes), and the scope of what is written (past and future).
3
Understand the acceptance of erasure and change
The commentator affirms that the Tablet accepts erasure and change, and he withholds definitive judgment on its reality.
This aligns with the concept of Bada' in some interpretations.
4
Reflect on the tradition about the Tablet's faces
The tradition describes two faces of red ruby and green emerald, emphasizing its beauty and grandeur.
Such descriptions are taken on faith without specifying modality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
وقوله : (اللَّوْحُ) معطوف على ما قبله بتقدير حرف العطف، فهو مرفوع، وليس معمولاً لـ (كاتبين) كما قد يُتوهم؛ لأن الملائكة لم تكتب فيه؛ بل القلم يكتب فيه بمجرد القدرة . وهو جسم نوراني ، كتب فيه القلم بإذن الله ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، وهو يكتب فيه الآن على التحقيق من أنه يقبل المحو والتغيير ؛ ونُمسك عن الجزم بحقيقته، وفي بعض الآثار: (إن الله لوحاً أحَدُ وجهيه ياقوتة حمراء، والوجه الثاني زمردة خضراء) (١) ، كما في شرح المصنف). وقوله : (كُلُّ حِكَمُ :أي: كل من هذه المذكورات ذو حكم؛ فكل واحد منها الحكمة يعلمها الله سبحانه وتعالى، وإن قصرت عقولنا عن الوقوف عليها، وبعضهم لم الحكمة ؛ لأنه تعالى يتصرف بما شاء وَلَا يُسْتَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ [الأنبياء: ۲۳]، والحكمة هي الأمر الصائب، وهو سِرُّ الفعل وفائدته المترتبة عليه . وقوله : (لا) لاختياج) أي: كل مخلوف لحكمة، لا لاحتياجه تعالى إلى شيء منها، فلم يخلق العرش للارتقاء، ولا الكرسي للجلوس ولا القلم لاستحصال ما غاب عن علمه تعالى ولا الكاتبين ولا اللوح لضبط ما يُخاف نسيانه . وقوله : (وَبِها الإيمانُ يَجِبْ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الإِنْسَانُ أي بهذه المذكورات كغيرها من كل ما ثبت بصحيح الأحاديث كالحُجب والأنوار التصديق يجب عليك أيها الإنسان المكلّف، فيجب الإيمان بوجودها شرعاً حسبما عُلم تفصيلاً أو إجمالاً، غاية الأمر أن الإيمان بها تعبدي. (١) أخرجه أبو الشيخ في كتاب العظمة (٢ / ٤٩٠) ، وأورده ابن الجوزي في الموضوعات» (۱۱۸/۱).
[The section on] Unseen matters (al-samiyyat). His saying: 'The Tablet' is conjoined to what precedes it with an implied conjunction, so it is nominative, and it is not the object of 'scribes' as might be mistakenly thought; because the angels did not write in it; rather the Pen writes in it by mere power. It is a luminous body, into which the Pen wrote by Allah's permission what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection, and it is still writing in it now based on the verification that it accepts erasure and change; and we withhold from definitively determining its reality. And in some traditions: 'Allah has a Tablet, one of its two faces is of red ruby, and the second face is of green emerald' as in the commentary of the author. His saying: 'All are wisdoms' meaning: each of these mentioned things possesses a wisdom; each one of them has a wisdom known by Allah, may He be exalted, even if our intellects fall short of grasping it. And some do not [uphold] wisdom because He, may He be exalted, acts as He wills and is not questioned about what He does [Surah al-Anbiya': 23]. And wisdom is the correct matter, and it is the secret of the action and its benefit resulting from it. His saying: 'Not out of need' means: every created thing is for a wisdom, not due to His need, exalted, for anything from them. So He did not create the Throne for ascension, nor the Footstool for sitting, nor the Pen to obtain what is absent from His knowledge, nor the scribes, nor the Tablet to preserve what is feared to be forgotten. His saying: 'And through them faith is obligatory upon you, O human' means: by these mentioned things like others that are established by authentic hadiths such as the veils and lights, affirmation is obligatory upon you, O accountable human. So faith in their existence is obligatory according to the Law, whether known in detail or in general, with the ultimate matter being that belief in them is devotional. (1) Reported by Abu al-Shaykh in Kitab al-'Azamah (2/490), and Ibn al-Jawzi mentioned it in al-Mawdu'at (1/118).
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage begins with the section heading 'al-samiyyat' (unseen matters) and then explains the Tablet. The commentator first makes a grammatical clarification: the word 'al-lawh' (the Tablet) is nominative as part of the list, not the object of 'scribes' as some might mistakenly think. He then describes the Tablet as a luminous body written upon by the Pen by Allah's permission, containing everything past and future. Importantly, he states that on the verified view, the Tablet accepts erasure and change, and again advises against certainty about its true nature. He cites a tradition describing its two faces as red ruby and green emerald. Next, he explains the phrase 'All are wisdoms': each of these entities has a wisdom known to Allah, even if human intellects cannot fully grasp it. He addresses those who deny that Allah acts with wisdom by citing the Quranic verse that He is not questioned about His actions. He defines wisdom as the correct purpose and the benefit of the action. Then he explains 'Not out of need': Allah created all these things for a wisdom, not because He has any need of them — for example, He did not create the Throne to ascend it, nor the Footstool to sit on, nor the Pen to learn what He does not know, nor the scribes or Tablet to prevent forgetfulness. Finally, he states the obligation of faith: every accountable person must believe in these entities and all other matters established by authentic hadiths, such as the veils and lights. This belief may be in detail or in general, and it is devotional (ta'abbudi) — meaning it is accepted on the basis of revelation without necessarily rationalizing every detail.

Key Terms
اللوح
السمعيات
المحو والتغيير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think angels wrote on the Tablet or that the Tablet is not subject to change.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that the Pen writes by Allah's power, and the Tablet accepts erasure and change.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, who writes on the Preserved Tablet?
A) The angels
B) The Pen
C) Allah directly
D) The scribes

Key Takeaway
The Tablet is a luminous creation of Allah, written upon by the Pen, recording all destinies while accepting erasure and change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Tablet contains what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection. How does the knowledge that your entire life is recorded there change the way you approach your next hour? What will you do differently today because of this?
?
The Pen writes by mere power of Allah—not by your effort. Does your daily reliance on your own plans and abilities reflect a belief in this absolute divine power? What would it look like for you to trust His writing more than your own striving?
?
The Tablet accepts erasure and change. Is there a sin or habit you have resigned yourself to, thinking it is already written and unchangeable? What would it mean for you to actively seek its erasure through repentance and good deeds today?

Divine Wisdom: Everything Created with Purpose
The commentator explains that all creations are for a wisdom, not for Allah's need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all of Allah's creations possess inherent wisdom, known fully to Him, and that He created them not out of need but for wise purposes.

Core Idea
Every creation carries a divine wisdom, and Allah is free from need.

The commentator now turns to the wisdom behind the creations. He affirms that each of the mentioned entities has a wisdom known to Allah, even if our intellects fall short. He counters those who deny wisdom by citing that Allah is not questioned about His actions. He defines wisdom as the correct purpose and benefit. Then he negates any notion of need: Allah did not create these things for His own benefit, such as sitting or writing for knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on wisdom
Note the affirmation that each creation has a wisdom known to Allah.
2
Understand the response to those who deny wisdom
The commentator cites the verse 'He is not questioned about what He does' to show that Allah's actions are not subject to external questioning, yet wisdom is inherent.
This refutes the idea that Allah acts arbitrarily.
3
Study the definition of wisdom
Wisdom is defined as 'the correct matter, the secret of the action and its benefit.'
4
Examine the negation of need
The commentator lists specific creations (Throne, Footstool, Pen, scribes, Tablet) and denies that Allah created them for His own benefit.
Each example targets a common anthropomorphic misconception.

Source Text

السمعيات
وقوله : (اللَّوْحُ) معطوف على ما قبله بتقدير حرف العطف، فهو مرفوع، وليس معمولاً لـ (كاتبين) كما قد يُتوهم؛ لأن الملائكة لم تكتب فيه؛ بل القلم يكتب فيه بمجرد القدرة . وهو جسم نوراني ، كتب فيه القلم بإذن الله ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، وهو يكتب فيه الآن على التحقيق من أنه يقبل المحو والتغيير ؛ ونُمسك عن الجزم بحقيقته، وفي بعض الآثار: (إن الله لوحاً أحَدُ وجهيه ياقوتة حمراء، والوجه الثاني زمردة خضراء) (١) ، كما في شرح المصنف). وقوله : (كُلُّ حِكَمُ :أي: كل من هذه المذكورات ذو حكم؛ فكل واحد منها الحكمة يعلمها الله سبحانه وتعالى، وإن قصرت عقولنا عن الوقوف عليها، وبعضهم لم الحكمة ؛ لأنه تعالى يتصرف بما شاء وَلَا يُسْتَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ [الأنبياء: ۲۳]، والحكمة هي الأمر الصائب، وهو سِرُّ الفعل وفائدته المترتبة عليه . وقوله : (لا) لاختياج) أي: كل مخلوف لحكمة، لا لاحتياجه تعالى إلى شيء منها، فلم يخلق العرش للارتقاء، ولا الكرسي للجلوس ولا القلم لاستحصال ما غاب عن علمه تعالى ولا الكاتبين ولا اللوح لضبط ما يُخاف نسيانه . وقوله : (وَبِها الإيمانُ يَجِبْ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الإِنْسَانُ أي بهذه المذكورات كغيرها من كل ما ثبت بصحيح الأحاديث كالحُجب والأنوار التصديق يجب عليك أيها الإنسان المكلّف، فيجب الإيمان بوجودها شرعاً حسبما عُلم تفصيلاً أو إجمالاً، غاية الأمر أن الإيمان بها تعبدي. (١) أخرجه أبو الشيخ في كتاب العظمة (٢ / ٤٩٠) ، وأورده ابن الجوزي في الموضوعات» (۱۱۸/۱).
[The section on] Unseen matters (al-samiyyat). His saying: 'The Tablet' is conjoined to what precedes it with an implied conjunction, so it is nominative, and it is not the object of 'scribes' as might be mistakenly thought; because the angels did not write in it; rather the Pen writes in it by mere power. It is a luminous body, into which the Pen wrote by Allah's permission what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection, and it is still writing in it now based on the verification that it accepts erasure and change; and we withhold from definitively determining its reality. And in some traditions: 'Allah has a Tablet, one of its two faces is of red ruby, and the second face is of green emerald' as in the commentary of the author. So faith in their existence is obligatory according to the Law, whether known in detail or in general, with the ultimate matter being that belief in them is devotional. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you sometimes feel you are doing Allah a favor? How does knowing that Allah is wholly independent of your worship change the sincerity of your intention? Will you audit your deeds today to ensure they are solely for His sake, not out of a sense of obligation or need?
?
Have you ever been disturbed by not understanding why something happens in your life? Can you surrender that discomfort to the truth that every creation and event has a wisdom known to Allah, even if you never grasp it? What would it look like to live in complete trust, without demanding explanations from your Creator?
?
You often assume that the universe revolves around your own needs and purposes. But this lesson declares that everything exists for a divine wisdom, not for your comfort. How would your priorities shift if you truly lived as if you were not the center of the story? What is one attachment you can release today to align with that reality?

Faith in the Unseen: An Obligatory Devotional Duty
The commentator declares the obligation to believe in all unseen matters reported in revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the unseen matters mentioned in revelation is obligatory, and that this belief is devotional—accepted on faith without needing full rational understanding.

Core Idea
Belief in unseen creations is an obligatory devotional act.

The commentator concludes by stating the obligation of faith. He declares that every accountable person must believe in these entities, as well as in all other matters established by authentic hadiths, such as the veils and lights. This faith can be detailed or general, and it is fundamentally a devotional act (ta'abbudi)—meaning it is accepted on the basis of revelation, even if the intellect cannot fully grasp it.

Guided Path
1
Read the final passage about the obligation of faith
Note the address 'O human' and the scope of belief.
2
Identify the scope of belief
Belief includes these specific entities and all others established by authentic hadiths, such as veils and lights.
The list is not exhaustive.
3
Understand the nature of the belief: devotional
The commentator emphasizes that belief is ta'abbudi (devotional), meaning it is based on submission to revelation, not rational proof.
This distinguishes Islamic faith from philosophical speculation.
4
Reflect on why this obligation matters
Belief in the unseen is a test of faith; accepting what revelation says without demanding detailed rational explanation is a sign of true submission.
