The Preserved Tablet and the Pen
Clarification of the nature of al-Lawh al-Mahfuz and al-Qalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Preserved Tablet and the Pen as described in Sunni theology, including how the Pen writes destiny and the Tablet accepts erasure.

Core Idea
The Pen writes destiny directly; the Tablet is not written by angels.

The author begins by clarifying a common misconception about the Preserved Tablet. He explains that it is not written in by the recording angels but by the Pen directly, and describes its nature as a luminous body that records all events and permits erasure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice the correction of the misunderstanding about the angels.
The author uses 'كما قد يُتوهم' to flag a misconception.
2
Identify the key claims
List what the author affirms: the Tablet is luminous, the Pen writes by Allah's power, it records past and future, it accepts erasure, and we refrain from defining its reality fully.
3
Understand the tradition cited
The tradition describes the Tablet's appearance in precious stones. Note that such descriptions are accepted without literal interpretation.
The author says 'ونُمسك عن الجزم بحقيقته'—we refrain from certainty about its reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات معمولاً لـ (كاتبين) كما قد يُتوهم؛ لأن الملائكة لم تكتب فيه؛ بل القلم يكتب فيه بمجرد القدرة. وهو جسم نوراني، كتب فيه القلم بإذن الله ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، وهو يكتب فيه الآن على التحقيق من أنه يقبل المحو والتغيير؛ ونُمسك عن الجزم بحقيقته، وفي بعض الآثار: (إن الله لوحاً أحَدُ وجهيه ياقوتة حمراء، والوجه الثاني زمردة خضراء) (١)، كما في شرح المصنف). وقوله: (كُلُّ حِكَمُ: أي: كل من هذه المذكورات ذو حكم؛ فكل واحد منها الحكمة يعلمها الله سبحانه وتعالى، وإن قصرت عقولنا عن الوقوف عليها، وبعضهم لم الحكمة؛ لأنه تعالى يتصرف بما شاء وَلَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ [الأنبياء: 23]، والحكمة هي الأمر الصائب، وهو سِرُّ الفعل وفائدته المترتبة عليه يلتزم. وقوله: (لا) لاختياج) أي: كل مخلوف لحكمة، لا لاحتياجه تعالى إلى شيء منها، فلم يخلق العرش للارتقاء، ولا الكرسي للجلوس ولا القلم لاستحصال ما غاب عن علمه تعالى ولا الكاتبين ولا اللوح لضبط ما يُخاف نسيانه. وقوله: (وبها الإيمان يَجِبْ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الإِنْسَانُ) أي بهذه المذكورات كغيرها من كل ما ثبت بصحيح الأحاديث كالحُجب والأنوار التصديق يجب عليك أيها الإنسان المكلّف، فيجب الإيمان بوجودها شرعاً حسبما عُلم تفصيلاً أو إجمالاً، غاية الأمر أن الإيمان بها تعبدي.
The sam'iyyat (things known through revelation): [the Preserved Tablet] is not written in by (the two recording angels) as might be imagined, because the angels do not write in it; rather, the Pen writes in it by mere power. And it is a luminous body; the Pen wrote in it by Allah's permission what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection, and it is writing in it now, upon the verification that it accepts erasure and change; and we refrain from making a definitive statement about its reality. And in some traditions: (Allah has a tablet, one of whose sides is a red ruby, and the second side is a green emerald), as in the author's commentary. And His saying: 'All [are] wise' means: each of these mentioned things possesses wisdom; so each one has wisdom that Allah, exalted, knows, even if our intellects fall short of comprehending it. And some of them [denied?] wisdom; because He, exalted, acts as He wills, and He is not questioned about what He does (Quran 21:23). And wisdom is the correct affair, and it is the secret of the action and its benefit that results from it. And His saying: 'Not due to need' means: every created thing is for a wisdom, not due to His, exalted, need of anything from them. So He did not create the Throne for rising, nor the Footstool for sitting, nor the Pen to obtain what is absent from His knowledge, exalted, nor the two recording angels, nor the Tablet to record what is feared forgotten. And His saying: 'And by them faith is obligatory upon you, O human' means: by these mentioned things and others like them from everything established by authentic hadiths, such as the veils and lights, confirmation is obligatory upon you, O responsible human. So it is obligatory to believe in their existence according to the Law, in detail or in summary as known; the bottom line is that belief in them is devotional (ta'abbudi).
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn about the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz) and related matters. The author begins by clarifying that the Tablet is not written in by the two recording angels (as might be misunderstood); rather, the Pen writes in it directly by divine power. He describes the Tablet as a luminous body in which the Pen writes destiny, and clarifies that it accepts erasure and change (i.e., it is the Lawh al-Mahw wa al-Ithbat). He cites a tradition describing its appearance. Then he explains the phrase 'كل حكم' (all are wise) from the matn, meaning every created thing has a wisdom known to Allah, even if humans cannot grasp it. He notes that some denied wisdom, but Allah acts as He wills and is not questioned. Wisdom is the correct purpose and benefit of an action. Next, he explains 'لا لاحتياج' (not due to need): creation is for wisdom, not for any need in Allah. He gives examples: the Throne is not for sitting, etc. Finally, he explains 'وبها الإيمان يجب' (and by them faith is obligatory): belief in all these things confirmed by authentic hadiths is obligatory, and this belief is devotional (ta'abbudi), meaning it is accepted on authority, not necessarily through rational proof.

Key Terms
اللوح المحفوظ
القلم
المحو والتغيير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that the two recording angels write in al-Lawh al-Mahfuz.
Correction: The angels do not write in the Preserved Tablet; rather, the Pen writes in it directly by Allah's power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what writes in the Preserved Tablet?
A) The two recording angels
B) The Pen
C) Allah directly
D) The Prophet Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The Preserved Tablet is inscribed by the Pen, not angels, and it records destiny with the possibility of erasure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Preserved Tablet is not written by angels but by the Pen, and it accepts erasure and change. Allah is writing your destiny even now. Are you living as though your choices matter in altering what is written? Repentance and good deeds can erase bad records. Which sins have you resigned yourself to, thinking they are already fixed? Commit today to seek erasure through sincere repentance.
?
The passage says the Tablet is a luminous body and the Pen writes by mere power. This reminds you that your destiny is in Allah's hands alone, not in the hands of angels or any creation. Do you truly rely on Allah for your fate, or do you secretly rely on people or your own strength? Examine your heart: when you fear the future, do you turn to Allah first or to other means? Let this lesson push you to place your trust solely in the One who holds the Pen.

The Wisdom in Creation
Explanation of the wisdom behind creation and negation of divine need.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that everything Allah creates has a wise purpose, not due to any need on His part, and that His actions are not subject to questioning.

Core Idea
Creation is for wisdom, not for need.

The author explains the phrase 'كل حكم' from the matn, affirming that every created thing has a wisdom known to Allah, even if we cannot grasp it. He then clarifies that creation is not due to any need in Allah, giving examples like the Throne not being for sitting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the two key phrases: 'كل حكم' and 'لا لاحتياج'.
The passage includes a Quranic verse: 'لا يُسأل عما يفعل'.
2
Understand the first point: wisdom in creation
The author says each thing has a wisdom (hikma) that Allah knows, even if our intellects fall short. Some denied wisdom, but Allah does as He wills and is not questioned.
This refutes the idea that creation is arbitrary.
3
Understand the second point: no need in Allah
Creation is for wisdom, not for Allah's need. Examples: He did not create the Throne to sit on, etc.
This refutes anthropomorphism and attributing need to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات معمولاً لـ (كاتبين) كما قد يُتوهم؛ لأن الملائكة لم تكتب فيه؛ بل القلم يكتب فيه بمجرد القدرة. وهو جسم نوراني، كتب فيه القلم بإذن الله ما كان وما يكون إلى يوم القيامة، وهو يكتب فيه الآن على التحقيق من أنه يقبل المحو والتغيير؛ ونُمسك عن الجزم بحقيقته، وفي بعض الآثار: (إن الله لوحاً أحَدُ وجهيه ياقوتة حمراء، والوجه الثاني زمردة خضراء) (١)، كما في شرح المصنف). وقوله: (كُلُّ حِكَمُ: أي: كل من هذه المذكورات ذو حكم؛ فكل واحد منها الحكمة يعلمها الله سبحانه وتعالى، وإن قصرت عقولنا عن الوقوف عليها، وبعضهم لم الحكمة؛ لأنه تعالى يتصرف بما شاء وَلَا يُسْأَلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ [الأنبياء: 23]، والحكمة هي الأمر الصائب، وهو سِرُّ الفعل وفائدته المترتبة عليه يلتزم. وقوله: (لا) لاختياج) أي: كل مخلوف لحكمة، لا لاحتياجه تعالى إلى شيء منها، فلم يخلق العرش للارتقاء، ولا الكرسي للجلوس ولا القلم لاستحصال ما غاب عن علمه تعالى ولا الكاتبين ولا اللوح لضبط ما يُخاف نسيانه. وقوله: (وبها الإيمان يَجِبْ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا الإِنْسَانُ) أي بهذه المذكورات كغيرها من كل ما ثبت بصحيح الأحاديث كالحُجب والأنوار التصديق يجب عليك أيها الإنسان المكلّف، فيجب الإيمان بوجودها شرعاً حسبما عُلم تفصيلاً أو إجمالاً، غاية الأمر أن الإيمان بها تعبدي.
The sam'iyyat (things known through revelation): [the Preserved Tablet] is not written in by (the two recording angels) as might be imagined, because the angels do not write in it; rather, the Pen writes in it by mere power. And it is a luminous body; the Pen wrote in it by Allah's permission what was and what will be until the Day of Resurrection, and it is writing in it now, upon the verification that it accepts erasure and change; and we refrain from making a definitive statement about its reality. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson teaches that Allah is not in need of your worship. Does your heart feel humbled or entitled? Ask yourself: 'Do I ever act as if I am doing Allah a favor by obeying Him?' If so, repent and renew your intention to worship out of love and need, not as a transaction.
?
The passage mentions created things like the Throne and Pen to correct anthropomorphic thoughts. What subtle, unworthy images of Allah have you harbored in your mind? Resolve to replace them with the descriptions from the Qur'an and Sunnah, starting by memorizing one verse about His majesty today.

The Obligation of Devotional Belief
Conclusion: obligation of devotional faith in revealed matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the unseen matters confirmed by authentic hadiths is obligatory as a devotional act (ta'abbudi), accepted on revealed authority.

Core Idea
Belief in sam'iyyat is devotional, based on revelation.

The author concludes by stating that faith in all these mentioned things (Tablet, Pen, etc.) and other unseen matters from authentic hadiths is obligatory. This belief is devotional (ta'abbudi), meaning it is accepted on the authority of revelation, not necessarily through rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the final part of the source, focusing on the phrase 'وبها الإيمان يجب' and the conclusion that belief is ta'abbudi.
2
Understand the scope of obligatory belief
It includes not only the things mentioned but also everything confirmed by sound hadiths, like veils and lights.
The author says 'كغيرها من كل ما ثبت بصحيح الأحاديث'.
3
Grasp the meaning of 'ta'abbudi'
Devotional belief means accepting on the basis of divine command, without needing rational demonstration. It is an act of worship.
This distinguishes faith in sam'iyyat from rational theological proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

Unseen Matters

Paradise and Hell: Already Created and Existing Now
Author affirms Hell's present creation and refutes deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now, based on scriptural evidence and consensus, and you will be able to refute those who deny their present existence.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are real and ready now—Allah prepared them for the Day of Judgment.

In this lesson, we examine a core Sunni belief: that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist in the present. The author not only affirms this but also decisively refutes those who claim they will be created only on Judgment Day. Let's see the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the matn and commentary
Read the Arabic line 'والنار حق أوجدت كالجنة فلا تمل لِجَاحِدِ ذِي جِنَّهُ' and its explanation. Notice how the author states that Hell is true and created like Paradise.
The matn is the foundational statement.
2
Identify the refuted groups
The commentary mentions two groups: philosophers who deny both Paradise and Hell entirely, and Mu'tazilites who deny their past existence. Understand the difference.
This refutation is central to the lesson.
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
The author uses the story of Adam (indicating Paradise existed) and the verse 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (present tense) to prove present existence.
The verse أُعِدَّتْ is a key proof.
4
Understand the position on location and layers
The passage notes that location is unknown or delegated to Allah, and describes the seven layers of Hell, with Jahannam as the highest.
This shows the scope of knowledge.
5
Contrast with sectarian views
Compare the Sunni position (existence now) with the Mu'tazilite view (existence later). Reflect on why this matters for eschatology.
This reinforces the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ الجنة والنار موجودتان وهما دارا الخلود] (109 - والنار حق أوجدت كالجنة فلا تمل لِجَاحِدِ ذِي جِنَّهُ) قوله: (والنار حق أوجدت كالجنة) أي: والنار التي هي دار العذاب ثابتة بالكتاب والسنة واتفاق علماء الأمة، أوجدها الله تعالى فيما مضى كالجنة التي هي دار الثواب في كونها حقا، وأنها أوجدت فيما مضى، وردّ المصنف بحقيتهما على منكرهما بالمرة كالفلاسفة وبإيجادهما فيما مضى على منكر وجودِهما فيما مضى، وأنهما إنما يوجدان يوم القيامة كأبي هاشم وعبد الجبار المعتزليين). ويدلُّ لنا قصة آدم وحواء عليهما السلام على ما جاء به القرآن والسنة وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المخالف، فذلك يدلُّ على ثبوت الجنة، ولا قائل بثبوتها دون النار، فهي ثابتة أيضاً، والآيات صريحة في ذلك وقد أجمع العلماء على أن تأويلها من غير ضرورة إلحاد في الدين، كما قيل: آدم كان رجلاً في جنة؛ أي: بستان له، على ربوة: أي: محلّ مرتفع؛ فعصى ربه فأنزله لبطن الوادي. ولم يرد نصّ صريح في تعيين مكان الجنة والنار كما في شرح المقاصد»، والأكثرون على أن الجنة فوق السموات السبع وتحت العرش، وأن النار تحت الأرضين السبع والحق تفويض علم ذلك إلى اللطيف الخبير، كما في شرح المصنف. وطبقات النار سبع: أعلاها جهنم؛ وهي لمن يُعذب على قدر ذنبه من المؤمنين، وتصير خراباً بخروجهم منها (1) القائلين: إن النار والجنة لم توجدًا بعد؛ لأنه لا يوجد من يدخلهما الآن، وإنما توجدان يوم الجزاء، والدخول إليهما بعد الحساب. وأما أهل السنة والجماعة فيقولون بوجودهما من الآن، مستدلين بقوله تعالى في حق النار: أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَفِرِينَ [البقرة: 24]، وفي حق الجنة: وَقُلْنَا يَتَادَمُ اسْكُنْ أَنتَ وَزَوْجُكَ الْجَنَّةَ.
[Paradise and Hell are existing and they are the two abodes of eternity] (109 - And Hell is true, [already] created like Paradise, so do not incline to a denier of foolishness). His saying: 'And Hell is true, created like Paradise' means: Hell, which is the abode of punishment, is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the scholars of the Ummah. Allah, exalted, created it in the past like Paradise, which is the abode of reward, in being true, and that it was created in the past. The author refutes by their truth those who deny them entirely, like the philosophers, and by their creation in the past those who deny their existence in the past and claim they will only exist on the Day of Resurrection, like Abu Hashim and Abd al-Jabbar the Mu'tazilites. And the story of Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, indicates to us what came in the Quran and Sunnah and upon which consensus was held before the appearance of opposition. So that indicates the existence of Paradise, and no one claims its existence without Hell; thus it is also established. The verses are explicit about that. And the scholars have unanimously held that interpreting them without necessity is atheism in religion, as was said: 'Adam was a man in a garden; that is, his own orchard, on a hill; that is, a high place; so he disobeyed his Lord, and He caused him to descend to the bottom of the valley.' And there is no explicit text specifying the location of Paradise and Hell, as in Sharh al-Maqasid. The majority hold that Paradise is above the seven heavens and under the Throne, and that Hell is under the seven earths. The truth is to delegate knowledge of that to the Subtle, the All-Aware, as in the author's commentary. And the layers of Hell are seven: the highest is Jahannam; it is for those who are punished according to their sin from the believers, and it will become empty upon their exit from it. (1) Those who say: 'Hell and Paradise have not been created yet, because there is no one to enter them now; rather, they will be created on the Day of Recompense, and entry into them will be after the Reckoning.' As for Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, they say they exist now, adducing the saying of Allah, exalted, regarding Hell: 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (Quran 2:24), and regarding Paradise: 'And We said, O Adam, dwell you and your wife in Paradise' (Quran 2:35).
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. The author first states the matn line: 'And Hell is true, created like Paradise, so do not incline to a denier of foolishness.' He then explains that Hell is established by the Qur'an, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus. Allah created it in the past just as He created Paradise. The author refutes two groups: (1) philosophers who deny both entirely, and (2) Mu'tazilites like Abu Hashim and Abd al-Jabbar who deny their past existence, claiming they will be created only on Judgment Day. As evidence, the author cites the story of Adam and Eve, which shows Paradise existed (Adam was placed in it). Since no one claims Paradise exists without Hell, Hell also exists. He rejects allegorical interpretations (ta'wil) of these matters without necessity, calling them atheism. He mentions the debate about the location of Paradise and Hell, noting that the majority hold Paradise above the heavens and Hell under the earths, but the safest position is to delegate knowledge to Allah. He then describes the seven layers of Hell, the highest being Jahannam, which will become empty after believing sinners are purified. The footnote clarifies the Mu'tazilite position and the Sunni position, citing the verse 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (present perfect) and Adam's entry into Paradise as evidence for their current existence.

وجود

المعتزلة

Misconception: Some believe Paradise and Hell are not yet created because no one is in them now.
Correction: The correct belief is that they are created now, as evidenced by the Quranic phrase 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (present perfect) and the story of Adam entering Paradise.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell already exist now, created by Allah, as proven by Quranic verses and consensus, and we must affirm this against deniers.

?
Allah says Hell is 'prepared for the disbelievers' (present tense). If someone you love is still disbelieving, does this verse stir urgency in your heart to speak to them? What will you do about that urgency before this day ends?

Paradise and Hellfire Are Already Created
Commentator proves Paradise and Hellfire are already created, refuting deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hellfire are already created and exist now, based on the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus, and how the commentator refutes those who deny their past existence.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are already created, not just future realities.

This lesson examines a key passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid affirming that Paradise and Hellfire are already created. The commentator draws on the story of Adam, the consensus of scholars, and explicit verses to refute those who deny their present existence. Understanding this reinforces the believer's conviction in the unseen realities of the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then its full translation. Let the author's own words set the foundation.
Notice the key terms: النار, الجنة, الحق, أوجدت.
2
Identify the Two Groups Refuted
The commentator refutes two groups: those who deny Paradise and Hell entirely (philosophers) and those who deny their past creation (Mu'tazilites like Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar).
This shows the passage is both affirming existence and timing.
3
Examine the Proof from Adam
The story of Adam and Eve in Paradise is used as evidence that Paradise existed in the past. By extension, since no one affirms Paradise without Hell, Hell also exists.
This is a key scriptural and consensus-based argument.
4
Understand the Location Discussion
The commentator notes that there is no explicit text on location, but majority views exist. The safest position is to delegate knowledge to Allah.
This is not the main point but shows scholarly caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والنَّارُ حَقٌّ أُوْجِدَتْ كَالجَنَّهُ) أي : والنارُ التي هي دار العذاب ثابتة بالكتاب والسنة واتفاق علماء الأمة، أوجدها الله تعالى فيما مضى كالجنة التي هي دار الثواب في كونها حقا، وأنها أوجدت فيما مضى، وردّ المصنف بحقيتهما على منكرهما بالمرة كالفلاسفة وبإيجادهما فيما مضى على منكر وجودِهما فيما مضى، وأنهما إنما يوجدان يوم القيامة كأبي هاشم وعبد الجبار المعتزليين . ويدلُّ لنا قصة آدم وحواء عليهما السلام على ما جاء به القرآن والسنة وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المخالف، فذلك يدلُّ على ثبوت الجنة، ولا قائل بثبوتها دون النار، فهي ثابتة أيضاً، والآيات صريحة في ذلك. وقد أجمع العلماء على أن تأويلها من غير ضرورة إلحاد في الدين، كما قيل : آدم كان رجلاً في جنة؛ أي: بستان له، على ربوة: أي: محلّ مرتفع؛ فعصى ربه فأنزله لبطن الوادي. ولم يرد نصّ صريح في تعيين مكان الجنة والنار كما في شرح المقاصد»، والأكثرون على أن الجنة فوق السموات السبع وتحت العرش، وأن النار تحت الأرضين السبع والحق تفويض علم ذلك إلى اللطيف الخبير، كما في شرح المصنف .
His saying: (And the Fire is true, created like Paradise) means: The Fire which is the abode of punishment is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the scholars of the ummah. Allah Almighty created it in the past like Paradise which is the abode of reward, in that they are true, and that they were created in the past. The author refutes by their truth those who deny them altogether, like the philosophers, and by their creation in the past those who deny their existence in the past, claiming they will only be created on the Day of Judgment, like Abu Hashim and ‘Abd al-Jabbar the Mu‘tazilites. The story of Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, indicates to us what the Qur’an and Sunnah have brought and on which consensus was reached before the emergence of the opponent. That indicates the establishment of Paradise, and there is no one who affirms its establishment without the Fire, so it is also established, and the verses are explicit in that. The scholars have agreed that interpreting it without necessity is atheism in religion, as it was said: Adam was a man in a garden; i.e., an orchard of his, on a hill; i.e., an elevated place; then he disobeyed his Lord, so He brought him down to the valley floor. There is no explicit text specifying the location of Paradise and Hell as in Sharh al-Maqasid, and the majority hold that Paradise is above the seven heavens and beneath the Throne, and that Hell is beneath the seven earths, but the truth is to delegate knowledge of that to the Subtle, All-Aware, as in the author's commentary.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line from Jawharat al-Tawhid affirming that Hellfire is true and already created like Paradise. The commentator begins by explaining that the Fire, as the abode of punishment, is proven by the Qur’an, Sunnah, and consensus of scholars. It was created by Allah in the past, just as Paradise was created in the past. The author (Ibn al-Jawhari?) refutes two groups: those who deny both Paradise and Hell entirely (the philosophers), and those who deny their past existence, claiming they will only be created on the Day of Judgment (like the Mu‘tazilites Abu Hashim and ‘Abd al-Jabbar). The commentator then provides a proof from the story of Adam and Eve, which is recorded in the Qur’an and Sunnah and was accepted by consensus before any opposition. The story establishes the existence of Paradise, and since no one claims Paradise exists but not Hell, Hell is also established. The verses are explicit. He further states that scholars agree that interpreting these matters without necessity is atheism, giving an example of an invalid interpretation: that Adam was merely in an orchard on a hill. Finally, he notes that there is no explicit text specifying the location of Paradise and Hell, and while the majority hold that Paradise is above the heavens and Hell below the earth, the correct position is to delegate knowledge to Allah.

Will you commit to accepting them as they are, even when they challenge your comfort?

The Seven Layers of Hellfire
Enumeration of the seven layers of Hellfire with their inhabitants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven layers of Hellfire and which groups of people are assigned to each.

Core Idea
Hell has seven layers, each for a specific category of sinners.

The text of al-Jawhara enumerates the seven layers of Hellfire, from the highest to the lowest, and specifies the inhabitants of each layer. This classification is based on transmitted knowledge (sam‘iyyat) and underscores the divine justice in varying degrees of punishment. Let's explore these layers one by one.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration
Read the Arabic passage listing the seven layers and their inhabitants. Notice the order from top to bottom.
The highest layer, Jahannam, is for sinful believers who will eventually be rescued.
2
Identify each layer and its group
For each layer, note the name and the group assigned. Reflect on the spiritual state of each group (e.g., hypocrites are in the lowest layer).
3
Understand the significance
Ask yourself why the author included this classification. It reinforces the reality of Hell and serves as a warning to avoid these sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطبقات النار سبع : أعلاها جهنم ؛ وهي لمن يُعذب على قدر ذنبه من المؤمنين، وتصير خراباً بخروجهم منها. وتحت\ها لظى وهي لليهود، ثم الحُطَمةُ وهي للنصارى، ثم السعير وهي للصابئين وهم فرقة من اليهود، ثم سَقَرُ وهي للمجوس، ثم الجَحِيمُ وهي لعبدة الأصنام، ثم الهاوية وهي للمنافقين. وذكر ابن العربي أن هذه النار التي في الدنيا ما أخرجها الله إلى الناس من جهنم غُمست في البحر مرتين، ولولا ذلك لم ينتفع أحدٌ بها من حرها، وكفى بها زاجراً، وبعد أخذ نار الدنيا منها أوقد عليها ألف سنة حتى ابيضت، ثم ألف سنة حتى احمرت، ثم ألف سنة حتى اسودت، فهي سوداء مظلمة، وحرها هواءٌ مُحْرِفٌ، ولا جمر لها سوى بني آدم والأحجار المتخذة آلهة من دون الله، قال تعالى: ﴿يَاتها الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا قُوا أَنفُسَكُمْ وَأَهْلِيكُمْ نَارًا وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ وَالْحِجَارَةُ ﴾ [التحريم: ٦].
The layers of the Fire are seven: the highest is Jahannam, which is for those believers who are punished according to their sin, and it becomes desolate after they come out of it. Beneath it is Laza, which is for the Jews; then al-Hutama, which is for the Christians; then al-Sa‘ir, which is for the Sabians—a sect of the Jews; then Saqar, which is for the Zoroastrians; then al-Jahim, which is for the idol worshippers; then al-Hawiya, which is for the hypocrites. Ibn al-‘Arabi mentioned that this fire in the world is what Allah extracted for people from Jahannam; it was dipped in the sea twice, and were it not for that, no one would benefit from its heat, and it suffices as a deterrent. After taking the worldly fire from it, it was kindled for a thousand years until it became white, then a thousand years until it became red, then a thousand years until it became black. So it is black and dark, its heat is scorching air, and it has no ember except the children of Adam and the stones taken as gods besides Allah. He said: 'O you who have believed, protect yourselves and your families from a Fire whose fuel is people and stones' [al-Tahrim: 6].
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage enumerates the seven layers of Hellfire and describes their nature. The author lists them from top to bottom: Jahannam (the highest) for sinful believers who will eventually be taken out; then Laza for Jews; al-Hutama for Christians; al-Sa‘ir for Sabians; Saqar for Zoroastrians; al-Jahim for idolaters; and al-Hawiya for hypocrites. He then relates a tradition from Ibn al-‘Arabi: the worldly fire is a small part of Jahannam that was extracted and dipped in the sea twice to cool it, otherwise no one could benefit from it. It was then heated for three thousand years (white, red, black) resulting in its black, dark appearance, with a scorching heat and no fuel other than humans and idolatrous stones, citing Qur’an 66:6. The passage emphasizes the intense reality of Hell and serves as a warning.

Key Terms
جهنم
لظى
الحطمة
السعير
سقر
الجحيم
هاوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which layer of Hell is designated for the hypocrites?
A) Jahannam
B) Laza
C) al-Hawiya
D) Saqar

Key Takeaway
Hellfire has seven distinct layers, each for a specific category of sinners, with Jahannam being the highest and for sinful believers who are eventually saved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Nature and Intensity of Hellfire
Description of Hellfire's origin, transformation, and fuel based on Ibn al-‘Arabi's report.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical reality of Hellfire as described by Ibn al-‘Arabi, including its origin, transformation, and fuel.

Core Idea
Hellfire is a literal, intense fire whose worldly counterpart is just a cooled fragment.

After listing the layers, the author relates a tradition from Ibn al-‘Arabi that explains the nature of Hellfire. This description emphasizes its extreme heat, blackness, and its fuel—humans and stones. The passage aims to instill fear and deterrence.

Guided Path
1
Read the description
Read the Arabic passage about Hellfire's nature. Note the series of events: extraction, dipping, heating, and fuel.
2
Trace the transformation

This shows how intense Hellfire is compared to worldly fire.
3
Understand the fuel
The fuel is humans and stones (idols). Connect to the Quranic verse cited (al-Tahrim 66:6).
This underscores the literal reality.
4
Reflect on the warning
Consider why this description is given: to serve as a deterrent (zajir) and to encourage protection from Hell.

The Seven Gardens of Paradise and Their Hierarchy
Enumeration of the seven gardens of Paradise with their hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the names and hierarchy of the seven gardens of Paradise as described in traditional Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Paradise has multiple gardens, with al-Firdaws as the highest and best.

This lesson examines the traditional classification of Paradise into seven gardens. The passage from Tuhfat al-Mureed presents the view that these gardens are adjacent yet distinct in rank, with al-Firdaws being the highest. Let's explore the names and order.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a disagreement about whether the gardens are adjacent.
2
Identify the seven gardens in order
The passage lists seven gardens in descending order of excellence. Find each name and notice how the author ranks them.
Al-Firdaws is described as the best, middlemost, and highest.
3
Note the special status of al-Firdaws
Al-Firdaws is not only the best but also the highest, with the Throne above it and the rivers flowing from it. Reflect on its centrality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في الجنة : هل هي سبعُ جناتٍ متجاورة؟ أفضلها وأوسطها الفردوس، وهي أعلاها والمجاورة لا تنافي العلو وفوقها عرش الرحمن، ومنها تتفجر أنهار الجنة، ويليها في الأفضلية جنة عدن ثم جنة الخلد، ثم جنة النعيم، وجنة المأوى، ودار السلام، ودار الجلال. والجنان كلُّها متصلة بمقام الوسيلة؛ ليتنعم جميع أهل الجنة بمشاهدته لظهوره لهم منها ؛ لأنها تشرق على أهل الجنة كما أن الشمس تشرق على أهل الدنيا، وهذا ما ذهب إليه ابن عباس .
And there is disagreement about Paradise: Is it seven adjacent gardens? The best and middlemost is al-Firdaws, and it is the highest—and adjacency does not negate height—and above it is the Throne of the Most Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise burst forth. Next in excellence is the Garden of ‘Adn, then the Garden of Eternity, then the Garden of Bliss, and the Garden of Refuge, and the Abode of Peace, and the Abode of Majesty. And all the gardens are connected to the Station of the Means (al-Wasila), so that all the people of Paradise may delight in witnessing it because it appears to them from it, for it shines upon the people of Paradise as the sun shines upon the people of this world. This is what Ibn ‘Abbas held.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage discusses the structure of Paradise. The author notes disagreement: are there seven adjacent gardens? He describes al-Firdaws as the best, middlemost, and highest—adjacency does not prevent it being above. Above it is the Throne of Allah, and from it flow the rivers of Paradise. Then he lists the other gardens in descending order of excellence: ‘Adn, Khuld, Na‘im, Ma’wa, Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal. He then explains that all gardens are connected to the Station of the Means (al-Wasila), which is a high station of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). This connection allows all inhabitants to see it, as it shines upon them like the sun shines on earth. This view is attributed to Ibn ‘Abbas.

Key Terms
الجنة
الفردوس
عدن
الخلد
النعيم
المأوى
دار السلام
دار الجلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Paradise is a single garden with no internal differentiation.
Correction: This passage clarifies that Paradise consists of seven distinct gardens, each with its own name and rank, and al-Firdaws is the highest.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which garden is described as the highest and best?
A) Jannah al-Khuld
B) Jannah al-Na‘im
C) al-Firdaws
D) Dar al-Salam

Key Takeaway
Paradise consists of multiple gardens with al-Firdaws as the highest in rank and location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Firdaws is described as the best and highest garden, from which all rivers flow. In your daily life, what is your 'al-Firdaws'—the highest goal you are sincerely striving for? Are your actions flowing from that pure intention, or have you settled for lesser aims? Write down one concrete change you can make today to realign your efforts toward the highest reward.
?
The passage notes that adjacency does not negate height. How often do you let the 'adjacency' of worldly concerns—work, family, distractions—convince you that spiritual height is unattainable? What is one excuse you need to abandon to pursue nearness to Allah without compromise?
?
Above al-Firdaws is the Throne of the Most Merciful. When you envision your final destination, does it include a direct view of your Creator? What steps can you take to increase your longing for that vision, and how will you prioritize that longing over temporary pleasures starting today?

The Connection of All Gardens to the Prophet's Station
Explanation of the connection between all gardens and the Prophet's station.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how all gardens of Paradise are connected to the Prophet's station (al-Wasila) and how its light benefits all inhabitants.

Core Idea
All gardens are connected to the Prophet's station, whose light shines upon them all.

The passage concludes with a profound statement: all gardens are linked to the Station of the Means (al-Wasila), a lofty rank of the Prophet Muhammad. This connection allows every resident of Paradise to witness and benefit from its illumination. Let's explore this beautiful concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Focus on the sentence beginning with 'والجنان كلُّها متصلة بمقام الوسيلة'. Read it in Arabic and then in translation.
Notice the analogy comparing the light of al-Wasila to the sun shining on earth.
2
Understand the concept of al-Wasila
Al-Wasila is a high station granted to the Prophet Muhammad. This passage says all gardens are connected to it. Ask yourself: what does 'connection' mean here?
The passage indicates that from this station, the Prophet's light appears in all gardens.
3
Reflect on the purpose of the connection
The purpose is 'so that all the people of Paradise may delight in witnessing it'. Contemplate the inclusiveness of this blessing.
The analogy with the sun emphasizes universality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في الجنة : هل هي سبعُ جناتٍ متجاورة؟ أفضلها وأوسطها الفردوس، وهي أعلاها والمجاورة لا تنافي العلو وفوقها عرش الرحمن، ومنها تتفجر أنهار الجنة، ويليها في الأفضلية جنة عدن ثم جنة الخلد، ثم جنة النعيم، وجنة المأوى، ودار السلام، ودار الجلال. والجنان كلُّها متصلة بمقام الوسيلة؛ ليتنعم جميع أهل الجنة بمشاهدته لظهوره لهم منها ؛ لأنها تشرق على أهل الجنة كما أن الشمس تشرق على أهل الدنيا، وهذا ما ذهب إليه ابن عباس .
And there is disagreement about Paradise: Is it seven adjacent gardens? The best and middlemost is al-Firdaws, and it is the highest—and adjacency does not negate height—and above it is the Throne of the Most Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise burst forth. Next in excellence is the Garden of ‘Adn, then the Garden of Eternity, then the Garden of Bliss, and the Garden of Refuge, and the Abode of Peace, and the Abode of Majesty. And all the gardens are connected to the Station of the Means (al-Wasila), so that all the people of Paradise may delight in witnessing it because it appears to them from it, for it shines upon the people of Paradise as the sun shines upon the people of this world. This is what Ibn ‘Abbas held.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage discusses the structure of Paradise. The author notes disagreement: are there seven adjacent gardens? He describes al-Firdaws as the best, middlemost, and highest—adjacency does not prevent it being above. Above it is the Throne of Allah, and from it flow the rivers of Paradise. Then he lists the other gardens in descending order of excellence: ‘Adn, Khuld, Na‘im, Ma’wa, Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal. He then explains that all gardens are connected to the Station of the Means (al-Wasila), which is a high station of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). This connection allows all inhabitants to see it, as it shines upon them like the sun shines on earth. This view is attributed to Ibn ‘Abbas.

The Seven Layers of Hell and Their Occupants
Lists the seven hells and their designated groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven named layers of Hell and the specific groups assigned to each according to the transmitted narration.

Core Idea
Hell has seven named layers, each assigned to a different category of disbelievers.

This lesson presents the classification of Hell into seven distinct levels as mentioned in the transmitted sources. Each level has a name and is associated with a particular group of people. Understanding this classification helps us grasp the detailed descriptions of the afterlife found in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the list of seven hells and their occupants from the Arabic text and its English translation.
Focus on the names and the groups.
2
Identify each hell and its group
Go through each of the seven names: Laza, al-Hutama, al-Sa'ir, Saqar, al-Jahim, al-Hawiya, and note which group is assigned.
The groups include Jews, Christians, Sabians, Magians, idol worshippers, and hypocrites.
3
Reflect on the purpose of classification
Consider why this classification is important for understanding divine justice and the reality of the afterlife.
It shows that punishments are tailored to groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات وتحت لظى وهي لليهود، ثم الحطمة وهي للنصارى، ثم السعير وهي للصابئين وهم فرقة من اليهود، ثم سقر وهي للمجوس، ثم الجحيم وهي لعبدة الأصنام، ثم الهاوية وهي للمنافقين. وذكر ابن العربي أن هذه النار التي في الدنيا ما أخرجها الله إلى الناس من جهنم غمست في البحر مرتين، ولولا ذلك لم ينتفع أحد بها من حرها، وكفى بها زاجراً، وبعد أخذ نار الدنيا منها أوقد عليها ألف سنة حتى ابيضت، ثم ألف سنة حتى احمرت، ثم ألف سنة حتى اسودت، فهي سوداء مظلمة، وحرها هواء محرف، ولا جمر لها سوى بني آدم والأحجار المتخذة آلهة من دون الله، قال تعالى: {يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا قُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ وَأَهْلِيكُمْ نَارًا وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ وَالْحِجَارَةُ} [التحريم: 6].
The Samiyyat (matters of audition). Under it is Laza, which is for the Jews; then al-Hutama, which is for the Christians; then al-Sa'ir, which is for the Sabians, who are a sect of the Jews; then Saqar, which is for the Magians; then al-Jahim, which is for idol worshippers; then al-Hawiya, which is for the hypocrites. Ibn al-Arabi mentioned that this fire which is in the world, God did not bring it out to people from Hell except that it was dipped in the sea twice, and were it not for that, no one would benefit from its heat. Sufficient is it as a deterrent. And after taking the fire of the world from it, it was kindled upon it for a thousand years until it became white, then a thousand years until it became red, then a thousand years until it became black, so it is black and dark. Its heat is fiery air, and it has no embers except the children of Adam and the stones taken as gods besides God. God said: {O you who have believed, protect yourselves and your families from a fire whose fuel is people and stones} [At-Tahrim: 6].
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage describes the seven layers of Hell, their specific names, and the groups assigned to each. It is a classification: Laza for Jews, al-Hutama for Christians, al-Sa'ir for Sabians, Saqar for Magians, al-Jahim for idol worshippers, and al-Hawiya for hypocrites. Then it relates a tradition from Ibn al-Arabi explaining that the fire of this world is a small sample from Hell, dipped in the sea twice to reduce its intensity, otherwise it would be unbearable. It then describes how this fire was then heated for millennia, turning white, red, and finally black. Its heat is described as a corrupting wind, and its fuel is humans and stones used as idols. The passage concludes with a Quranic verse (66:6) commanding believers to protect themselves and their families from such a fire.

Key Terms
السمعيات
لظى
الحطمة
السعير
سقر
الجحيم
الهاوية
جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hell has only one level or is undifferentiated.
Correction: The passage explicitly lists seven named layers, each for a specific group, showing that Hell has degrees.

Checkpoint

A) Jews
B) Christians
C) Sabians
D) Magians

Key Takeaway
Hell comprises seven distinct layers, each assigned to a specific category of disbelievers, illustrating the detailed nature of divine justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals that Hell has layers for specific groups. If you died tonight, which group's description would you fear matching your own beliefs? What change must you make today to avoid that fate?
?
The hypocrites are assigned to al-Hawiya, the lowest layer. Examine your heart: in what areas of your life are you showing off or insincere? What concrete action will you take this week to purify your intention?
?
The list includes those who worshipped idols. What 'idols' in your life—status, wealth, desires—distract you from exclusive devotion to Allah? How will you dismantle one of them starting tomorrow?

The Origin and Nature of the Fire of This World
Describes the origin and nature of the worldly fire from Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the tradition regarding the origin of the worldly fire from Hellfire, its tempering, and its characteristics as described by Ibn al-Arabi and the Quran.

Core Idea
The fire of this world is a cooled sample from Hell, and its true intensity is unimaginable.

This lesson explores a tradition attributed to Ibn al-Arabi describing how the fire of this world originates from the Hellfire. It explains that the fire we know is but a small, tempered portion, and details its transformation over time. The lesson also highlights a Quranic verse that describes the fuel of Hellfire, serving as a warning to believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text about the worldly fire and its English translation.
Focus on the sequence of events.
2
Understand the origin story
Note that the fire of this world was taken from Hell and dipped in the sea twice to reduce its heat, otherwise it would be unbearable.
This explains why worldly fire is not as intense as Hellfire.
3
Note the transformation over time
The fire then underwent millennia of being burned, turning white, then red, then black.
The black color indicates extreme heat.
4
Reflect on the fuel
The fuel of Hellfire is people and stones, as mentioned in the Quranic verse; there are no embers except humans and idols.
This emphasizes the severity of punishment.

The Number and Names of the Gardens of Paradise
Discusses three views on the number of gardens in Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly views on the number of gardens in Paradise and the significance of their names.

Core Idea
Paradise is one reality described by many names reflecting its eternal bliss.

This lesson explores a classical theological discussion about the structure of Paradise. Scholars have differed on whether Paradise consists of seven gardens, four gardens, or is a single garden with many names. Understanding these views helps us appreciate the richness of Islamic eschatology and the mercy of Allah in describing the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the three views presented.
Notice how each view is supported by Quranic verses or reasoning.
2
Identify the three views
Find the three distinct opinions: seven gardens, four gardens, and one garden with many names. Note the evidence each view uses.
3
Reflect on the common thread
Consider how all views ultimately affirm the greatness and mercy of Paradise, despite their differences.
The names all describe attributes like permanence, safety, and bliss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في الجنة: هل هي سبع جنات متجاورة؟ أفضلها وأوسطها الفردوس، وهي أعلاها والمجاورة لا تنافي العلو وفوقها عرش الرحمن، ومنها تتفجر أنهار الجنة، ويليها في الأفضلية جنة عدن ثم جنة الخلد، ثم جنة النعيم، وجنة المأوى، ودار السلام، ودار الجلال. والجنان كلها متصلة بمقام الوسيلة؛ ليتنعم جميع أهل الجنة بمشاهدته لظهوره لهم منها؛ لأنها تشرق على أهل الجنة كما أن الشمس تشرق على أهل الدنيا، وهذا ما ذهب إليه ابن عباس. أو أربع؟ ورجّحه جماعة لقوله تعالى: {وَلِمَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِ جَنَّتَانِ} [الرحمن: 46]؛ جنة النعيم وجنة المأوى، ثم قال: {وَمِن دُونِهِمَا جَنَّتَانِ} [الرحمن: 62] أي: جنة عدن وجنة الفردوس، كما قاله بعض المفسرين وهذا ما ذهب إليه الجمهور. أو جنة واحدة وهذه الأسماء كلها جارية عليها لتحقق معانيها فيها، إذ يصدق على الجميع جنة عدن؛ أي: إقامة وجنة المأوى؛ أي: مأوى المؤمنين، وجنة الخلد ودار السلام؛ لأن جميعها للخلود والسلامة من كل خوف وحزن، وجنة النعيم؛ لأنها كلها مشحونة بأصنافه.
And there is disagreement concerning Paradise: is it seven adjacent gardens? The best and middlemost is al-Firdaws, and it is the highest of them, and adjacency does not negate loftiness, and above it is the Throne of the Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise gush forth. Next in excellence is the Garden of 'Adn, then the Garden of Khuld, then the Garden of Na'im, and the Garden of Ma'wa, and Dar as-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal. And all the gardens are connected to the Station of al-Wasila, so that all the people of Paradise may enjoy witnessing it, because it appears to them from it; for it shines upon the people of Paradise as the sun shines upon the people of the world. This is what Ibn 'Abbas held. Or four? And a group favored this due to His statement: {But for him who feared the standing before his Lord are two gardens} [Ar-Rahman: 46]; the Garden of Na'im and the Garden of Ma'wa. Then He said: {And besides these two are two gardens} [Ar-Rahman: 62], i.e., the Garden of 'Adn and the Garden of Firdaws, as some exegetes said, and this is what the majority held. Or one garden, and all these names apply to it due to the realization of their meanings in it, for all are called the Garden of 'Adn, i.e., permanent abode; the Garden of Ma'wa, i.e., the refuge of the believers; the Garden of Khuld and Dar as-Salam, because all are for eternity and safety from every fear and grief; and the Garden of Na'im, because it is all filled with its varieties.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents three views on the number of gardens in Paradise. First, the view that there are seven adjacent gardens, with al-Firdaws as the highest and best, above which is the Throne. All gardens are connected to the Station of al-Wasila, from which the Prophet (peace be upon him) will intercede, and it shines upon them. This is attributed to Ibn 'Abbas. Second, the view that there are four gardens, based on the two pairs of gardens mentioned in Surah Ar-Rahman. This is the majority view. Third, the view that there is only one garden, and the various names (e.g., 'Adn, Khuld, Na'im) describe its different attributes, such as permanence, refuge, eternity, safety, and bliss. The passage thus explains the theological positions on the nature and structure of Paradise, emphasizing that all names point to the same ultimate reality of eternal bliss.

Key Terms
الجنة
الفردوس
جنة عدن
جنة الخلد
جنة النعيم
جنة المأوى
دار السلام
دار الجلال
مقام الوسيلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That there is only one garden in the afterlife with no variety.
Correction: The passage shows multiple legitimate scholarly views, including seven and four gardens, indicating diversity in understanding Paradise.

Checkpoint

C) One

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refutation of Deniers of Paradise and Hell
Identifies two categories of deniers and labels their denial as madness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two categories of deniers of Paradise and Hell and why the author labels their denial as madness.

Core Idea
Denying Paradise and Hell is either disbelief or madness.

This lesson examines the opening warning of the poetic line: 'So do not incline to a denier.' The commentary explains that 'denier' includes those who completely reject the afterlife (philosophers) and those who deny their past existence (some Mu'tazilites). Such denial is described as madness because it contradicts what is known of the religion by necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the two types of deniers mentioned.
The passage uses 'jahid' for a complete denier and 'munkir' for a partial denier.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the two groups: philosophers (complete deniers) and Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar (deniers of past existence). Understand why they are mentioned together.
The first group is disbelievers, the second are innovators.
3
Reflect on the 'madness' explanation
The author says their denial is madness because it leads to the impossibility of necessary religious knowledge. Think about why this is a strong refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فلا تمل لجاحد) أي: فلا تصغ لقول منكر لهما بالمرة لكفره كالفلاسفة، أو منكر لوجودهما فيما مضى لبدعته كأبي هاشم وعبد الجبار المعتزليين. وقوله: (ذي جنة) أي: صاحب جنون؛ لأن إنكارهما لا يكاد يصدر عن ذي عقل؛ فإنه يؤدي إلى إحالة ما علم من الدين بالضرورة. 110 - دارا خلود للسعيد والشقي معذب منعم مهما بقي. قوله: (دارا خلود) أي: دارا إقامة مؤيدة، ورد المصنف بذلك على الجهمية؛ هم منسوبون لجهم، اسم رجل يقولون بفنائهما وفناء أهلهما، وهم كفار لمخالفتهم للكتاب والسنة. وقوله: (للسعيد والشقي) أي: فالجنة دار خلود للسعيد، وهو من مات على الإسلام، وإن تقدم منه كفر، ودخل في السعيد عصاة المؤمنين، فدار خلودهم الجنة، فلا يخلدون في النار إن دخلوها، بل لا يدوم عذابهم فيها مدة بقائهم؛ لأنهم يموتون بعد الدخول بلحظة ما يعلم إلا الله مقدارها، فلا يحيون حتى يخرجوا منها.
His saying: (So do not incline to a denier) i.e., do not listen to the words of one who denies both of them entirely because of his disbelief, like the philosophers, or one who denies their existence in the past due to his innovation, like Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar the Mu'tazilites. And His saying: (possessing madness) i.e., a person of insanity; because their denial is hardly issued by one of intelligence; for it leads to the impossibility of what is known of the religion by necessity. 110 - Two abodes of eternity for the felicitous and the wretched, one punishing, one delighting, as long as [anything] remains. His saying: (Two abodes of eternity) i.e., two abodes of permanent residence. The author refutes by that the Jahmiyyah; they are attributed to Jahm, a man's name, who say that both of them perish and their inhabitants perish, and they are disbelievers for contradicting the Book and the Sunnah. And His saying: (for the felicitous and the wretched) i.e., Paradise is an abode of eternity for the felicitous, and he is the one who died upon Islam, even if disbelief preceded from him, and the sinful believers enter into the felicitous, so their abode of eternity is Paradise, so they do not abide eternally in the Fire if they enter it; rather, their punishment does not last for the duration of their stay, because they die after entering it by a moment whose measure only God knows, so they do not live until they come out of it.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a line from the poem, followed by refutation. It first clarifies the phrase 'fala tamil li jahid' (so do not incline to a denier), warning against listening to those who completely deny Paradise and Hell, such as philosophers, or those who deny their existence in the past, like the Mu'tazilites Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar. Such denial is described as madness. Then the line of poetry is quoted: 'Two abodes of eternity for the felicitous and the wretched, one punishing, one delighting, as long as anything remains.' The commentary explains that 'darani khulood' means two abodes of permanent residence, and this refutes the Jahmiyyah who believe both abodes and their inhabitants will perish. They are declared disbelievers for contradicting scripture. Then it explains 'li-sa'eed wa al-shaqiyy' (for the felicitous and the wretched): Paradise is eternal for the felicitous (those who die in Islam, including sinful believers). If sinful believers enter Hell, they do not abide forever; they die a momentary death and are later brought out. The passage thus defends the eternity of both Paradise and Hell for their respective inhabitants, with the exception of sinful Muslims who are eventually saved.

Key Terms
جاحد
منكر
ذو جنة
الفلاسفة
أبو هاشم
عبد الجبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying Paradise and Hell is a minor sin or acceptable difference of opinion.
Correction: The text declares it as either disbelief or madness because it contradicts fundamental religious truths.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on philosophers who completely deny Paradise and Hell?
A) They are considered mistaken but still Muslims
B) They are disbelievers (kuffar)
C) They are innovators (mubtadi'a)
D) They are sinful believers

Key Takeaway
Denying Paradise and Hell is a form of disbelief or madness that contradicts essential religious knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live with the certainty that Paradise and Hell are real, or do you sometimes act as if they are distant myths? What one concrete change can you make today to align your daily actions with that reality?
?
The text calls denial of these truths 'madness.' Have you ever entertained subtle doubts about the afterlife, perhaps thinking it is too far off to matter? How can you strengthen your conviction so that these whispers do not take root?
?
If you knew with absolute certainty that the first moment of the Hereafter begins for you tonight, what would you do differently right now? Why are you waiting?

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
Eternity of Paradise and Hell and Refutation of Jahmiyyah
Affirms eternity of Paradise and Hell, refutes Jahmiyyah, and explains fate of sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes for the felicitous and wretched, and how the author refutes the Jahmiyyah who claim their annihilation.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are eternal; the Jahmiyyah who deny this are disbelievers.

This lesson addresses the poetic line 'Two abodes of eternity for the felicitous and the wretched.' The commentary affirms that Paradise and Hell are permanent residences, refuting the Jahmiyyah sect who believed they would perish. It also clarifies that sinful believers (who may enter Hell) do not abide eternally there; they die a momentary death and are eventually brought out.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the key phrase 'darani khulood' (two abodes of eternity).
2
Identify the refutation of Jahmiyyah
Find where the author explicitly refutes the Jahmiyyah, who claim both abodes and their inhabitants will perish. Note the ruling: they are disbelievers.
The Jahmiyyah are attributed to a person named Jahm.
3
Understand the exception for sinful Muslims
The passage explains that 'felicitous' includes sinful Muslims. If they enter Hell, they do not remain eternally; they die and are later brought out. Grasp this nuance.
This is important for understanding Islamic eschatology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jahmiyyah are considered Muslims despite their denial of eternity.
Correction: The text explicitly says 'they are disbelievers for contradicting the Book and the Sunnah.'

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the Jahmiyyah?
A) They are misguided but still Muslims
B) They are disbelievers because they deny the eternity of Paradise and Hell
C) They are correct in their view
D) They are considered sinful believers

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are eternal; their eternity is a fundamental belief, and the Jahmiyyah who deny it are disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your life will end, and then you will face an eternal abode. Do you truly believe that Paradise and Hell are eternal? If so, why do you still procrastinate in obeying Allah and avoiding sin? What would you change today if you knew you had only one year left?
?
The Jahmiyyah were declared disbelievers for denying the eternity of Hell. Are there any beliefs in your heart that contradict clear Quran and Sunnah, even subtly? Are you willing to examine your creed honestly and repent from any deviation?
?
The sinful Muslim may enter Hell for purification, but not remain forever. Does this make you complacent about your sins? Or does it drive you to seek forgiveness now, to avoid even a moment of that punishment? What sin do you need to abandon immediately to spare yourself from the Fire?
